when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師 , 她確實這麼做了 , 但真正要說的是 , 未來會更加深遠 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙來了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 1936年 , 發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器完全是機械化的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	圖靈的機器完全是理論上的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都是從數學的觀點來的 , 但圖靈告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不論你怎麼做電腦 , 都無所謂 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你電腦的機械裝置是不是像巴比奇的機械裝置 , 或是電子裝置 , 像今天的電腦 , 或是未來的電腦 , 或者 , 細胞 , 或者 , 再一次 , 再一次 , 重申 , 只要我們進入了奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到巴貝奇的機器 , 把它做得很小 。 所有這些都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上 , 電腦的本質是存在的 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 「 教堂反對論文 」 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你有了這個連結 , 你說巴貝奇的這個東西真的是一部電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它可以做到我們今天用電腦所做的每件事 , 只是真的很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓大家知道 , 記憶有多慢 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它使用打孔卡 , 被餵進來 , 打孔卡的速度大約是第一號zx81的一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一群ram包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以加上很多額外的記憶體 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	那麼 , 今天這會帶給我們什麼呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 有計劃 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館的檔案館 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴貝奇所寫的關於這個分析引擎的筆記 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一項就是我們稱之為計劃28的計畫 , 這也是我和doronswade一起開始的一個慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的負責人 , 也是開這個計劃要建造出一個差異引擎的人 , 我們的計劃是要建造它的 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部 , 我們將建造一個分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案有幾個部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	第一 , 是巴貝奇的檔案庫的掃描 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	已經完成了 。 第二項研究是關於所有這些計畫的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是模擬那台機器的電腦 , 最後一部份是實體的在科學博物館裡把它做出來 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它完成時 , 你終於能夠理解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為與其在你面前有一小片晶片 , 你必須看著這個巨大的東西 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽到它在運作 。 我可能聞到它在運作 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在兩者之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝奇自己寫信 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它肯定會引導未來的科學發展 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有蓋過它 , 因為他總是以新的計劃迷惑著 , 但在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我來給各位看看它在動畫時的樣子 , 它只是其中一個cpu的機械裝置運作的部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只不過是三組齒輪 , 而且還會加上 。 這是加上機械的動作 , 所以 , 各位可以想像一下這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年之前 , 我們將會成功 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個充滿影像的演說中 , 雅南•亞伯特在他的網路上展示了他三項最新的關於人性的企劃 , 我們的棲息地震震震撼了他的系列《從上方來的地球》 , 個人的訪談 , 來自全球的個人訪談 , 在他的網路《六十億人》當中 , 及他在網路上所拍攝的電影《家園》 , 記錄了人們對於環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變化、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、照片 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅南•亞伯特用寬角度捕捉脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對這個星球有很大的影響 , 可以透過飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了9噸的二氧化碳 ; 這兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談談生態學 , 每年我排放的二氧化碳和法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼辦 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我得要殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來抵消我的碳 , 就像我每次都這樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是向各位展示我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 關於我去年拍攝的最後一幅照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達省的油砂 , 大量的污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 , 我們不想相信我們知道的
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省 , 人們的工作時間是非石油的24小時 , 七個小時是七個小時 , 盡可能地抽取石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是長期解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油比我們每年發現的還多三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新克里多尼亞的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	百分之百的珊瑚可能在2050年前因為全球暖化而被消滅 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度有多敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性也很重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 , 我去年夏天拍了這張照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前 , 拍下這張照片是不可能的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	大西洋和太平洋之間有一種新的開放方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	自1960年起 , 北極的厚度減少了超過40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	有一面新的面貌 , 沒有冰 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了百分之八十的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家 , 在一百年內 , 所有的山冰都消失了 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命來說是非常重要的 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像高爾所說的 , 二十億人住在水上來自喜馬拉雅冰河的冰河 。
return of fish men .	再回來談魚人 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	五分之一的人類是依靠魚生存 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今百分之七十的魚都被過度利用 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據聯準會 , 如果我們不改變捕魚系統的捕魚系統 , 2050年就會消失 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們知道的 。

one human of six have not enough to eat in the world .	世界上六個人中有一位不夠吃東西的人 。

in africa , corn is one of the main foods in many places .	在非洲 , 玉米是許多地方的主要食物之一 。
here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國 , 90%的玉米耕種是用來餵養動物或石油 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	在婆羅洲棕櫚樹種植 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球已經有四十五億年的歷史 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 已有數億年的歷史 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	我們人類已經直立行走了大約兩萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們成功地適應了 , 並且征服了整個地球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	世代以來 , 我們一直在養育我們的孩子 , 不像住在我們身邊的數百萬個物種 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我親眼目睹土地和它的居民從天上高高空向上觀看 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生活和地球的幸福緊緊相連 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們仰賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖、農業 , 至今仍然是世界上最重要的職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們結合在一起的 , 遠遠超過 「 分裂我們 」 的意思 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們對地球的禮物都有同樣的需求 , 希望能超越我們自己 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們卻繼續在牆壁上築起牆壁 , 讓我們分崩離析 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	今天最大的戰役就是保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	在不到50年內 , 我們徹底改變了這一點 , 比人類歷史上全部都還要徹底 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源的運輸量很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集的農作物正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危害我們自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只在試著改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越廣 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的演講中 , 理查德•雷斯尼克的演講顯示 , 將要顛覆健康照護的基因定序有多便宜和快速 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、科技等 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查德•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我會給你們看人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 最左 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女人有兩份大的x染色體的複製品 ; 男人有一份x , 當然還有一小份y的複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	對不起 , 男生們 , 但這只是個小東西 , 讓你與眾不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	如果你放大這個基因組 , 你就會看到 , 當然 , 這個雙螺旋結構--生命的密碼--四個生化字母 , 或者我們稱它為鹼基 , 沒錯:a、c、g、t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 三十億 。
is that a big number ?	這是個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以隨便丟出很大的數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但 , 事實上 , 如果我把這1280年的每一個像素放入一個基對 , 到800個解析度屏幕上 , 我們需要3000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順帶一提 , y染色體的人們 , 決定他們想要把染色體排序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	事實上 , 15年後 , 大約40億美元後 , 基因組被定序並出版了 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最終的版本被出版了 , 他們繼續研究它 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都在一部像這樣子的機器上完成 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每基底都要花一塊錢 , 非常緩慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們做的是 , 我們將一個基因組做成50個複製品 , 我們把這些複製品切割成50個鹼基 , 然後我們把它們做成非常平行的序列 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把它放到軟體中 , 然後再重新組合它 , 再告訴你這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	給大家看看這看起來是什麼樣子的 , 人類基因組計劃:3gabas , 沒錯 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台機器跑來跑去:一週內200gabs 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	那個夏天 , 兩百人將會改變到六百年 , 沒有什麼跡象顯示這速度的緩慢 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	要定序基礎的價格已經下跌了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	相當於你在1998年時把車裡裝滿油氣 , 一直到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星上 , 前後再來兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc定位、所有醫學文獻的檔案、摩爾定律、舊定律 , 還有新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是對數尺度的看法 , 通常看不到像這樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全世界對於人類基因組的測序能力 , 今年大約有5萬到10萬人 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們知道這一點 , 基於被放置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預計會有雙重、三重或四倍 , 年復一年會出現在可預期的未來 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個實驗室 , 代表20%的容量 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京的基因體研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順帶一提 , 中國在贏得這場比賽的中國 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學意味著什麼 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	一個女人37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她帶著第二個雌激素受體雌激素受體的乳癌
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受了手術、化療和放射治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她又回到了 「 階段三 」 卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療來治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲時再次復發 , 得了卵巢癌 , 接受更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她再度患有急性骨髓性白血病 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她陷入呼吸道衰竭 , 八天後死亡 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女性接受治療的方式 , 在短短的10年內 , 看起來就像是血跡 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	這是因為我的同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學基因組學院的研究人員決定研究這位女性後剖析
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他定序 , 取下皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 和癌症骨髓 , 並在幾週內完成了這兩組基因組的序列 , 沒什麼大不了 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他把這兩組基因組做比較 , 他發現 , 在其它事物中 , 有兩千個鹼基在一個叫做tp53的基因中 , 超過三十億個鹼基 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有這種致命突變 , 你一生中有90%會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位女性沒有幫助 , 但這對她的家人來說是很嚴重、很深遠的 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 他們得到了這個基因測試 , 然後他們了解它 , 然後他們可以定期去做篩檢 , 並且能夠早期發現癌症 , 有可能在更長壽的情況下活著 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我向各位介紹啤酒雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時 , 被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是個非常勇敢的女性 , 她們不相信這些症狀與眾不同 , 透過一些英勇的努力和網際網路搜尋 , 她說服了醫療團體 , 實際上 , 他們還有別的 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們的做法是保護性的肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了左旋多巴 , 他們的症狀確實有進步 , 但他們沒有完全的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	這張照片裡的先生是joebeery , 他很幸運地是一家叫做生命科技的公司的執行長 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是兩家公司中的一員 , 製造出巨大的全基因定序工具 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他所做的是讓他的孩子們做的事被定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現在一個叫做spr的基因中有一系列突變 , 負責製造血清素和其他東西的基因 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在左上方 , 他們給這些孩子一種血清素的前導性藥物 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 如果沒有全部的基因定序 , 就不會有這種事發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	在幾年前 , 花費10萬美元 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美元 。 明年是一千美元 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	年復一年 , 價格是100元 , 還是一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這是它移動的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	像蝙蝠俠和水槍一樣 ,
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克在兒童醫院出現 , 肚子像個飢荒的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	不是說他沒有吃東西 , 而是當他吃飯的時候 , 他的腸道基本上就打開了 , 排泄物流到他的腸子裡 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	經過了一百次手術 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽媽 , 請祈禱我 , 我很痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道到底發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓我們把這個孩子的基因定序 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現在控制細胞死亡的基因中 , 有一個單點突變 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	理論上 , 他的反應是對食物的反應有一定的反應 , 而這是一種自然反應 , 會造成一些編寫過的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但是管制它的基因被破壞了 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	這就告訴了其他事情 , 當然 , 除了對骨髓移植的治療之外 , 他也接受了 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的嚴厲恢復後 , 他現在正在吃牛排 , 拿著a1醬汁 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	使用基因組作為普遍診斷的前景就在我們今天面前 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 它就在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	這意味著在座的各位都可以再多活五、十年、二十年 , 只因為這一件事而已 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個了不起的故事 , 除非你想想人類在這個星球上的足跡 , 否則我們有能力可以提高食物產量 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植新的玉米、小麥、黃豆 , 和其他高度包容乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑的作物 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得繼續種植和吃基因改造的食物 , 這是我今天唯一要做的事 。
unless there's anybody in the audience that would like to volunteer to stop eating ?	除非觀眾中有人願意自願停止進食嗎 ?
none , not one .	沒有 , 沒有 。
this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是打字機 , 數十年來 , 每個桌上型電腦的主角 。
and in fact , the typewriter was essentially deleted by this thing .	事實上 , 打字機基本上被這個東西淘汰了 。
and then more general versions of word processors came about .	然後更普遍的文字處理器出現了 。
but ultimately , it was a disruption on top of a disruption .	但 , 最終 , 它是在破壞的頂端發生的 。
it was bob metcalfe inventing the ethernet and the connection of all these computers that fundamentally changed everything .	這是bobmetfe發明了ethernet以及所有連接著改變一切的電腦 。
and suddenly we had netscape , and we had yahoo and we had , indeed , the entire dotcom bubble .	突然間 , 我們有了netscape , 我們有了yahoo和我們 , 整個網路泡沫化 。
not to worry though , that was quickly rescued by the ipod , facebook and , indeed , angry birds .	不用擔心 , 很快就被ipod、facebook和憤怒的鳥類拯救了 。
look , this is where we are today .	聽著 , 這就是我們現今的狀況 。
this is the genomic revolution today . this is where we are .	這是今日的基因革命 。 這是我們現在所處的狀況 。
so what i'd like you to consider is: what does it mean when these dots don't represent the individual bases of your genome , but they connect to genomes all across the planet ?	所以 , 我想要各位思考的是:當這些點不代表你個人的基因組基礎時 , 是什麼意思 ? 但它們能和全世界的基因組連接起來 ?
so i just recently had to buy life insurance .	最近 , 我只需要購買生命保險 。
and i was required to answer: a . i have never had a genetic test , b . i've had one , here you go , and c . i've had one and i'm not telling .	我需要回答:a.我從來沒有過基因測試 , b.我有過 , 開始了 , c.我有過基因測試 , 我沒有說話.
thankfully , i was able to answer a , and i say that honestly in case my life insurance agent is listening .	謝天謝地 , 我能回答a , 老實說 , 以防我的生命保險經紀人在傾聽 。
but what would have happened if i had said c ?	但如果我說了c , 會發生什麼事 ?
consumer applications for genomics , they will flourish .	基因組學的消費者應用 , 會蓬勃發展 。
do you want to see whether you're genetically compatible with your girlfriend ? sure .	你想要知道你是否和你的女朋友基因上相容嗎 ? 當然 。

so anybody who's here today with your significant other , just turn over to them and swab their mouth , send it to the lab and you'll know for sure .	所以 , 今天在座的各位 , 和你們一樣的其他人 , 只要轉過身來 , 換嘴 , 送到實驗室 , 這樣你們就會知道 。
do you really want to elect a president whose genome suggests cardiomyopathy ?	你真的想要選一位總統他的基因組建議心肌病嗎 ?
now think of it , it's 2016 and the leading candidate releases not only her four years of back tax returns , but also her personal genome .	想想看 , 2016年 , 主導的候選人不僅釋放她四年後的稅收 , 還有她個人的基因組 。
and it looks really good .	看起來還不錯 。
and then she challenges all of her competitors to do the same .	接著 , 她挑戰她所有的競爭者也要這樣做 。
do you think that's not going to happen ?	你認為這不會發生嗎 ?
do you think it would have helped john mccain ?	你認為這會對約翰•麥肯有幫助嗎 ?
how many people in the audience have the last name resnick like me ? raise your hand .	在座有多少人有像我一樣的姓氏resnick ? 請舉手 。
typically , there's one or two .	通常 , 總共有一到兩種 。
so my father's father was one of 10 resnick brothers .	我父親的父親是十位雷斯尼克兄弟 。
they all hated each other .	他們都討厭彼此 。

but imagine if my genome were deidentified , sitting in software , and a third cousin's genome was also sitting there , and there was software that could compare these two and make these associations .	但想像一下 , 如果我的基因被辨識出來 , 坐在軟體中 , 第三個表親的基因組也被安排在那兒 , 有軟體可以比較這兩者 , 並且製造出這些關聯 。
not hard to imagine . my company has software that does this right now .	不難想像 , 我的公司現在有軟體可以做到這一點 。

and if we both say yes , voila ! welcome to chromosomally linkedin .	如果我們都答應了 , voila ! 歡迎染色體連結 。

okay , so experts think that one to three percent of you are not actually the father of your child .	好吧 , 專家認為1%到3%的人不是你孩子的父親 。

and like any new technology , it's really in humanity's hands to wield it for the betterment of mankind , or not .	如同任何新科技一樣 , 它的確是在人性的雙手中 , 為了人類的改善而戰勝它 。
