daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾•克拉夫 , 他的骨髓採取了一個新裝置 , 很快地將救命的骨髓移植到捐贈者身上 。 他強調 , 在骨髓中發現的成人幹細胞可以被用來治療許多末期條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟疾病 。
biology , biotech , health , health care , medicine , science , technology	生物、生物科技、健康、醫療、醫療、醫療、醫療、科學、科技、科技等 。
daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	丹尼爾克拉夫斯發明了一種更好的方法來收割骨髓 。
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是一名小兒科癌醫生 , 也是史丹佛大學的幹細胞研究人員 , 我的臨床研究焦點是骨髓移植 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	去年jillboltetaylor的靈感來源 , 我沒有帶一個人腦 , 但我確實帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	骨髓其實是用來拯救數萬名病人的生命 , 大部分患有較先進的惡性腫瘤 , 如血癌、淋巴結 , 及其他疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	幾年前 , 我在史丹佛移植我的移植獎金 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在開刀房裡 。 我們這裡有bob , 他是一個志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國各地 , 以拯救白血病孩童的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何取得這塊骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.r.團隊 , 麻醉 , 護士 , 和我的另一位醫生.
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃在桌上 , 我們拿著這支小針 , 不是太大的 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們是用柔軟的組織將它輸入硬骨頭 , 輸送到tuchus這是個技術用語 , 每次使用注射器時 , 大約十mls的骨髓出去 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把它交給護士 。 她將它注射到一個釘子裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交還給我 。 我們一而再再而三地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	大約兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	我的手臂末端是索雷爾 , 我手上有通話機 , 更不用說bob了 , 他的屁股看起來更像這樣 , 像瑞士起士起士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道嗎 , 這項手術四十年來沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	或許有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想出了一個最小侵入性的方法 , 一個我們稱之為骨髓的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而它運作的方式 , 在這裡顯示的 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準見到患者 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭數十次 , 我們只需進入一次 , 進入骨頭 , 進入骨頭的前面 , 或臀部的後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個靈活的導管 , 帶著一個特殊的電線圈尖 , 可以在骨髓中擠壓的部分 , 跟著它四處走動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	它可以讓你非常快速地吸引或吸出豐富的骨髓 , 快速地通過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過相同的入口多次進口 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃只能得到一個穿刺 , 局部麻醉 , 這樣做 , 哈維斯特作為一個門診 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 。 我在史丹佛得到了一個小額獎助 。
and played around with this a little bit .	稍微玩一下這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到兩種大型動物和豬的研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 出乎我們的意料之外 , 我們不但把骨髓移除 , 我們還發現了骨髓內骨髓內的幹細胞活動 , 相較一般的裝置 , 比一般的裝置 , 比一般的骨髓幹細胞活動的10倍 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年才被美國食品及藥物管理局批准 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是一名活生生的病人 , 你可以看到 , 它遵循著彎曲的彎曲 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人 , 同一個病人 , 同一個洞 , 會有兩段路徑 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在局部麻醉下完成的 , 做為門診病人 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們得到的 , 比起一般標準的方法 , 大約三到六倍的幹細胞 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要在乎呢 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成人幹細胞來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道關於胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞遍佈我們身體各處 , 包括我們骨髓內的血液變形幹細胞 , 已被當作幹細胞療法使用了超過四十年 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	近十年來 , 已有一場大爆炸 , 利用骨髓幹細胞來治療病人的其他疾病 , 如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至在神經學上治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	今年 , 我們剛出櫃 , 正在商業化 , 相當於2.0世代的骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這會吸收更多幹細胞 , 翻譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能鼓勵更多人登記成為能拯救生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你可以在更年輕、更健康的情況下利用你自己的骨髓幹細胞 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後 , 這是一張我們骨髓移植倖存者的照片 , 他們每年都會在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garretlisi提出了一個有爭議的宇宙模型 , 它可能可以回答所有的大問題 。 如果沒有 , 它是你所見過最美麗的8維模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技 ,
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	哈雷特里特•利西對每件事的理論都提出了他的理論 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 , 看看那些致命方程式 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我要盡我所能地描述粒子物理學的美好 , 卻沒有方程式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	事實證明 , 我們能從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚的頭部由上千個珊瑚群組成 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚持續地生長和分裂成為基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們把它想像成一個超高度智能的珊瑚 , 我們可以單獨挑出一個珊瑚 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個地方和他鄰居的相比 , 到底他到底有多好 , 或多大 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們把溫度升高過高的一月之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以很像 , 你看 , 我有衝浪的疤痕可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這珊瑚會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居很明顯地和他一模一樣 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也處在其他地方 , 但身為獨立個體 , 卻感受到他們 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分支成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不一樣 , 超級聰明的珊瑚 , 將會是獨一無二的準備 , 來了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學方法非常準確地描述宇宙的運作方式 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是持續分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是很奇怪的 , 因為我們只能經歷一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子力學的奇特現象最初是由薛丁格和他的貓所描述的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個裝置裡 , 薛丁格在一個有放射性樣本的盒子裡 , 根據量子力學定律的定律 , 分支成一個放射線的狀態 , 一個沒有放射線的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在輻射樣本的枝幹裡 , 引發了一個觸發器 , 釋放有毒物質和薛丁格已經死亡 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個個體都有不同的經歷 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	不論如何 , 另一種可能是不存在的 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每一個人都只能經歷一個獨立的存在 , 而我們無法看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	好像我們每個人 , 像薛丁格 , 都有點像是珊瑚分支 , 分支成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學理論告訴我們 , 這就是世界在微小的尺度下運作的方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用一個句子總結:所有可能發生的事都可以做 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示所有事情都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理學是要描述可能發生的事和不能發生的事 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們的是 , 一切都是幾何學 , 以及基本粒子的相互作用 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	唯有這些互動是完全平衡的 , 事情才有可能發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我要描述一下我們對這些粒子的了解 , 它們是什麼 , 以及它們的平衡是如何運作的 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 質子和反質子的光束會加速到接近光速的速度 , 以碰撞的方式聚集在一起 , 產生出純能量的衝擊 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換為亞原子粒子的噴霧器 , 用偵測器和電腦來分析它們的性質 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這個巨大的機器 , 日內瓦的大型強子對撞機的周長有17英里 , 當它在運作時 , 產生的能量相當於蒙特利的城市的五倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法精確地預測哪些粒子會在任何個體對撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們一切皆可能 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們什麼粒子能被製造出來 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質子和能量必須由質子和反質子所帶著的質量和能量相同 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何顆粒都比能量極限更大的粒子都不會生成 , 而且對我們來說都是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼新粒子加速器如此令人興奮的原因 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將超越前所未有的能量極限七倍 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到什麼之前 , 讓我描述我們已知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	亞原子粒子有一整個動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都熟悉電子
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在座的各位 , 許多人在這個房間裡過著良好的生活來推動他們 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中性伴侶 , 稱為微中子 , 沒有帶電 , 和非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上夸克的夸克有很大的質量 , 用三種方式組成質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都在左邊和右手邊 , 還有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也有比較不熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 第一代有相同的載荷 , 但質量較高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都會和不同的力粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	透過光子 , 電磁力和帶電粒子的電磁力相互作用 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	另外還有一種非常微弱的力 , 難以想像的 , 這種弱力 , 只能和左旋物質互動 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用力帶有一種不同的載荷 , 叫做顏色載荷 , 由三種不同品種產生:紅綠和藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪莫里•蓋爾曼 , 因為這些名字是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 有重力 , 透過質量和旋轉 , 透過它的質量和物質產生交互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 每一種力都各不相同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量會根據每個粒子所擁有的載荷互動 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 它給了所有其他的粒子質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是要看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確定它會發生 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的奧秘在於我們還能看到什麼 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示一段美麗的可能性 , 讓這場演說結束 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷計算所有這些不同的粒子 , 總共有226個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	這是很多粒子用來追蹤的 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	很奇怪 , 大自然有這麼多的基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的指控來畫出它們 , 一些美麗的圖案出現了 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有一個負電荷 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克結合成一個質子時 , 它的電荷總量是一加一加一加 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是另外兩種載荷的結合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開在這個二度載荷空間中畫出粒子載荷的位置 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力會根據超荷和弱荷而產生交互作用 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這被稱為 「 統一的電子傳播模式 」 , 它在1967年被重新組合起來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以只熟悉電荷 , 而不是這兩者都是因為希格斯粒子的緣故 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子有很大的質量 , 打破了這個波紋的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它讓弱力非常弱 , 因為它給弱粒子一個很大的質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這個巨大的希格斯粒子在水平方向上 , 電磁力學的光子仍然是無質量的 , 並且在載荷空間中與電荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	電磁力和弱力是用這種二度空間的粒子載荷模式來描述的 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以將強力加入 , 藉由將兩個載荷方向擴散 , 將載力粒子沿這些方向標示出來 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度空間中畫出來 , 投射到像這樣的二度空間中 , 這樣我們可以看到 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用 , 自然就會在完美的平衡中保持完美 。 四個載荷方向都是 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子的碰撞 , 就會產生出爆炸的能量 , 以及四個載荷方向的載荷 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時此刻 , 任何東西都可以產生 , 只要它擁有相同的能量 , 並且保持完全零電荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如 , 這種弱力粒子和其反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	一個弱的粒子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中子 , 這三個粒子仍然會增加到零總電荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的圖案並不是很漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們什麼樣的互動是被允許的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉載荷空間 , 以得到更好的觀察強相互作用 , 這種對稱性很高 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強大的相互作用中 , 強力的粒子 , 比如這個 , 和有顏色的夸克互動 , 比如這個綠色的 , 讓夸克有不同的顏色來載紅色 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強相互作用每秒都在我們身體的每個原子中發生數百萬次 , 將原子核融合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四種載荷相對應的三種力量並不是故事的結尾 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以將兩個載荷與重力相對應 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把它們納入 , 每個粒子都有兩種不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉載荷 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分裂了 , 在六度載荷空間中形成一個完美的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間裡旋轉這個圖案 , 看看它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	此時此刻 , 這個圖案符合我們目前對於大自然的最佳知識 , 在這些基本粒子的尺度下 ,
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們確信的知識 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子的極限在實驗中 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙是如何以極小的尺度運作的 , 非常美麗 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些關於我們還不知道的新、舊的想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要僅僅用數學來擴展這個模式 , 看看我們能否把我們的手放到整個安吉拉達 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到構成宇宙的所有粒子和力 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們希望用這張圖來預測新的粒子 , 當實驗到達更高的能量時 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	在粒子物理學中有一種古老的想法 , 這種已知的載荷模式 , 不對稱 , 可以從一個更完美的圖案中產生出來 , 類似希格斯粒子如何打破電弱的模式 , 來產生電磁力 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了達成這個目標 , 我們需要引進新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹一個新的方向時 , 我們能猜出粒子在這個方向上所帶的載荷 , 然後我們就可以讓它和其他的粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	若我們明智地猜測 , 我們可以在六度載荷維度中建構標準載荷 , 做為破解的對稱性 , 在這七度載荷度下 , 完美的圖案 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這項特別的選擇 , 引入了大統一理論 , 由帕蒂和薩拉姆在1973年推出 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們觀察這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到一些粒子似乎缺少的空缺 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論的理論 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家會尋找更大、更對稱的模式 , 包含已知的模式 , 作為一個子集 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的圖案能讓我們預測從未見過的粒子的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 該作用的程度很像弱力 , 只是比較弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這一組載荷 , 考慮到關於粒子的奇怪現象:第二代和第三代物質的載荷與第一代物質的載荷相同 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子的獨特性不是它們的六個載荷 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	在標準載荷空間中 , 它們會彼此坐在對方的頂端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 我們就能對每個粒子分配出獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後在八度空間裡旋轉 , 看看整個圖案是什麼樣子的 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代物質的交互作用 , 由一個叫做 「 三重性 」 的對稱性 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	這種在八度空間中的載荷模式 , 其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的謊言群 , e8的模式 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言組是一個光滑的曲線形狀有248維度
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案中的每一點都與這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀對稱有關 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8的一小部份可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的扭曲時間解釋重力
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	加上量子力學 , 這個形狀的幾何學能夠描述宇宙如何在最微小的尺度下運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀生活在八度載荷空間中是多麼美麗的 , 總結成千上萬個基本粒子間的相互作用 , 每一個都只是這個複雜的形狀的一小部份 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉它時 , 我們可以看到其中的許多錯綜複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特定的旋轉 , 我們可以在八度空間中沿著一個對稱軸來觀察這個圖案 , 同時看到所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何統一一樣 , 我們可以看到一些孔 , 在這裡 , 新的粒子被這個圖案所需要 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	這裡有20個空缺 , 新粒子應該有 , 其中兩個已經被帕達姆粒子所填補 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從圖案的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是極小的領域 , 像是希格斯粒子 , 但它們有色荷 , 和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	在這些新粒子中填補了這個圖案 , 讓我們得到完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有很深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	很多人認為它是數學界最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個很棒的觀點 , 這個偉大的數學美的物體能夠描述在最小的尺度下粒子相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	這種被數學所描述的大自然完全不是新的想法 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫道: 「 大自然的偉大書 , 一直開放給我們的凝視 , 都是用數學的語言寫的 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 及其他幾何形狀 , 沒有這些幾何圖形 , 人類無法理解它的單一單詞 ; 沒有這些 , 人類在黑暗的迷宮中四處遊蕩 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著用伽利略的指導來描述粒子物理學的數學 , 只用三角形、圓形和其他幾何形狀來描述 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他的物理學家和我實際在研究這些東西時 , 數學和黑暗迷宮的相似 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但確保在這個數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入了量子力學 , 數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個正在生長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在各個位置相互作用 , 根據美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著使用新機器的圖案越來越多 , 例如大型強子對撞機 , 我們或許可以觀察大自然是否使用這種e8圖案 , 或不一樣的圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程是一個美好的探險 , 能夠參與其中 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8圖案的粒子 , 那就非常非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新的粒子 , 但不符合這個圖案 , 那會非常有趣 , 但對e8理論不好 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我來說 , 不好過 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會多糟呢 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 還蠻糟的 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但 , 預測大自然如何運作是個非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論都是很長的景象 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多努力 , 知道大部份這些想法可能最後不會成為真正的大自然 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣子的:有很多的無線電 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論就像新創公司一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	如同任何大型投資一樣 , 在不成功的情況下 , 要拋棄這一系列研究是很困難的 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果沒有用 , 你就得拋棄它 , 嘗試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	要維持理智和成就幸福的唯一方法 , 在不確定的範圍內要保持生命的平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我盡了最大的努力過著一個平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的生命在物理、愛和衝浪中平衡我的三個載荷方向
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣一來 , 即使我研究的物理學一無所有 , 我仍然知道我已經過了好人生 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年 , 我大部份時間都住在毛伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在 , 這是我父母最大的謎之一 , 我如何在沒有任何類似全職工作的情況下活下來 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是從我在毛伊的家中辦公室看的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你們可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的景色相似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了非常不尋常的人生 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租讓我花時間做我喜歡的事
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	有時活著流浪的存在已經很艱苦了 , 但它讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 保持我一生中幸福的平衡 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我花了很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的陪伴 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興被邀請來ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概知道這其中的2% , 但我還是很喜歡 。 所以我要聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你對每件事的理論:我很習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 。 少數人至少感到興奮的原因是 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是在說 , 我們應該想想宇宙 , 它的核心 , 認為最小的事物 , 是有可能的e8物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度上 , 有沒有一個尺度 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	高爾:嗯 , 現在我展示給你們看的圖案圖案 , 與我們所知的基本粒子物理學有關 , 已經有了非常漂亮的圖形 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我說過的 , 我們很肯定知道 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這種形狀有著很驚人的相似性 , 其適合於e8圖案的方式 , 可能是其餘的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給各位看的這些圖案 , 實際上代表了這個高維物體的對稱性 , 會在我們經歷的時空中扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們看到的所有基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但弦理論學家 , 如我所知 , 用更小的弦震動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們應該如何看待e8和e8之間的電子 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	高爾:不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱性之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空中移動時 , 它扭曲了方向 。 當它移動時 , 它扭曲的方向就是我們看到的粒子的尺寸 。 克:e8的大小 , 跟電子有何關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	它會變大嗎 ? 會變小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	高爾:據我們所知 , 電子是點粒子 , 所以它會向下到最小的可能尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 在量子場理論中 , 這些東西被解釋的方式是 , 所有的可能性同時擴張和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我用珊瑚的比喻 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	這樣一來 , e8的來源方式就是 , 在時空中每一點 , 都將是一個固定在時空的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說 , 形狀會改變方向 , 形狀在移動這個曲線表面時 , 扭曲的方向是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	通過量子場理論 , 他們將自己視為點和互動的點 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能讓它更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種奇妙的感覺 , 我肯定想要更了解這一點 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但 , 非常謝謝你來到這邊 。 這實在太吸引人了 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇中的黑猩猩研究員珍.古德爾談到tacare和其它的社區計畫 , 協助非洲興起的小鎮 , 帶有威脅的動物住在旁邊 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類動物、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍古德能協助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去jmbo , jambo , jambo , abend , bonsoir , 但是我們也可以--oooh , oooh , oooh , oooh , oooh , ooooh , ooooh 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩在晚上去睡覺前的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到的是從山谷的一端傳到另一端 , 從一群巢穴到下一群 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上 , 我想從昨天 , zeray昨天的演講中挑選出這場演說 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個了不起的 , 三歲小孩 , 三歲的澳洲血統兒童 , 塞拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過人類基因圖譜的歷史、家族樹、人類基因圖譜 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	是一個古生物學家 , 已故的路易斯•李奇 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的路徑 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	在當時 , 這真的很不尋常 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在很普遍 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石遺骸 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石得知不少這些生物的長相從化石 , 從肌肉的外觀看出他們從各種手工藝品中發現的
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但它們的行為呢 ? 這是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張 , 現在是一個相當普遍的理論如果我們在現存的近親、大猩猩和人類之間找到相似的行為模式也許這些行為在七百萬年前出現在人猿的祖先身上
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們把這些特質從古代、古老的過去帶給我們 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	如果你看看今天的教科書 , 要處理人類的進化 , 你常常會發現人們在推測早期人類的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為來推測人類的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比其他生物更像我們 , 在這場ted會議中 , 我們也聽過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 至於我要說的 , 是關於黑猩猩在某些特定行為方面 , 會如此相似 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每一隻黑猩猩都有自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們取名字 。 他們可以活到60歲以上 , 雖然我們認為大部分的人在野外大概不會活到60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	urzel先生 。 雌性先生在十一或十二歲時生了第一個寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她每五到六年就有一個寶寶 , 一個長時間的童年依賴期 , 當孩子在哺乳期時 , 晚上和媽媽睡覺 , 騎在背上 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長時間的童年對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 就像對我們而言 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	當大腦在不同形式的動物進化過程中變得更複雜時 , 所以我們發現 , 學習在個體的生命歷史中扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間觀察長輩的行為 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道他們有能力模仿他們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 以這種方式現在在所有不同黑猩猩的族群中 , 所看到的不同的誘人行為 , 透過觀察、模仿 , 和實踐 , 研究這些行為是如何從一個世代傳到下一個世代 , 藉由觀察、模仿和實踐 , 來描述這些使用工具的行為 , 作為原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語 。 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 當中有許多和我們很相似 , 甚至和我們相同 , 在相同的情境下 , 和我們相似的黑猩猩相擁 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	牠們也會親吻 , 握手 , 拍對方的背 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	牠們會大量移動 , 牠們會扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會中 , 我們發現許多許多許多有同情心的例子 , 包含愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 對於他們的天性有很黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有極端殘酷的能力 , 甚至一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些極具攻擊性的行為 , 大部分都是針對鄰近社會群體的對象 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	他們非常地激進 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信 , 黑猩猩比任何其他生物都更能了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和動物王國之間並沒有明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 每當我們做更多的觀察時 , 它就會變得更加模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始的研究至今仍然持續著
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩在野外生活著複雜的社交生活 , 使我們瞭解到我們是其中的一員 , 和我們共享這個星球的動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以很讓人感傷的是 , 發現像世界上許多其他生物的黑猩猩 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片而已 , 它顯示了長達數量的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那時我飛越整個地區 , 大約十六年前 , 那時我了解到 , 在這個公園之外 , 在1960年 , 在這片森林之外 , 幾乎沒有破壞 , 沿著坦岡尼卡的東岸 , 那裡有著微小、三十平方形的岡貝國家公園 , 問了我一個問題 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 住在國家公園附近的居民很難生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	那裡的居民比土地還多 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民的數量增加 , 是因為他們從蒲隆地湧入湖中 , 和剛果湖的難民數目增加 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	很窮的人 , 他們無法從其他地方購買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了我們稱之為tacare的計畫 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是個非常全面的方式 , 可以改善住在公園附近村落裡的人的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村落開始 , 現在在24年 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間介入它 , 但它包括了樹木的護士 , 如今最適合種植作物的方法 , 如今已被退化 , 像沙漠一樣的土地 , 在這些山上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制的方式 , 預防土壤侵蝕 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	收回過度濫用的農地的方法 , 這樣在兩年內 , 農地就能夠再有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	致力於幫助村民從井裡取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校教室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與一小群女性合作 , 提供她們機會給微型貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同世界各地的情況 , 我們有95%的貸款回來 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	授權給女性 , 與教育合作 , 提供獎學金給女孩 , 讓她們能完成中學 , 清楚地了解到 , 隨著女性的教育改善 , 家庭規模下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭計劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫 , 對於保育有所貢獻 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的做法是 , 農夫住在這24個村落裡 , 沒有把我們當成一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順帶一提 , 許多員工現在現在坦尚尼亞 , 但當我們開始坦尚尼亞計畫時 , 是坦尚尼亞人的團隊進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一支坦尚尼亞團隊和村民談話 , 問他們感興趣的是什麼 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更加了解保育的重要性 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 當山丘的上層被開採樹木 , 土壤侵蝕和土石流就變得糟糕了 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在開發一種我們稱為 「 更偉大的gomb生態系統 」 的東西 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是遠離國家公園的範圍 , 延伸到所有這些非常退化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落擁有更好的生活標準時 , 他們實際上同意將百分之十到二十的土地放在高地上 , 所以 , 再一次 , 當樹木長回來時 , 黑猩猩就會有葉子走廊 , 通過這些地方可以在國家公園外交流 , 與其他在國家公園外的殘餘團體做交流 。
so tacare is a success .	坦尚尼亞造林計劃是成功的
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其它地區複製它 , 沿著其它野生的區域 , 面臨極端的人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 在非洲的問題 , 正如我們在一開始的ted演講中所討論的 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很大的貧窮問題 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有很大量的人住在陸地上 , 沒有那麼多肥沃 , 尤其是當你砍樹的時候 , 你把土壤打開 , 讓土壤流入侵蝕風層 , 因為絕望的人口減少了越來越多的樹木 , 所以他們可以試著為自己和家人種植食物 , 會發生什麼事 ? 什麼事 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	除了非洲 , 還有其他的問題 , 還有其他的開發中國家 , 甚至 , 無所不在 , 我們對地球做了什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道嗎 , 著名的科學家 , e.o.wilson曾說過 , 如果地球上每個人的生活水準都含有歐洲人或美國人的平均生活水準 , 我們需要三個新的行星 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說的是四個 。 但是我們沒有他們 , 我們只有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題是 , 我們在這裡是最聰明的人 , 可以說是最聰明的人 , 可以說是最聰明的人 , 可以說是最聰明的人 , 可以說是最好的科技 , 可以被ted的研討會所使用 , 而我們卻可以摧毀我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決定之前 , 通常會坐下來問自己: 「 這樣的決定如何影響我們前面的七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	現今 , 重大的決策 , 我並不是特別在談非洲 , 而是世界主要的決策 , 涉及數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常都是基於: 「 這會如何影響下一個股東的會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地旅行時 , 談到黑猩猩所面臨的問題 , 談到黑猩猩和牠們消失的森林所面臨的問題 , 我了解到越來越多非洲的問題 , 可能是存在於先前殖民地剝削的大門 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外旅行 , 在歐洲演講 , 在美國和亞洲談話 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	各位都知道我在說什麼 , 我在說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水水可能是本世紀我們要面對的最關鍵的議題之一 , 不論在哪裡 , 水都被污染了 , 被農業、工業和家庭用化學物所污染 , 仍然在世界各地被噴殺 , 似乎無法從經驗中獲取利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍倒 ; 海嘯的影響更加嚴重 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有無數燃燒的石化燃料 , 還有其他溫室氣體 , 造成氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	終於 , 全世界的人開始相信我們的氣候有問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都混合在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	更糟糕的是 , 窮人受到影響 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲早已受到影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱更加嚴重 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨來的時候 , 會造成大量的洪水和更多的痛苦 , 還有貧窮、飢餓和疾病的惡性循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在一個地區的人數 , 土地無法支援 , 貧窮到無法購買食物 , 無法搬離 , 因為整片土地都退化了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	因此 , 隨著最後一棵樹被砍倒 , 整個沙漠化的擴張 , 逐漸蔓延 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只在非洲 , 全世界都一樣 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 不意外的是 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多似乎失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 失去了原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這聰明的大腦之間 , 可能有某種隔閡 , 那種在ted科技所展示的大腦 , 和人類的心一樣 ? 用非科學的詞語來說 , 愛和同情心 , 是否有某種隔閡 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們是沮喪的、冷漠的、痛苦的 , 或生氣的 。 他們說的或多或少是一樣的 , 「 我們會有這種感覺 , 因為我們覺得你已經打算了我們的未來 , 而我們對未來卻束手無策 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經瓦解了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們時 , 每當我在他們年紀以來 , 我都會想 , 我們如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 我就會感到絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這也導致了這個計畫 , 我們稱之為根與芽 , 這個計畫始於坦尚尼亞 , 目前已傳播到全球97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它具有象徵性的意義 。 根構了一個堅定的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	芽看起來似乎很小 ; 要抵達太陽 , 它們能突破磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為地球上所遭遇到的問題、環境和社會問題、希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界有數十萬名年輕人能夠突破並為所有生物創造一個更美好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要訊息是:我們每一個人每天都在做改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有一個選擇 。 在這房間裡的每一個人 , 我們都有一個選擇 , 來決定我們想要做什麼樣的不同 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人沒有選擇權 , 要靠我們改變現狀 , 窮人也有選擇權 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	樹根與芽的小組都選了三個計畫 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年齡多大 , 哪個國家 , 不論他們是否在城市或鄉下 , 哪個國家都一樣 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼兒園到大學的計劃 , 越來越多的成人開始著手進行他們自己的根部和芽 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體在他們之間做選擇 , 做三個不同的專案 , 讓這個更美好的世界 , 認識到這些不同的問題彼此有所連結 , 並互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們的其中一項計畫是要協助他們自己的人類社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	如果他們能夠 , 他們可能會募集資金來幫助世界其他地區的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的項目之一是幫助動物不只是野生動物 , 家庭動物也一樣 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的專案之一是幫助我們共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	撰寫這一切 , 是一種學習如何在自己的內在和平和和和諧中生活的訊息 , 在我們的家庭中、在我們的家庭中、在我們的社區中、在國際間、文化之間、宗教間 , 和自然界之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然界 。 我們不能再以我們現在的速度破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只是在非洲挑選一兩項計畫 , 計畫的根與芽集團正在進行 , 一兩項專案只在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果巴西利亞、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆和其他團體 。 如我所說的 , 目前在世界上的九十七個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們在種樹 , 他們在種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 帶著雞賣蛋 , 賣了一點點錢 , 或用這些錢來餵飽他們的家人 , 讓他們感到自豪和自主感 , 因為他們不再無助 , 不再依靠別人對他們有蔬菜和雞隻的食物 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 造成一些精神上的幫助 , 讓士兵能得到一些心理上的幫助 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	像這樣的專案計畫是把他們自己帶出去 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是有用的社會成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多的根和芽了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	這是根與芽的重要要素 , 年長的孩子和年長的孩子對話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	不想要懷孕 , 諸如此類的 , 年輕人會傾聽其他年輕人的心聲 , 而不是成人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 我在世界各地被問到這個問題: 「 珍 , 你見過這麼多可怕的事 , 你見過你的黑猩猩 , 從一百萬年前開始 , 減少了十五萬隻 , 到現在不超過十五萬隻 , 和許多其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經有森林的沙漠也消失了 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 可以嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 其中之一是驚人的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	想想這些科技 ,
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我很興奮 , 最後 , 能來談談堆肥式的廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把所有的水往下沖 , 水都很糟 ,
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著 , 談到再生能源極其重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們在乎孩子的星球嗎 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有小孩或孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們在乎他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們在乎他們的未來 , 我們 , 身為世界上精英份子 , 我們可以做點什麼 。 我們可以做一些選擇 , 來做我們每天的生活 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 , 穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周圍的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 它會如何影響我的孩子的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或其它的 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 和人類的心臟連結在一起 , 我們和世界各地的人類連結在一起 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	而這正是ted在幫助我們 , google也在幫助我們 , esri也在幫我們繪製國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有我們能使用的科技 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 它也開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你們今天下午聽說過 , 即將開始發生 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 如果我們關心未來 , 我們必須看到改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	下一個原因 , 希望大自然有驚人的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把這塊完全被摧毀的區域 , 用時間 , 甚至有些幫助它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	例如 , 塔克爾計畫 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴各位 , 看似已經死了的樹木 , 如果你停止砍伐它們 , 就不用了 , 因為你有木頭 , 五年內你就會有一棵三十英呎的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎快要絕種的邊緣 , 可以再次機會 , 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這是很鼓舞人心的 。 這也為我帶來了最後一類的希望 , 在過去的兩天中 , 我們聽到了這麼多這樣的事:不屈不饒的人類精神 。 人們堅韌的決心 , 人類的決心 , 人類的決心 , 人類的決心 , 讓那些你認為會被貧窮或疾病所打擊的人 , 不論如何 , 都可以把他們自己拉出來 , 用手幫助他們 , 把他們帶到社會中 , 帶到他們改變的世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想那些對非洲非常鼓舞人心的非洲人 ,
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出很長的清單 , 但很明顯的 , 納爾遜•曼德拉 , 來自17年的辛苦勞工 , 23年的監禁 , 帶著這不可思議的原諒能力 , 讓他能夠領導他的國家擺脫種族隔離的邪惡政權 , 沒有血戰 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	在奈及利亞 , 肯薩羅瓦在巨型石油公司工作 , 儘管全世界的人盡力而為 , 卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人很鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 是我們需要年輕非洲人的典範 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環境的榜樣 , 我今天也聽到了其中一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	我很感激這個機會再次與ted的每個人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人可以聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個消息是 , 一位經營這整個會議的年輕女性 , 我今天遇到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她非常興奮 , 帶著證書 , 她是根與芽的成員 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在達爾斯薩拉姆的領導地位 。
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這幫助她做她在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 非常振奮人心的見到她 , 看一個例子 , 關於年輕人如何被賦權、有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正成為我們對未來的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家戴安娜•柯恩 , 對於海洋及生活中的塑膠污染 , 還有一些想法 , 如何從塑膠漩渦中解放自己 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費者主義、全球議題、綠色、使命藍、海洋、塑膠等 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜.柯恩:關於塑膠污染的棘手真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是個視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我和塑膠袋一起工作 , 過去二十年 , 我把這些塑膠袋剪下來 , 再縫合起來 , 做成我的藝術作品的主要材料 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我將它們分為二維和三維的部分 , 雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	大約八年後 , 我和塑膠一起工作 , 我有些作品開始裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太棒了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	跟我們一樣 , 是短暫的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	一旦我更進一步地去了解塑膠 , 我就意識到這是一件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	這是件壞事 , 塑膠會分解成小片段 , 因為它永遠是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 在海洋環境中 , 很多都是這樣的 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	然後 , 在過去幾年裡 , 我學到了太平洋的垃圾場和垃圾場 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是很多人的第一個反應是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得走出去把這東西清乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我確實提出了一個提案 , 要和一艘貨物搭上貨物 , 和兩艘退休的捕魚船 , 一艘起重機、一艘拖網和一台冷模機器一起出去 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是要走出垃圾漩渦 , 提高人們對這個議題的認知 , 並開始把塑膠帶進一些小片段 , 將之塑膠製成冷凍的磚塊 , 可以用在已開發的社區中建立材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和真正去過垃圾漩渦的人談話 , 他們在研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 並且在做這件事情時 , 我意識到 , 清理乾淨的垃圾 , 會是很小的一滴 , 和全世界每天產生的產量相比 , 實際上 , 我需要回頭看看更大的狀況 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更重要的是:我們需要找到方法去關掉表面 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切斷使用的單一使用和丟棄的塑膠 , 每天進入海洋環境 , 以全球性的規模 , 每天都要進入 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	仔細觀察後 , 我發現自己真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只在乎塑膠 , 你還在試著想像在太平洋中間的海洋 , 我現在知道有11個塑膠垃圾 , 可能是世界上五個主要海洋中的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我所關心的 , 不只是一團塑膠垃圾 , 而是超市裡的塑膠垃圾 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都是用塑膠包裝的 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的河水都被包裝在塑膠裡 , 甚至在健康食品市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很擔心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我也很關心從塑膠滲出的有毒物 , 滲透到我們身體裡的塑膠和毒素 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群人一起 , 他們都在研究這個問題 , 我們也創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多我們正在進行的方案 , 但有些方案非常基本 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們在海洋中發現的海洋中有80%到90%的物質是我們在海洋中發現的 , 海洋廢物是塑膠 , 那我們為什麼不把它稱為塑膠 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每一個人 , 都終結了他們關於永續與環保的書籍 , 帶著回收的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你在垃圾桶裡放了東西 , 你不用再去想它 。
what is the reality of that ?	這一切的現實是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 不到百分之七的塑膠被回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你仔細觀察它 , 特別是談到塑膠瓶 , 大部分的塑膠瓶只會被降級 , 或被送到中國去 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它是循環的 , 轉變成較少的東西 , 玻璃瓶可以再次使用 , 或者再次使用塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會再變成塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們在看並要求人們思考的事情是我們在 「 減量、使用、回收 」 的前面加上第四個環節 , 這三個環節是拒絕的 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	盡可能地 , 拒絕使用過的單一使用和丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些是非常古老的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 用它們來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易就拿起一瓶不銹鋼瓶或一瓶玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅行時忘了帶著一瓶又一瓶的廢棄鋼瓶 , 裝滿水或濾過濾的水 , 來買一瓶塑膠瓶 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想我要告訴在座的各位我知道你們都知道這個議題 , 是因為在海洋中 , 這是個大問題 , 但身為消費者 , 我們已經創造出這個問題 , 我們可以解決這個問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高對這個問題的認知 , 教導人們選擇替代方案來解決這個問題 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 不論何時 , 要選擇使用單燃料塑膠的替代方案 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把流層切入海洋 , 這樣一來 , 拯救我們的海洋、拯救我們的地球、拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這個來自麻省理工學院的帕蒂馬斯實驗室 , 帕納•米特利是ted的專家 , 它是一個可以穿戴的裝置 , 可以為我們環境的深度互動鋪路 。 想像一下 , 「 關鍵性報告 」 和一些人 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示、設計、界面設計、科技等 ,
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派特提馬和帕納•米爾斯密特 , 展示了第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很有興趣 , 關於我們是否能夠進化或發展出第六感 , 一種能夠讓我們無縫接觸、簡單的代謝和現有的資訊 , 來協助我們做出正確的決定 , 不論我們身在何處 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	有些人可能認為 , 嗯 , 現今的手機不是已經做到的嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted看到某人時--當然 , 這是今年最佳的網路網絡地點--你不會握某人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能在我拿出手機和谷歌的時候保持一下嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者 , 當你去超市 , 站在那巨大的走廊上 , 站在那兒 , 穿著各種各樣的衛生紙 , 你不會拿出手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 到網站上 , 試著決定哪些不同的衛生紙是最環保的負責任的購物 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們沒有很容易取得這些相關的資訊 , 能夠協助我們做出最佳決策 , 決定接下來要做什麼 , 要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組正在研發一系列的發明 , 以某種簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 不必要求使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭開我們最新的努力 , 最成功的努力 , 到目前為止 , 這仍然是一個過程中的工作 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	實際上 , 我現在正在戴著這個裝置 , 我們已經將它與在架上擺脫的零件結合在一起 , 順帶一提 , 目前這個裝置的成本只有350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我正戴著一台攝影機 , 一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜式的電池驅動力投影系統 , 用一面鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件在我的口袋裡跟我的手機通訊 , 作為通訊和計算機的運算裝置 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生 , 帕納•米特利 , 他是真正實施和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統如何讓他走到任何平面上 , 開始用他的雙手 , 來和他面前投射在他面前的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統會追蹤這四隻重要手指 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個案例中 , 他戴著你可能認得的簡單印刷 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較時髦的版本 , 你也可以用不同的顏色來繪製你的指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上能追蹤這四根手指 , 識別他做出的任何手勢 , 例如 , 他可以直接到一個長灘的地圖 , 拉近 , 拉近 , 拉近 , 拉近等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出具代表性的手勢 , 例如 「 拍照 」 手勢 , 然後拍下你面前的任何東西 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他回到媒體實驗室時 , 他可以走到任何一面牆上 , 將他所拍攝的所有照片 , 分類並組織起來 , 再利用所有自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	有些人可能兩年前就在這裡 , 看到了jefffhan的示範 , 你們有些人可能會想: 「 這不是看起來像微軟的表面桌子嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別在於 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面前 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他表面可以取得 , 和這個投影的資料進行互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置完全可攜帶 , 也可能是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個不同點是它完全是行動化的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另外一個更重要的差別在於 , 大量生產的成本不會比現在的手機更昂貴 , 而且不會變成更大的包裝 , 看起來會比我脖子上穿著的這個版本還要時髦很多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	除了讓你們其中一些人活在《關鍵報告》裡 , 看起來像湯姆克魯斯一樣酷的幻想之外 , 我們對於這個裝置感到非常興奮的原因是它真的可以當作第六感裝置的裝置 , 讓你知道你面前的任何東西 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到帕納進入超市 , 他在買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起這個系統時 , 系統可以辨識出他撿到的產品 , 用影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以尋求額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以這個特定的選擇是特別好的選擇 , 基於他個人的標準 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	你們之中有些人可能想要用最漂亮的衛生紙 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他能取得亞馬遜書局的評分 , 就直接投影在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們之前的演講者 , 順帶一提 , 在亞馬遜 , 取得了很棒的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納翻轉了這本書的頁面 , 還可以看到書籍讀者留言的額外資訊 , 也許是他最喜歡的評論家所寫的 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他翻到某個特定的一頁 , 他會找到一段註解 , 給我們一個朋友的專家 , 給他一些額外的資訊 , 關於那一頁的任何資訊 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀那些從未過時的報紙 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以在影片上看到你正在讀到的事件的註解 , 你可以得到最近的體育比例等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這個比較有爭議性 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你和ted的人互動時 , 也許你能看到標籤上的字雲 , 和那個人在部落格和個人網頁上的連結在一起的字 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個案例中 , 學生對攝影機感興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的航班延遲了 , 門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道當下的時間 , 就跟在手臂上畫一個手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	到目前為止 , 我們正朝著發展第六感的方向發展 , 為我們提供無縫接觸的資訊 , 關於我們可能遇到的事物的相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 非常 , 像我說的 , 這背後的天才 。
