and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 或許在未來的十年內 , 我們會帶著終極第六感大腦植入來這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	phyllisrodriguez和aichaelwafi有一個很強大的友誼船 , 生於無法想像的損失 。 rodriguez的兒子在2001年9月11日 , 在世界貿易中心被殺害 ; 在2001年9月11日的9月11日 , elwafi的兒子薩路人被判定為一個角色 , 並且在這些攻擊中為一句子服務 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、政治 ,
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	911的療癒:那些發現原諒和友誼的母親們 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	phyllisrodriguez:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們有大多數人認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次了解到 , 我兒子在2001年9月11日的早上 , 已經在世界貿易中心 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否死了 , 直到36小時後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	那時 , 我們知道那是政治化的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家要怎麼做 , 以我們兒子 , 我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 我和家人的名義 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它 , 透過震驚 , 震驚的震驚 , 和生活中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後 , 薩烏里亞人被指控以六種陰謀來犯罪 , 美國政府要求對他判死刑 , 如果罪名被判死刑 , 我和我的丈夫公開反對 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些 , 透過人權團體 , 我們和其他受害者的家人聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 她的兒子被指控時 , 過來找我 , 我心想: 「 多麼勇敢的女人啊 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想要碰見那位更強壯的女人 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我仍然陷入深刻的悲痛中 ; 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我的兒子是受害者時 , 我馬上得到同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她兒子被指控的是什麼 , 她沒有得到同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的痛苦和我的一樣 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月見面 , 現在aicha會告訴你怎麼回事 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasamussaoui之母
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我請人權組織讓我接觸到受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們把我介紹給五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是這群人中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姐妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是一個母親 , 跟我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為一個母親 , 我痛苦很多 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲的時候就結了婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我在十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 一個十六歲的第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以 , zacarias的故事實在太多了
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然很痛苦 , 因為我的兒子就像被活埋一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 , 我不知道他是否受虐 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 這樣我的痛苦對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有女性而言 , 所有賦予生命的母親 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	這取決於我們女人 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們必須手牽手一起做些什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	這不是反對女性 , 而是為我們 , 為我們女人 , 為我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我反對暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去了學校 , 去和年輕的穆斯林女孩對談 , 這樣他們才不會接受結婚 , 以免年輕就結婚 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以如果我能拯救其中一個年輕女孩 , 盡量避免她們結婚和受苦 , 嗯 , 這是件好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是我站在你們面前的原因 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我從aicha學到很多 , 從那天開始 , 我們第一次和其他家庭成員見面是非常私人的會議 , 因為那是2002年11月 , 老實說 , 我們害怕當時國家的超級愛國主義 ,
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都很緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼想要和我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她很緊張 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 為什麼我們想要和她見面 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們彼此想要什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們知道別人的名字之前 , 或任何事之前 , 我們都已經欣然接受和哭了 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們就坐成一圈 , 帶著支持 , 帶著協助 , 人們有這種和解的感覺 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	然後aicha就開始了 , 她說: 「 我不知道我兒子有沒有罪 , 或無辜 , 但我想要告訴你們 , 我對你們家人的遭遇有多麼不好意思 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道痛苦是什麼 , 且我覺得 , 如果犯罪發生了 , 一個人應該被公平對待和懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她以這種方式接觸我們 , 我想說 , 那是個破冰者 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的事 , 我們都說了自己的故事 , 身為人類 , 我們都建立了連結 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午結束時 , 大概是午餐後的三小時 , 我們覺得好像我們彼此都認識了一樣 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不但能夠如此慷慨地在這些當下 , 如此慷慨 , 和當時的狀況 , 還有她兒子在做什麼 , 還有她所經歷的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有見過這麼艱苦的生活的人 , 來自我自己的完全不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種很特別的連結 , 我非常重視它 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我想這一切都和害怕對方有關 , 但走了這一步 , 了解到: 「 嘿 , 這不是那麼難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能遇到誰 ? 我不知道 , 或說我和別人很不一樣 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , 艾卡 , 你有幾句話可以做結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	艾美:我想說我們必須試著認識其他人 , 其他人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須要寬容 , 你的心也要寬容 , 你的心也要寬容 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定要很寬容 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。

this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想要說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界上太多地方無法取得乾淨的飲用水 。 工程師邁克爾普立塔克在發明可攜式的生命安全過濾器時 , 可以在幾秒內讓最難以置信的飲用水 。 2009年的tedglobal做了一個很棒的示範 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	企業、demo、設計、全球議題、發明、科技、水資源等 。
michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	邁可爾普立特的濾水過濾器會變成骯髒的飲用水 。
i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想要談幾件事 。
the first thing is water .	第一是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都在享受這座大會上所提供的水 , 在過去的幾天裡 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這一切都源自於安全的源頭 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果沒有呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是來自這樣的來源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	統計數據顯示 , 在座有一半的人現在正遭受腹瀉的折磨 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	我在過去談了很多關於統計 , 以及對所有人的安全飲用水的預設 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但他們似乎沒有經歷過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經搞清楚為什麼了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	因為 , 用當前的思維 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法去思考解決 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們就關掉了:我們、政府 , 和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	嗯 , 今天 , 我想讓各位用不同的方式思考 , 問題已經被解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 自從我說話以來 , 世界各地有一萬三千人現在正遭受腹瀉的折磨 。
and four children have just died .	四個孩子剛剛死去 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesver濾水瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和大部分人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節後的隔天 , 當時我在看2004年 , 亞洲海嘯捲入時的消息 , 在電視上播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的幾週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下被污染的水 , 或面對死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	這真的困擾著我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風卡崔娜颶風襲擊了美國的這一邊 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這是第一個世界國家 , 讓我們看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道要花五天才把水送到超級主體嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相射殺電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時 , 我決定我得要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我花了很多時間在我的車庫裡 , 接下來幾週、幾個月 , 我在廚房裡待了很多時間 , 讓我的妻子感到沮喪 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過幾次失敗的原型後 , 我終於想到了這個 , 生命安全瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好 , 現在來談談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在生命安全局之前 , 最好的手動過濾器只能過濾到200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約有25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以這絕對會穿過那200奈米的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	生命安全氣孔是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有任何東西可以通過 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我來示範一下 。
would you like to see that ?	你們想看看嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我花了很多時間準備它 , 所以我猜我應該要花很多時間 。
we're in the fine city of oxford .	我們正在一個美好的牛津城 。
so someone's done that up .	有人這麼做了 。

but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我開始想 , 如果我們身在孟加拉的洪水區中間 , 水不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以我拿了一些東西來加入 。
and this is from my pond .	這是從我的池塘裡來的 。

the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	生命安全瓶子真的很簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水挖出來就好 。
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一個木頭來展示給你們看 。 讓你們看看裡面的一些木頭 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	這樣還不夠髒 。 讓我們稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好 , 現在我要用這個非常骯髒的水 , 把它放在這裡 。 你還想要一個飲料嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好 , 開始吧 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些幫浦 , 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這就是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我把茶壺打開 , 無菌的飲用水就會流出來 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我得快點 。 準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	這樣 , 心裡想著電 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那是安全無菌的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	來吧 , 克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	它的味道是什麼 ?

okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好 , 世界各地數以千計的人使用lifesver濾水瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	可以維持6000公升
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它過期時 , 使用失敗安全的科技 , 系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把車子打開 , 把車子打開 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	另外六千公升是好的 。
so let's look at the applications .	咱們來看看應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	然後 , 幾個星期後 , 我們建立了營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫進難民營取得安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當二萬人聚集在難民營時 , 會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	散播疾病 , 需要更多的資源
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	這個問題就變成了自我繁榮 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但透過不同的思考 , 運送這些資訊 , 人們可以留在原地 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌的飲用水 , 開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	這並不需要天然災害才有用 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊思維 , 國家基礎建設和管道工程的費用太高了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上運行計算機的數量 , 你就沒有辦法運行了 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這就是 「 換個想法 」 的部份 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水 , 使用人造的過程來運送 , 讓我們使用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費除去它的鹽水 , 運送到那裡 , 把水倒在山上、河流和溪流上 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水源的地方 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的就是讓它消毒 。 我們要怎麼做呢 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以使用lifesaver濾水瓶
or we could use one of these .	或者我們可以使用其中一種 。
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 裝在jerry的罐子裡 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這會處理二萬五千公升的水 , 足以維持四、三年的家庭 。
and how much does it cost ?	要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	一天要跑大約半分錢 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 用水處理 , 每天母親和小孩不用再每天走四小時來取得他們的用水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的源頭取得它 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	只要花八十億美元 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 讓無法取得安全飲用水的人數減半 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	若要把這件事情納入考量 , 英國政府每年花費大約120億英鎊在國外援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼就此打住 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	只要200億美元 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	所以 , 每年因此受苦的三十五億人 , 每年死亡的兩百萬個孩子將會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	padyashown主張 , 我們生活在歷史上的這個時刻 , 權力從未改變過的方式 。 在tedxbrusels的演講中 , 他發表了三個全球性的重大轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化等 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	padyashown:全球權力移轉 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩是由一位非常有名的英國詩人在十九世紀末寫的 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 教堂的大腦被認為會回音 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是這樣寫的: 「 在夏天的象坡上 , 充滿了河流 , 我聽見遠方的鼓聲 , 我聽見遠方的鼓聲 , 就像夢想中的聲音 , 遠遠 , 近乎低沉、低沉、低沉 , 繞著地球的路上 , 親愛的朋友和食物 , 親愛的食物 , 親愛的士兵遊行 , 很快就要死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩作感興趣的人 , 這首詩叫做《購物師店小姐》 , 由a.e.豪斯曼寫的 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但豪斯曼所了解到的 , 你也在尼爾塞遜交響曲中聽到的 , 是十九世紀長久、炎熱、西爾文夏天的穩定感近來 , 我們即將進入歷史中最恐怖的時期之一 , 當權力的改變時期 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	女士們先生們 , 經常伴隨著亂流 , 經常是血來潮 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我想要傳達的訊息是 , 我相信我們被譴責 , 只在歷史上的某個時刻 , 當那些已經建立的權力秩序逐漸改變 , 新看世界時 , 世界上存在的新權力開始成形 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	我們現在看到的 , 很明顯地 , 現今幾乎總是高度動亂的時代 , 非常艱難的時代 , 很多時候都非常血腥 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順帶一提 , 這種事每世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你也許會說 , 上一次 , 發生了這一切 , 那就是霍斯曼所感受到的 , 也是教會的感受 , 當權力從舊國 , 歐洲的舊勢力通過 , 穿越了大西洋 , 到達美國的新興時期 , 美國的開始 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在這個真空中 , 過去兩個世紀中歐洲人的政權被用來演奏兩場血腥的災難 , 第一部份和第二部分:兩場大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經稱他們為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是更準確的描述他們的方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在其中一個階段 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 今天我要談的是三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 其中的兩個 , 是關於權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個例子是關於我想要表達的新維度 , 目前從來沒有像現在一樣發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談正在發生的權力移轉 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	現今正在發生的事 , 在某種程度上 , 令人害怕 , 因為從未發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們見過橫向的權力移轉希臘的權力被送到羅馬以及在歐洲文明中發生的權力移轉但我們看到的有些不一樣
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	因為權力不只是從國家移轉到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也向垂直方向移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今正在發生的是 , 被預測的權力 , 被要求負責的權力 , 遵守法律的規則 , 目前 , 在這個國家的機構內 , 已經遷移到全球舞台上了 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們談到全球化的權力 , 市場全球化 , 但實際上 , 它是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級 , 權力被灌輸給負責任的責任 , 受到法律的統治 , 國際舞台上沒有 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台現在的權力掌握在網際網路的權力 , 衛星廣播的權力 , 金錢的權力 , 這巨大的金錢流通了現在流通了32倍的資金 , 供給交易所需的金錢用量 , 應該是用來財務上的改變者 , 如果你願意 , 財務上的規範者近來推動我們膝蓋的權力 , 往往往往往更大的權力發展中國家推動 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生存在一個全球性空間 , 大多是沒有規範的 , 沒有受到法律的規範 , 人們可能沒有法律限制的行為 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	這就符合了強而有力的時刻了 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合那些有權力在沒有限制的空間中運作的人 , 但是歷史的教訓是 , 遲早 , 沒有受制於法律規範的空間 , 不僅僅是透過你想要國際貿易、網路、網路等等的東西 , 還有那些你不希望國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義的東西 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件的揭示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些生活在城市裡的人 , 仍然能夠攻擊你 , 即使在九月的一個明亮的早晨 , 也會攻擊你 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 花費了大約60%的資金來資助911恐怖攻擊的花費 , 其實是透過雙子星大樓的大樓 , 911摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	我們的敵人也使用這個空間 , 大量旅遊、網路、衛星廣播人員 , 讓他們得以擺脫毒液 , 也就是摧毀我們的系統和方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	遲早 , 遲早 , 歷史的規則就是權力接管的地方 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	假如我相信 , 如果是這樣 , 我們這個時代的一個現象就是全球化的權力 , 那麼我們這個時代所面臨的挑戰就是把統治者帶到全球的空間中 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信在我們眼前的數十年 , 將會是更大或更小的混亂 , 更不可能達到那個目標:把統治者帶到全球的空間中 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是說要建立一些全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順帶一提 , 我自己的觀點是 , 女士們先生們 , 這樣做是不太可能的 , 透過吸收更多的聯合國機構 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	這個世界需要一個國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種手段 , 可以合法化國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但 , 談到全球性空間的管理 , 我想這不會發生 , 透過聯合國的機構的創建 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	會由強權團結在一起 , 做出以條約為基礎的系統 , 以條約為基礎的協定 , 來管理那全球的空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到他們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:完全以條約為基礎的組織 , 卻強大到可以容納最強大的組織 , 美國 , 負責任的國家 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:掙扎的開端 , 創造一個合約的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國集團現在 , 我們知道我們必須組成一個機構 , 它能夠為財務空間帶來管理的能力 , 來實現財務上的猜測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而這就是二十國集團的所在 , 一個以條約為基礎的機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在這裡有個問題 , 我們等一下再回來談 , 如果你把最有權力的人集合在一起 , 來制定以條約為基礎的體制的規則 , 來填補統治的空間 , 那弱國會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 待會兒會再回來談這件事 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一條訊息是 , 如果你越過這些亂流的倍數 , 甚至更少的亂流 , 那麼我們的成功將取決於我們有能力將合理的管理帶入全球空間 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這一切開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要跟像這樣的觀眾談談這件事 , 但是權力不只是垂直移轉 , 還包括橫向移轉 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會爭辯說 , 文明的歷史 , 人類的文明聚集在海上 , 和最先在地中海附近的文明 , 更近期 , 在西方大西洋上 , 西方靠近大西洋的力量的後裔 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到的是一個根本的權力轉移 , 廣泛來說 , 遠在大西洋的範圍內 , 遠在大西洋的範圍內 , 遠在太平洋的範圍內 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	從經濟實力開始 , 但這也是一直以來的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 強化軍事預算的發展 , 發生在世界上其他不斷成長的政策中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我覺得這其實不是太大的改變 , 從西方移到東邊 , 而是不一樣的改變 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 值得一提的是 , 美國在接下來的十年、十五年 , 仍然是世界上最強大的國家 , 但她掌握權力的環境現在已經徹底改變了 ; 這種情況已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	五十年來 , 歷史上最不尋常的年份 , 人類的歷史中 , 有著完全壟斷的世界 , 每次指控針頭或反對 , 都需要依據它的位置來華盛頓這個世界 , 一個巨大的身分 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但在歷史上 , 這並不是常見的情況 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在正在發生的事 , 是歷史上更正常的例子 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多極化的世界出現了 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是世界上最主要的特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保持最強大的國家 , 但在越來越多的極端世界中 , 他們會是最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你會開始看到在中國建立權力的替代中心 , 當然 , 我自己的猜測是 , 中國是朝向偉大邁進的 , 不是平順的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	這將會相當艱難 , 因為中國在自由經濟之後 , 開始民主化她的社會 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是另一個主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度 , 巴西 。
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	逐漸地 , 逐漸地 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 世界現在看起來越來越像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀時歐洲:偉大的英國外交部長 , 大君.坎德 , 曾經將它描述成歐洲人的權力協議 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 一個五面八方的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國人總是在玩平衡 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林結合 , 英國和維也納和羅馬合作 , 提供了反平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在單極世界主導的時期中 , 有一個有固定聯盟的北約組織 , 戰場上的戰場 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定的權力的兩極性意味著結盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但多重權力的兩極性 , 意味著改變和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們正在進入的世界 , 在這個世界裡 , 我們會逐漸發現 , 我們的聯盟並沒有被修復過 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	偉大的英國外交部長坎寧曾經說: 「 英國有共同的興趣 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	即便在西方國家 , 我們也將看到越來越多的趨勢 , 必須向外伸出 , 超越大西洋的舒適圈 , 和他人結合 , 只要我們想要在世界上完成事情 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	請注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方的做法不夠好 ; 我們必須讓其他人進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方試圖做這件事時的最後幾次 , 而我們還沒有成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我想 , 我們快要到達了400年底的開始 , 我說了400年後 , 這是西方國家權力、西方體制和西方價值觀的終點 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道嗎 , 到目前為止 , 如果西方國家能同心協力 , 它可以在世界的每個角落提出和消除 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是真的了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以上一次的金融危機為例 , 第二次世界大戰之後 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方結合了布雷頓森林體制、世界銀行、國際貨幣基金組織──問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須在其他人打電話 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在 , 我們必須創造二十國集團 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們要超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我來做個預測 , 這可能更令人吃驚 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我猜我們現在已經快要到達了400年的終點 , 當時西方的力量已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會涉及到調停 , 世界各地的多邊調停 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	是嗎 ? 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷特的背後工作 , 正在聯合國指揮下服務 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 十一歲 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	最大海軍陸戰隊在處理索馬利海盜的議題是什麼 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍陸戰隊 。
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是慈善主義的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要讓海道保持開放
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們將和我們不分享價值觀的人做生意 , 但在此刻 , 我們共同的興趣就在此 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的觀點 , 一種嶄新的觀點 , 一種現在正在浮現的世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素 , 完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今 , 在我們的現代世界裡 , 由於網路 , 人們在此所談到的事物 , 每件事都和網路有關 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是互相依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在的關係 , 作為一個國家 , 作為一個國家 , 作為一個從未有過的國家 , 以前從未有過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國際關係的關係 , 一直以來都存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交是管理國家之間的相互關係
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們卻被緊密地鎖在一起了 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥得到了豬流感 , 這是24小時後 , 查爾斯•德高爾機場的問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟墮落了 , 整個社會都倒塌了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯大草原上有大火 , 非洲的食物暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在已深深地、深深地相連 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著一個國家獨立行動 , 而不是與他人建立聯繫 , 與他人合作 , 不再是一個可行的主張 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動並不局限於自己 , 也不夠讓國家自己去控制自己的領土 , 因為國外的影響已經開始影響他們的內心 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我當時是個年輕的士兵 , 身在英國最後一個小型的內戰中 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我的國家的防禦是一回事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多堅強 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的海軍有多堅強 , 我們的盟友有多堅強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	敵人就在牆壁外 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人就在牆壁裡 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想談談我的國家的防禦 , 我必須對國內的健康說話 , 因為傳染病對我的安全而言是個威脅 , 我必須對農業部說話 , 因為糧食安全對我的安全有威脅 , 我必須跟工業部談談 , 因為我們的希區基礎設施很脆弱 , 對於我們敵人的攻擊 , 如同我們從網路戰火中看到的一樣 , 我必須對農業說話 , 因為在我的家鄉 , 在我們看到的內部 , 在我們的家鄉 , 那些在我們的房子裡 , 那些在我們看到的內部 , 在我們的家鄉 , 會發生了什麼樣的內部 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	一個國家的安全不再只是士兵和國防部的問題 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力是把其機構鎖在一起的能力 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴我們 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構的 , 以工業革命的經濟模式為基礎 , 垂直的等級制度 , 任務的專業化 , 指揮結構 , 已經完全弄錯了結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在座的商人都知道我們這個時代的典範結構 , 女士們先生們 , 就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	它是你擁有網路的能力 , 不論在你的政府內部或外部都一樣 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashown的第三個法則 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順帶一提 , 別問我第一個法則和第二個法則 , 因為我還沒發明這些 ; 如果有第三個法則 , 聽起來會更好 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashown的第三法則是 , 在現代 , 所有事物都和所有事物有關 , 對於你能做的事 , 最重要的是你能和他人做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的是 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍人 , 不論你是企業家 , 不論你是做什麼事 , 不論你是做什麼事 , 你的連接者 , 你和他人有沒有連結的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	在工業界 , 政府不了解這一點 。
but now one final thing .	但最後一點 ,
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣的 , 各位先生女士 , 現在我們被鎖在一個以前從來沒有改變過的方式上 , 那麼 , 情況也是我們彼此有著相同命運的情況 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 也是第一次 , 集體防禦 , 那些主導我們國家安全的概念 , 已經不足了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	過去 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更有權力 , 我很安全 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強 , 我很安全 ; 我的聯盟 , 如北約 , 比他們的聯盟更有權力 , 我很安全 。
it is no longer the case .	這已經不是事實了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互連結和大規模毀滅性武器的出現 , 越來越多 , 我和敵人有著共同的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是一名外交官在1970年代與日內瓦聯合會談判時我們成功了 , 因為我們知道我們和他們有共同的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全還不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為雙方都知道零和的遊戲行不通 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們與敵人共享一個命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	在中東 , 和平的大障礙之一是以色列和巴勒斯坦人不了解他們有共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 突然間 , 各位先生女士 , 一直以來 , 對於有遠見的人和詩人的建議 , 變成了我們必須要認真看待的公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首詩作結 。
the great poem of john donne's .	偉大的約翰•丹尼的詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不用吹鈴聲 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是孤島 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它會說: 「 每一個人的死亡都會影響到我 , 因為我和人有關係 , 不要問鐘聲是誰 , 不用費力 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	至於約翰•丹尼 , 道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	我認為 , 對我們而言 , 等於生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽和健康的路徑 , danbuettner和團隊研究世界的 「 藍寶石 」 , 其老年人與vim和充滿活力的社群 , 一起生活在tedxtc上 , 他分享了九種常見的飲食和生活習慣 , 讓它們能在一百歲前生存 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物 , 文化 , 探索 , 食物 , 健康 , 生命 , 科學 ,
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到一百歲
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	有個叫丹麥雙胞胎的研究發現 , 在某些生物限制下 , 平均壽命只有10% 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外百分之九十是以我們的生活方式決定的 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍色區塊的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能想出一個實際的長壽公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 壽命最佳的公式是什麼 ? 他們可能沒辦法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘的飲食 , 或飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國農業部的食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是:
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們 ,
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實上 , 有很多困惑 , 困惑了我們真正的壽命更長 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你要跑馬拉松還是做瑜珈 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是你應該吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到營養問題 , 你該吃嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	那麼荷爾蒙或反物質的荷爾蒙呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是要在裡面玩嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神層面呢 ? 那我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們研究長壽的方法是與國家地理雜誌以及國家老化研究院合作 , 找出四個人口確認地理界限的地區 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後請一群專家加入一群專家 , 透過這些人的所作所為 , 來提煉這些跨文化的精華 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	到最後 , 我要告訴各位那精華是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 關於長壽 , 我想要揭開一些常見的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你真的很努力 , 你可以活到一百歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 在美國 , 大約五千人中只有一個會活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機率非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使是美國人口成長最快的地區 , 很難達到一百歲 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是我們不是為了長壽而設計的 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被設計為一種叫做 「 行進成功 」 的東西 。
i love that word .	我很喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起了我的大學時期 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 " 複製成功 " 意思是你生育下一代的年齡 。 意思是生育後代的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	演化的效果完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類 , 如果你是隻老鼠 , 或大象 , 或人 , 在兩者間 , 都是一樣的 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 若要活到一百歲 , 你不僅要有很好的生活方式 , 你還必須贏得基因樂透 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有些治療可以幫助緩慢、反轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	仔細想想 , 有99件事會讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘的時間 , 那些腦細胞就會死掉 , 永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太過努力 , 膝蓋上毀了你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 , 我們的大腦可以用血漿塞住 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情會出錯 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有三十五兆個細胞 , 有一兆個 「 t 」 的數量 , 我們在這裡談的是國債的數量 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	每八年 , 這些細胞就會自動轉動一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們翻過身 , 就會產生一些損害 , 這種損害就會增加 。
and it builds up exponentially .	而且它以指數型態來建造 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像我們都有披頭四或老鷹專輯的日子 , 我們會在錄音帶上複製它 , 讓朋友複製那錄音帶 , 很快地 , 世代代以來錄音帶聽起來很像垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞身上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化的速度比一個12歲的人快了125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有辦法減緩老化或停止老化 , 我在這裡幹嘛 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約有九十年的時間 , 女性的數量稍微多一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在美國 , 平均壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	沿著這條線的某處 , 我們將在那條桌子上留下十二年美好的年份 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來 , 我們可能可以做到 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 多年來大多沒有慢性病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為獲得這些消失的最佳方法就是看看世界上那些實際體驗到他們的文化 , 那些人們活到一百歲的地區比我們多出十倍的比率 , 那些預期壽命多出十幾歲 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們的第一個藍色地帶 , 離義大利海岸125英里遠 , 位在薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島 , 整個島約有一百四十萬人 , 只有在高地 , 一個叫做努奧羅省的地方 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	在這裡 , 我們有男人活得最長壽的地區 , 大約10倍於美國 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方的人們不僅活到一百歲 , 他們還帶著非凡的活力去做 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	一百零二歲的老人仍然騎腳踏車去上班、砍柴 , 還能打敗比他們年輕六十歲的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史回溯到基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它實際上是一個孤立的青銅文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此地地受害 , 主要是牧羊人 , 經常是低密度的生理活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是以植物為基礎的 , 以他們能帶到田裡的食物為中心 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了一種未經開發的全麥麵包 , 叫做卡塔音樂 , 用小麥做成的 , 一種來自青草餵食的動物的乳酪 , 這種乳酪的含量在omega-3脂肪酸中 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自玉米餵食的動物 , 這種酒的濃度比世界上任何酒都還高三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密我認為是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一就是他們對待老人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國社會平等在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 年紀越長 , 你就越有公平 , 你就越有智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 沒有看過體育畫出來的泳裝日曆 , 而是看到百歲人瑞的月曆 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這並不只對年齡老化的父母親有益於讓他們的家人更親近還會讓他們的壽命延長四到六年研究顯示這對那些家庭有益的孩子而言 , 他們的死亡率較低 , 罹病率也較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一端發現了第二個藍色區域 , 位在東京的南方 , 位在琉球河的阿奇特島上 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	琉球其實是161個小島嶼 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	主島的北部是世界長壽的原點
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方發現了最古老的女性族群 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這裡的人有世界上最長久的殘疾人士預期壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們擁有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活很長的時間 , 通常在他們的睡夢中死亡 , 非常快 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性過後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多活七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	在美國 , 百歲人瑞的人數是五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	五分之一的結腸癌和乳癌的機率 , 在美國這裡的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的比率是六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這種文化讓這些數字得以確切地表示 , 他們有東西可以教我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	同樣地 , 以植物為基礎的飲食 , 充滿了蔬菜 , 有許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃的食物比美國人多八倍 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比起他們所吃的食物 , 更重要的是他們如何吃
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略來避免過食這在美國是個大問題
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:它們會從小盤子裡吃掉 , 所以每坐著就吃少一點卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其提供家庭風格 , 你可以隨時隨意地吃東西 , 不如在櫃台上提供食物 , 再把食物帶到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一個三千年歷史的格言 , 我認為這是有史以來最棒的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由孔子所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食被稱為 「 哈拉、哈奇、飢荒 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在一餐前會說 , 提醒他們在80%的胃裡停止吃飯 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	要花上半小時 , 才能讓完整的感覺從肚子傳到你的大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住要在80%停下來 , 這樣做會幫助你不去做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 和薩丁尼亞一樣 , 琉球有幾個社會建構 , 我們可以把長壽聯想在一起 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道隔離會造成死亡 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 一般美國人有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	現在我們降到1.5% 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運生於俄吉納瓦 , 你出生在一個系統 , 自動和十幾個朋友共處 , 他們一生都在這個系統中 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為moai 。 如果你在moai , 如果你碰到運氣不好 , 你被期待要分享這本書 。 如果壞事發生了 , 孩子生病了 , 家長死了 , 你總是有人支持你 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個特別的moai , 這五位女士已經在一起97年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	一般來說 , 在美國我們已經把成人的生活分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作是有生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 突然間 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	一般來說 , 這意味著休息在輕鬆的椅子上 , 或下到亞利桑那州去打高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語裡甚至沒有退休的字眼
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之 , 有一個詞語侵犯了你的一生 , 那個詞就是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大概翻譯成 「 早上醒來的理由 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對於這位一百零二歲的凱特•馬斯特來說 , 他的生平是帶著這種火星藝術的 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位百歲的漁夫來說 , 每週捕魚三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究院實際上給了我們一個問卷 , 給這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們在文化上很有文化上的進步 , 那些提出問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikii是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上醒來 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對於這一百零二歲的老女人來說 , 她的生存價值只是她的曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在一百一十一歲時分離成兩人 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她感覺如何抱著一個曾曾曾孫女的曾曾孫女 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把她的頭放回來 , 她說: 「 這感覺像是跳上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我的地理雜誌的編輯要我找到美國的藍寶地 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子 , 我們研究明尼蘇達的草原 , 那裡有非常高比例的百歲人瑞 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現 , 美國最長壽的人口是加州的第七天冒險家 , 集中在加州的羅馬林達附近 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	創新者是保守的方法論者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們慶祝安息日 , 從星期五日落到星期六日落為止 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 二十四小時的保護區 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 向他們傳達了非凡的長壽 , 相對的 , 相對來說 , 相對來說 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性的平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對於一個進化論的女性來說 , 她們的預期壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差別更為明顯 , 預期男性的壽命比美國相對的多了11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這是一項研究追蹤了七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林的研究 。 我認為它最終闡明了這個藍寶石計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個異型的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共通的共通點 , 就是一系列非常小的生活習慣 , 大部分時間都遵循儀式的習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中抽取他們的飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	創世紀:第一章 , 詩詞29年 , 上帝談到豆子和種子 , 再一次談到綠色植物 , 顯然缺少肉品 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個保護區 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不管有多忙 , 不管在工作上有多忙 , 孩子在工作上有多大的壓力 , 都得停止一切 , 他們把焦點放在他們的神、他們的社交網路上 , 接著 , 在宗教中 , 天性就是走在大自然的路上 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這股力量並不是說它偶爾會失敗 , 它的力量是每週一次的發電 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不難 , 沒有一分錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	進步主義者也常和其他的進步主義者在一起 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個基督復臨派的 , 你不會看到人們在揮舞jimbeam或推出一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在談他們的下一個自然步行、交換食譜 , 沒錯 , 他們會祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以非常深刻、明顯的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這種文化讓埃爾斯沃•偉爾斯•偉姆得以康復 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯沃•偉倫九十七歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是千萬富翁 , 但當一個承包商想要6 , 000美元來建造一個隱私柵欄時 , 他說: 「 為了這類的錢 , 我自己自己就自己去做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	接下來的三天 , 他出去吃掉了水泥 , 還拖著兩極 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可想而知 , 也許在第四天 , 他最後到了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是桌上的那個人 , 而是開心手術的那個人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他每個月還做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 一百零三歲 , 一個活躍的牛仔 , 早上開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡踏上衝浪板 , 扔掉粗糙的尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在雙子星城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天從舉重的開始 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她在1994年的羅托貝拉克•塞維爾 , 把聖貝納迪納迪諾•高速公路拆了 , 當時她仍是七個不同的組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾有19個偉大的探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是你唯一會遇到的人在撒哈拉沙漠上騎腳踏車橫越撒哈拉沙漠 , 沒有防曬霜 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但是我要告訴你們 , 沒有任何探險比坐瑪莉•戴克斯頓的槍擊案更加恐怖 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	在這三種文化中 , 哪些共同點呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們所做的是什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功地將它煮沸到九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上我們已經完成了兩個藍寶地探險從這之後 , 這些共同的探險家也得到了真實的結果 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一 , 我即將要在這裡講一個 , 沒有一個是運動 , 至少我們對運動的看法 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之 , 他們設定了自己的生活 , 使他們持續地進入身體的活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球女人每天起床 , 坐在地上 , 一天三十到四十次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店 , 或去教堂 , 或去朋友家 , 都會有一個散步 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有按鈕可以按住院子工作或家庭工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們是手工製作的 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	燃燒的卡路里和跑步機一樣多 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們有意圖去做身體活動時 , 這是他們喜歡的東西 。 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一能證明如何阻止認知的衰退的方法 , 他們全都傾向有一個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式來生活 , 讓他們有正確的人生觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每個文化都需要時間來縮減 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 第七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人有這種祖先的復原者 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你趕快或有壓力時 , 會引發一種叫 「 發炎反應 」 的反應 , 這種反應和所有阿茲海默症到心血管疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天慢下來15分鐘 , 你就會把發炎的狀態變成更反炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	牠們有詞彙來表達目的的地、ikigai , 像是琉球人 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 和退休那年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的使命感 , 他們在生活中活躍 , 價值大約七年的額外預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天稍微喝點飲料 , 對美國人不好賣 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們往往會吃以植物為基礎的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說牠們不吃肉 , 而是吃很多豆子和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略來避免過食 , 有些小東西在對的時間點會讓他們遠離餐桌 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	所有這些的基礎是他們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人放在第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和年邁的父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們全部都屬於一個以信仰為基礎的社群 , 值得花上四到十四年的預期壽命 , 如果你一個月要做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們要麼出生 , 要麼他們積極地和對的人在一起 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從佛明翰的研究得知如果三個最好的朋友都過胖 , 有一半的機率會讓你過胖
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人混在一起 , 隨著時間的推移 , 會有很顯著的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你的朋友對休閒活動有興趣 , 保齡 , 或打曲棍球、騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝一點酒 , 不多 , 他們吃對 , 他們很投入 , 且很信任 , 且很值得信任 , 隨著時間過去 , 會產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	減肥是行不通的 , 世上沒有飲食是為了超過百分之二的人口而工作的 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計劃通常一月開始 , 通常是十月份完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	談到長壽 , 藥丸或任何其他藥丸都沒有短暫的修正條款 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許 , 你能做的最重要的事 , 讓你能在生命中加入更多年 。 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	傳導電力的那扇窗戶 , 從清晰變成不透明的窗戶 , 轉換成開關 ; 製成音樂的果實 , 所有這類東西的存在 , 卡達娜•莫塔說:該是時候玩它了 。 莫塔帶領我們參觀一趟驚喜和酷炫的新材料 , 建議我們找出方法 , 做好實驗的方式 , tinker和玩樂 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	卡塔琳娜•莫塔:玩聰明的材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有位朋友 , 他的祖父從腳踏車和洗衣機建造了一輛車 , 這樣他才能運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他之所以這麼做 , 是因為他負擔不起車子 , 也因為他知道如何建造一輛車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經 , 我們知道事情是如何運作的 , 如何做出來的 , 這樣我們就可以建立和修復 , 或者至少能做出有根據的決定 , 決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀的後半葉 , 許多這些自家的實踐已經消失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 自造者和開放原始碼的社群 , 正在把這些知識帶回我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個階段 , 到組成的零件上 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的時候 , 我們仍然知道紙和紡織品的傳統材料是由什麼製成的 , 以及它們是如何被生產出來的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有這些驚人、未來化合物 , 會改變形狀、會導電的油漆、會改變顏料的顏料、會發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	導電油墨讓我們能用傳統印刷電路或電線來繪製電路 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我手中拿著的這個小小的例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸控感應器 , 透過打開這個小光來對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家曾用過導電油墨 , 但近期的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能夠把它用在雷射印表機和筆記上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一片丙烯酸鹽粒子 , 充滿了無顏色的輕微粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般的丙胺酸纖維只會在邊緣散射光線 , 但當我打開燈時 , 整個表面都會發光 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這種材料的其中兩個應用程式包括內部設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而熱染色的顏料在特定溫度下會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	把這個放到一個熱盤上 , 溫度會比環境高一點點 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的其中一個原則是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 嬰兒奶瓶中 , 表示內容物是否夠酷 , 可以喝 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是少數我們所知的智慧型材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年內 , 它們會出現在我們每天使用的許多物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛天車在科幻小說中承諾了 , 但我們可以有牆壁 , 可以改變顏色 , 依溫度 , 鍵盤會滾動 , 窗戶會變成不透明的開關 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是個社會科學家 , 所以 , 我今天來這裡的目的就是要談智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事物是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何被製造出來的 , 也因為我相信我們應該更深入了解組成我們這個世界的元素 , 而現在 , 我們對於這些高科技的組成成成份的未來是不夠的 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料很難從小量中獲得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何關於如何使用它們的資訊 , 幾乎沒有任何關於它們如何被製造出來的資訊 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 現在 , 它們大部分都存在於交易秘密和專利的領域中 , 只有大學和企業能取得權利 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年前 , 一個kirsty男孩和我開始了一個我們稱之為開放原料的計劃
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是我們的網站 , 任何想加入我們的人 , 分享實驗、發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人 , 隨時隨地做出貢獻 , 並且聚集各種資源 , 例如 , 其他像我們這樣的創作者的研究論文和教材 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個巨大、集體產生的智慧型材料資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但為什麼我們要在乎智慧型材料的原理 , 以及它們的組成 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的事物 , 而我們不了解的 , 和使用最後卻影響著我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們所使用的物品 , 穿的衣服 , 我們所居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康及生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	如果我們要生活在一個由智慧型材料組成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並理解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	其次 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新總是被修改器給推動 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 都是發明家和改進者 , 從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學很複雜 , 需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩位科學家了解到這一點 , 當時他們用簡單的方法發表論文 , 以製作導電油墨 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 在讀這篇論文之前 , 直到讀到這篇論文 , 並在他的製造者空間裡複製了這個實驗 , 只靠現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至做出了自己的軟體混合器 , 根據其他科學家的指導 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登接著在網路上發表了他的成果 , 包括他曾經嘗試過、不成功的所有成果 , 讓其他人能夠學習並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	喬登的創新主要形式就是在一所熟練的大學實驗室裡做一個實驗在芝加哥的車庫裡 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 , 讓他自己做自己 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以從他離開的地方找到更簡單的程序和改進 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想要提到她的專案計畫的目的 , 是要強調材料的表達特質 , 同時關注製造者的創意和技巧 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置非常強大 , 能教導我們如何運作 , 但它們與設計的結合 , 影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以漢娜的辦法 , 相反地 , 是要制定一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物體 , 藉由教導我們有關材料本身的限制 , 來解放我們免於設計的限制 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	漢娜的許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的實驗之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一些銅膠帶 , 連接到mp3播放器和磁鐵 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的馬賽羅•科爾霍的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 用各種不同材料 , 從簡單的銅膠帶到導電布和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像jodan和許多其他製造者一樣 , 漢娜發表了她的食譜 , 讓任何人都可以複製和重製 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是最理想的材料科學分支之一 , 讓我們能創造更便宜、靈活的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的手工藝品 , 以及她共享的發現 , 為一連串新的可能性打開了一系列的可能性 , 既吸引人又能創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 關於製造家有趣的是 , 我們創造出熱情和好奇心 , 而我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常以非傳統的角度來解決問題 , 在這個過程中 , 最後發現了替代方案 , 或甚至更好的方式來解決問題 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人實驗材料 , 越多研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造商也願意分享他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正能服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得我有點像泰德.尼爾森在1970年代初期 , 他寫道: 「 你們現在應該要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	在那時 , 電腦是這些大型的主體 , 只有科學家在乎 , 沒有人夢想過 , 即使在家也沒有人想過會有一個主體 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 我站在這裡並說 , 有點奇怪 , 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得新興科技的先驅知識 , 是確保我們在未來能有發言權的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡 , 鎖定門和加速器 , 靠我們的眼睛來引導我們 , 儘管我們只能看到前面和後面的幾輛車 。 但如果車子能分享彼此的資料 , 關於他們的位置和速度 , 用預測模型來計算出在路上每個人的安全路線 ? 珍妮•嘿 , ~ 想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•喜利:如果車子能說話 , 車子可能可以避免發生事故 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧:開車很危險 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡去思考的事情之一 , 但事實是 , 宗教的象徵和好運的迷思出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16至19歲的人死亡的主要原因 , 車禍是導致死亡的主因 , 百分之七十五的意外和毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒人能肯定 , 但我記得我的第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我年輕時在高速公路上 , 車子在我面前 , 我看到煞車燈亮起 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙正在慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩到煞車上 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停在高速公路上停下來 , 死掉了 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只剩65比0嗎 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我衝在剎車上 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺那些abs開始運作了 , 車子還在運作 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 而且空氣袋開了 , 車子全都被安裝了 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我並不知道車子停止了 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我想我們能改變駕駛的經驗 , 透過讓我們的車子彼此對話 , 改變駕駛的經驗 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我希望你們能思考一下駕駛的體驗現在是怎樣的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進你的車裡 , 關上門 。 你在玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受周圍的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是 , 沿著部份的路道導航 , 和其他巨大的金屬巨星 , 以超人的速度在行駛 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要指導你是兩隻眼睛 。
