okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你所擁有的 , 眼睛不是為了這個任務而設計的 , 但人們要求你做像這樣的事 , 你想做一件事 , 做一件事 , 他們問的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路面上移開 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	不要再看你要去哪裡 , 轉過來 , 檢查你的盲點 , 不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的駕駛方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做選擇 , 我們必須做選擇 , 看這裡 , 還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常 , 我們會做很棒的工作 , 挑選我們在路上要走的方向 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯過一些事 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感覺到不對或太遲的東西 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它要來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這一點 , 我相信這一點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多影片 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但這項技術現在已經存在 , 可以協助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	未來 , 車子會互相交換資料 , 我們將能夠看到前面三輛車 , 後面三輛車 , 後面還有左邊的 , 同時 , 鳥的眼光 , 我們將能夠看見那些車 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能夠看到前面車子的速度 , 看看他前面的車子的速度有多快或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人要降到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	事實上 , 不 , 車子的確是不可能的
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維立體的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們在路上行駛 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在預定的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要預測車子在不久的將來會在哪裡 , 並不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在車子裡 , 有些摩托車騎士來到波士頓時速85英里 , 我知道你有這種經驗 , 有人沒有 「 出櫃 」 的經驗 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	這傢伙可能已經在路上待了半小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 30英里前 , 有人見過他 , 只要一輛車看到他 , 然後把他放到地圖上 , 他就在地圖上 , 速度 , 估計他會以每小時85英里的速度繼續前進 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他車會在他的耳朵中悄悄地在他的耳朵中 , 說: 「 順便說一句 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車 , 小心 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理的預測車子的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓人物 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說是非常好的 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 像車子之間共享我們車子的位置 , 只是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我的車子裡有gps和照相機 , 我就會精確地知道我在哪裡 , 以及我走得多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 有點像是在哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車子也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地知道他們在哪裡 , 並且可以大概知道其它車子在哪裡 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車共享那些資料 , 如果它們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你們發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	巴布•旺格教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 來估計當福利估計合併時 , 即便在輕量的交通中 , 當車子共用gps資料時 , 我們將這項研究移除電腦模擬 , 做機器人測試 , 讓現有的感應器在機器人身上 , 像是:立體攝影機、定位系統、定位系統 , 及二維度雷射定位系統內 , 來找出相機 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也裝置了一個短距離的通訊設備 , 機器人彼此對話 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此相互碰頭時 , 它們能準確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們能避開彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在這個組合中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當太多聊天時 , 很難去處理所有的封包 , 所以你得要把所有封包排優先順序 , 預測模型能協助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車子都在追蹤預測的軌跡 , 你不會多注意到那些封包 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	首先 , 有一個人似乎有點偏離軌道 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他在走路 , 你知道怎麼走 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而且你知道你需要提示哪些駕駛才能擺脫這條路 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要怎麼做 , 我們要如何警告大家 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車如何竊竊竊私語: 「 你需要逃離這條路嗎 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:一 , 車子的性能 , 第二個駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或是做某件事 , 他們可能就不會在急診室裡做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了不同的研究 , 做關於駕駛狀態的模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用三部攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛人是否會向前看、向下看、看著手機 , 或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外 , 我們可以預測誰 , 哪些車子就在最好的位置上 , 向所有人計算最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術現在就存在了 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願 , 願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我想這是個很讓人不安的想法 , 認為我們的車會看著我們 , 和其他車子談 , 說我們會在八卦的大海裡下車 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 它可以用一種保護我們的隱私的方式 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車時 , 我並不知道你是怎麼做的 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的車牌號碼 , 我並不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是件好事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望你們花點時間想想 , 如果你真的不希望後面那些被分心的青少年 , 知道你在煞車 , 知道你快要停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過自願分享資料 , 我們能為每個人做到最好 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子對你說八卦吧 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金在空中飛行 , 讓他在空中飛行 , 進入大氣中 , 體驗無重力 , 以零g為中心 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、簡短的談話、空間、科技、宇宙、宇宙等 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬•霍金的0格出現 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道我對打開太空前線有多熱情 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界的重力專家無重力的經驗時 , 真的很不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想要告訴各位這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我初次見到他 , 是因為基因組學的考古xprize 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 讓第一組在10天內完成100個人類基因組定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一百個人基因組排序 , 其中之一就是基因組排序 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克雷格•凡特那樣的事件 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇見了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想就是到太空中旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力狀態 , 進入零 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	然後他說: 「 沒錯 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	唯一能體驗世上無重力的 「 零 」 的方法 , 其實是透過降落傘的飛行、無重力的飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	搭飛機 , 飛越頂部 , 飛了25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再下來 , 重量兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	一而再 , 再而三地做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到八、十分鐘的無重力 , nasa如何訓練他們的太空人很久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始這樣做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣布我們要飛史蒂芬•霍金
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一家政府機關和一家公司的操作員 , 說你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你要殺了那傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們很努力地取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一場記者大會 , 我們宣布我們打算要做一顆無重力的拋物面鏡 , 給他25秒的零 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切順利 , 我們可能會做三個拋物線飛行 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼他想這樣做 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常感人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正處於不斷增加的危機 , 即被災難消滅的危機......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為如果人類不上太空 , 就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在太空總署的太空飛機裡 , 到零號飛機的後方 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有20個人捐款我們籌措15萬美元的捐款給那些與我們一起飛行的兒童慈善機構
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個ted成員 。
we set up a whole er .	我們成立了整間急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診醫生和兩位護士搭上飛機 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監控他的血液、他的心跳、他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們全部都準備好 , 以應付緊急情況 ; 天知道 , 你不想傷到這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落場起飛 , 太空梭起降 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我的另一半的拜倫.李希汀伯格和我小心地把他吊死在零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在現場 , 我們就讓他去體驗無重力的體驗 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一個拋物線飛行員之後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在笑 , 我們說: 「 去吧 。 」
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行器 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們其實漂浮著一顆蘋果 , 致力於艾薩克•牛頓爵士 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋擔任相同的座椅 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次 , 第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七和第八個 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅 ,
he was so happy .	他很開心 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在一個珍貴的珠寶身上 , 在我們這個世代 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這趟史詩般的探險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫家大衛•巴林斯基總共有3分鐘的驚人動畫 , 呈現出在細胞內部爆炸的生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計 , 娛樂 , 電影 , 健康 , 醫學 , 科學 , 科技 , 視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky描繪了一個細胞 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是個醫學插圖師 , 我從一個稍微不同的角度看待自己 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在觀察 , 藝術、真相和美的表現 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	儘管這些都是他們自身的美好事物 , 他們都有美好的事物 , 能夠將科學和數學視為理想的理想事物 , 如同理想的合理的組合雙胞胎 , 一個科學家想要約會 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達了真相作為敬畏的事物的表達 , 意思就是它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強大的理想 。 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時是有用的 , 通常在事實之後很長的時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在就可以滾一些照片了 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看到我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美麗 , 往往是對沒有在科學界的人並不反對的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們描述了美的事物 , 通常只有在你了解語言和對研究這個主題的人所使用的語言和語法時才會被描述出來 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看看宇宙的常數 , 那裡存在著人類的理想 , 你可以看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數字進化出這些東西是非常難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導成為一名醫學插圖師之後 , 我試著做的是從我被教導我的父親 , 他是一位雕塑家 , 也是我的視覺導師 , 我想找到一種方式 , 幫助人們理解生物科學中的真與美 , 透過動畫 , 用圖片 , 說出故事 , 這樣人們不見得能被帶到的東西 , 可以被教導 , 也可以被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生常常沉浸在一個環境中 , 在這樣的環境中 , 他們所學習到的主題是有真與美的 , 但他們被教導的方式 , 是分歧的 , 被吸引到一個時點 , 說實話和美麗不見得一定都是事實 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	這就像古老的雞湯的配方你煮雞肉直到香味消失為止
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想這樣對待學生 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育的機會 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 哈佛大學的羅伯特•路德打電話給我 , 他問我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意改變哈佛大學的醫學與科學教育方式 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始著手進行一項計畫 , 探究細胞能夠在分子和細胞生物學中探索真相和美 , 如此一來 , 學生就能更了解它們能夠記住所有的事實 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可以把細胞的形象想像成一個巨大、繁忙、非常複雜的城市 , 被微機械佔據的城市 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械真的就是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 是奈米技術人員在世界各地都很嫉妒 , 它們是自我引導、強大、精準、精確的裝置 , 是由胺基酸鏈所組成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械可以驅動細胞移動的方式 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能驅動細胞如何複製 。 它們能驅動我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們驅動了我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想要做的是 , 弄清楚如何把這個故事變成一個動畫 , 讓哈佛大學生物視野成為哈佛大學生物視覺的中心 , 一個網站 , 哈佛擁有它的分子和細胞生物學學生 , 除了所有的文字資料外 , 還有這些學生視覺化的視覺化影 , 以內化細胞在真相和美的事物 , 以至於能夠研究這個網站 , 如此一來 , 哈佛對於這些生物學的想像力 , 能夠被激發 , 這樣他們一生使用 , 來發現 , 這樣他們能夠被激發出生命 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子的組合方式 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 就是巨噬細胞在微血管中向下流動 , 它們會觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們會從微血管壁中挑出一些來自微血管細胞的信息 , 它們會收集到一些在體外的發炎信息 , 有些在體外的發炎信息 , 有些在微血管之外 , 看不見和感官的地方 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊會讓它們停止 , 讓它們內化 , 使它們必須製造各種各樣的零件 , 使它們改變形狀 , 試著從微血管中找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須與哈佛大學的科學家和資料庫合作 , 研究原子上精確的分子模型 , 找出它們是如何移動的 , 找出它們是如何移動的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	並且弄清楚如何做到這一點 , 用一種很誠實的方式來表明到底發生了什麼事 , 卻沒有那麼真實 , 細胞內很緊密的群眾會阻止這個現象發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要讓大家看的是我們所製作的第一層影片的最初版本的三分鐘的讀者 。 這是一個持續進行中的專案 , 會持續四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請你們看這段影片 , 看看這些細胞製造這些小型步行機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為動脈 , 以這些巨大的負荷 , 來挑戰相對大小的螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請播放這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器是非常不可思議的 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此之間的互動 。
they pass information to each other .	他們會把資訊傳遞給彼此 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成細胞內不同的事情發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會實際製造它在果蠅上所需要的部分 , 由讀取基因的分子所帶出的細胞核所產生的 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命 , 到這裡的每一個人 , 沒有這些微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 今天的出席率 , 克里斯 , 非常稀少 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做 「 動蛋白 」 , 他會拿出一個包包包 , 裡面充滿了全新製造的蛋白質 , 到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不論是對一個細胞膜 , 不論是對器官 , 不論是用來製造或修復 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人都有大約十萬個這種東西在運作 , 目前 , 在你一百兆個細胞裡 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	不論你有多懶惰 , 本質上來說 , 你並沒有在做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以當你們回家後 , 我希望你們想想這一點 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想我們正在學習關於細胞機械的一些事情 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們想通了一切 , 相信我 , 一旦我們弄清楚發生了什麼事 , 我們就知道將近百分之一的狀況 , 一旦我們搞清楚到底發生了什麼事 , 我們將能夠掌握我們對健康、我們對未來世代的做法 , 以及我們能活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能利用這個發現 , 發現更多真相 , 和更多美麗 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但 , 很驚人的是 , 這些細胞、這些微機械 , 都能意識到它們所需要的細胞 , 足以執行它們的目標 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	他們一起工作 。 他們讓細胞做它所需要的 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起合作 , 協助我們身體的巨大實體 , 讓他們永遠無法看到正常運作的實體 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	欣賞剩下的表演 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓計劃在她的車上住一年 , 看一下這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症發生時 , 她的露營工作結束時 , 她的旅程變成無家可歸 。 在這場親密的演說中 , 她描述她成為美國其中一名工作無家可歸的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險 , 快樂 , 生活 , 個人成長 , 貧窮 , 社會變革 , 說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪•布蘭頓:那一年 , 我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我也是個非常好奇的人 , 所以身為記者 , 在22年內 , 我學會了很多新東西 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到了一件事情 , 就是變得隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成了工作無家可歸的無家者 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了報紙編輯的工作 , 就在我父親同年二月去世之後 , 我決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死令我十分痛苦 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我做這件事的時候 , 我有很多想要感受和處理的事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營 , 我決定住在旅行車中一年 , 要做這件事 , 就像一趟漫長的露營之旅 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	於是我打包了我的貓 , 我的鹿特威爾和我的露營裝備 , 進入了1975年的雪佛車 , 開進日落 , 完全沒有發現三件非常重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會將生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至一個小屋內 , 身為人 , 擁有價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒辦法了解到 , 很快地 , 其他人對於負面的看法 , 只要我們願意 , 就會影響到我們的真實 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到 , 無家可歸是種態度 , 而非生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 定期吃飯 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 憤怒和沮喪 , 讓我父親的死亡發生了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我必須有一份全職的工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個非常溫和的春天 , 變成了一個非常溫和的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	要停在任何地方都不可能 , 要很明顯地 , 我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 非常熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓跑過車窗 , 開了一扇窗戶 ,
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗送到日光照顧中心 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能在辦公大樓和卡車停車時 , 我都會在辦公大樓裡洗澡 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或是在公共休息室洗澡 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間車廂中的溫度很少在華氏80度以下的華氏80度以下 , 造成難以入睡 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰箱裡的冰層在幾小時內融化了 , 很悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起找到一間公寓 , 或不能買得起一間公寓 , 讓我能有腐爛的推特和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我留在旅行車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當高溫讓我無法走五十英尺到車外的公共廁所時 , 我用一桶桶和一個垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天來臨時 , 溫度降低到零度以下 , 溫度降到零度 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面臨了一系列新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	每天晚上我都開著一個不一樣的停車位 , 這樣我就不會被警察注意到和困擾 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功的 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得我無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或如何發生 , 但我從身為有才華的作家和記者 , 轉變為一個住在旅行車裡的無家者 , 把我的呼吸帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒變 。 我的智商沒變 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的天份、我的誠信、我的價值觀、我對我的一切的看法都是一樣的 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我不知怎麼地改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我陷入更深的沮喪中 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最終 , 有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 , 三天沒洗澡
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中的人一樣沮喪和沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒喝醉或喝得很高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當一些無家可歸的人發現 , 包括之前的大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的人 , 你為什麼會站在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家者沒有把我視為無家者 , 但我認為我是無家可歸的人 ,
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	然後教授傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正無家可歸的人沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的藥物的反應──憂鬱症讓我有自殺傾向 。 我記得我當時在想: 「 如果我自殺 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 有一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯 , 一位全國知名的記者 , 在全國性的t.v上談過我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫的一篇文章是關於我父親的 , 在他死前的那一年 , 是在提姆的新書裡 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他當時正在做這場演講他在講我的作品
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我發現提姆•羅斯 , 《見報社》的前任主持人 , 當時我在一輛沃爾瑪的停車場裡 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了 , 是因為到達了那個時點 , 我是一個作家 , 還是一個無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 , 找到提姆的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那 , 重新讀了我的論文 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	不久之後 , 我搬回了田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在旅行車裡 , 和沙發衝浪中 。
and i started writing again .	我又重新開始寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天 , 我是個工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得了獎 , 我住在自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再是隱形的 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	成千上萬人全職、兼職工作 , 住在車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續把你車子或街頭的生活汙名化和犯罪化 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家者、工作無家者、工作無家者 , 大部份還是隱形的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇到他們 , 參與他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 給他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以在有希望的情況下戰勝任何事物 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡做為無家可歸者的海報 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你們把錢給下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在他們住的地方 , 不論他們睡在哪裡 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 不論他們的人生狀況如何 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一輛旅行車裡 , 停在沃爾瑪的停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望永遠都能找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxange , 泰國的 " 保險套先生 " , mechaivivaraida , 帶領我們走遍全國 , 大膽提升其生活水準 , 從1970年開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著很多法蘭克、滑稽 , 和非常有效的演講關於保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學 ,
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	切伊•維拉瓦迪亞:保險套先生讓泰國成為一個更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常、非常貧窮 , 有很多人生活在貧窮的環境裡 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 或從貧窮減少計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭規劃開始 , 追隨一個非常成功的母親健康活動 , 組成一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人會接受如果他們的孩子無法生存 , 家庭計畫就沒有人會接受 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:去找孩子 , 去找母親 , 然後跟著家人規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅是孩童死亡率 , 還需要家庭計畫 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在 , 讓我帶各位回顧為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的狀況 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有7個孩子的成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 而且只有非常少數的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們不把 「 不 」 視為答案 ; 我們不把 「 不 」 視為問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去看護士和助產士 , 他們也是女性 , 做得很棒 , 解釋如何使用避孕藥 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很棒 , 但這只佔全國的20% 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其他80%的人做的是讓他們孤獨說: 「 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去見了普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那個黃色標誌下 , 我希望他們還沒毀掉 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	那時我們比可口可樂多了 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們所選的對象是我們所選擇的對象 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很有名 , 他們知道顧客永遠是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們自己也在練習家庭規劃自己 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地提供避孕藥和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 就是這樣 。 我們去那些被認為是問題的根源的人 , 去找那些被認為是解決問題的人 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論人們在哪裡 , 你都能看到船和婦女賣東西 , 這裡是漂浮的市場 , 賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 不論你在哪裡找到人 , 都能在泰國找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 何不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會非常堅固 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去問他們 , 他們說: 「 聽著 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在藍色的那邊 , 不是黃色的那隻 , 把一碗神聖的水放到僧侶手裡 , 把神聖的水灑在藥丸和保險套上 , 讓家人的神聖聖聖水 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片被送到全國各地 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以 , 村落中的一些修士也做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去找老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人去試著提供任何能讓人類變得更美好的東西 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導要用新的字母a、b、b、保險套、iud、v做切除術 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有一個蛇和梯子遊戲 , 一個你丟擲骰子的地方 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你降落在任何我們熟悉的計劃上 , 你就要往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如: 「 媽媽每天晚上吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 往前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買了保險套 , 非常好 , 叔叔 , 前進 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉了 , 不用保險套 。 回來 , 重新開始 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣地 , 教育、娛樂等 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校這樣做 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們有和保險套的接力賽 , 我們有孩子的保險套比賽 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久前 , 保險套被視為是女孩最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人而言 , 鑽石不會讓它變成安全套 , 是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年提出了第一個小額貸款項目 , 婦女說: 「 我們只想向那些實行家庭計劃的婦女申請 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以從我們那裡借出一筆貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	他們就這樣經營著 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在35/36年之後 , 它仍然在進行中 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	這是鄉村發展銀行的一部分 , 不是真的銀行 , 而是一筆小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來經營 , 而是靠村民自己經營 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能沒看到泰國男人 , 那裡總有女性、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	接著 , 我們以為我們會協助美國 , 因為美國一直在協助每個人 , 不論他們是否想要協助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是七月四日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為全體男性提供輸精管切除術 , 但 , 特別是 , 排在隊伍前面的美國男性 , 位在大使館內 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	飯店給了我們一個非常適合的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	他們說: 「 好吧 , 我們會給你一些午餐時間 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 一定是美國的可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	兩品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	食物既不是漢堡或熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我覺得熱狗比較有象徵意義 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	以下是這個 , 年輕人名叫威利•波爾 , 他為美國國際援助工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很顯然 , 他已經做完手術了 , 因為他的熱狗一半被吃掉了 , 他非常開心 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國造成了很多消息 , 也讓一些人感到憤怒 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 過來 , 過來我會對你們做很多事 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	總而言之 , 從七個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率從3.3%到0.5% 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂的方法 , 如果你喜歡的話 , 它也是一樣的 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不知道可口可樂是否在追隨我們 , 或者我們在追隨可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是所有人加入的情況 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強大的政府 , 我們沒有很多醫生 。
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但每個人都有工作可以改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	然後愛滋病終於來到泰國 , 我們必須停止對抗愛滋病 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府被否認、否認、否認 。
so our work wasn't affected .	所以 , 我們的作品沒有受到影響 。
so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 就去軍隊吧 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去了軍隊 , 要求借300個電台 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們擁有的不只是政府 , 他們擁有的槍械比政府還多 。
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以 , 我問他們 , 他們能不能幫我們對抗愛滋病毒 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我做統計後 , 他們說: 「 是的 , 你可以使用所有的電台、電視台 。 」
and that's when we went onto the airwaves .	那時 , 我們進入了空氣波 。
and then we got a new prime minister soon after that .	之後不久 , 我們就有了新的首相 。
and he said , " mechai , could you come and join ? "	他說: 「 克里斯 , 你能來加入嗎 ? 」
he asked me in because he liked my wife a lot .	他問我是因為他很喜歡我太太 。
so i said , " okay . "	我說: 「 好吧 。 」
he became the chairman of the national aids committee and increased the budget fiftyfold .	他成了國家愛滋病委員會的主席 , 並且增加了五十倍的預算 。
every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每個部長 , 甚至法官 , 都得參與愛滋病的教育 , 每一個人 , 我們說 , 公共機構、宗教機構、學校 , 每個人都參與其中 。
and here , every media person had to be trained for hiv .	在這裡 , 每個媒體人都必須接受愛滋病毒的訓練 。
and we gave every station half a minute extra for advertising to earn more money .	我們給每一站 , 多花半分鐘做廣告 , 以賺更多的錢 。
so they were happy with that .	所以他們對此很滿意 。
and then aids education in all schools , starting from university .	然後在所有的學校 , 愛滋病的教育從大學開始
and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	他們是高中生 , 教導高中生 。
and the best teachers were the girls , not the boys , and they were terrific .	最好的老師是女孩 , 不是男孩 , 他們很棒 。
and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	這些到處教導安全性愛和愛滋病毒的女孩 , 被稱為 「 泰瑞莎修女 」 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後我們再往下走一步 。
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三年級、四年級的孩子 , 會去村裡的每個家庭 , 泰國的每個家庭 , 都會提供愛滋病的資訊和保險套 , 給每個家庭 , 給這些孩子們提供 。
and no parents objected , because we were trying to save lives , and this was a lifesaver .	沒有父母反對 , 因為我們試著拯救生命 , 這是個生命安全者 。
and we said , " everyone needs to be involved . "	我們說: 「 每個人都需要參與 。 」
so you have the companies also realizing that sick staff don't work , and dead customers don't buy .	所以有些公司也知道生病的員工沒有效果 , 消費者就不會買東西 。
so they all trained .	所以他們都受過訓練 。
and then we have this captain condom , with his harvard mba , going to schools and night spots .	接著 , 我們有位哈佛大學mba學位的船長 , 前往學校和夜間 。
and they loved him . you need a symbol of something .	他們愛他 。 你需要一個象徵 。
in every country , every program , you need a symbol , and this is probably the best thing he's ever done with his mba .	在每個國家 , 每一個計畫 , 都需要一個象徵 , 這大概是他用mba做的最好的事了 。
and then we gave condoms out everywhere on the streets everywhere , everywhere .	然後在街上到處都有保險套 , 到處都有 。
in taxis , you get condoms .	在計程車中 , 你有保險套 。
and also , in traffic , the policemen give you condoms our " cops and rubbers " programs .	此外 , 在車陣中 , 警察還會給你保險套 , 我們的 「 警察 」 計畫 。
so , can you imagine new york policemen giving out condoms ?	所以 , 你們能想像紐約警察放棄保險套嗎 ?
of course i can . and they'd enjoy it immensely ; i see them standing around right now , everywhere .	當然我可以 。 他們很享受 , 我看到他們站在一旁 , 到處都看得到 。
imagine if they had condoms , giving out to all sorts of people .	想像他們有保險套 , 給各式各樣的人 。
and then , new change , we had hair bands , clothing and the condom for your mobile phone during the rainy season .	接著 , 新的變化 , 我們的頭髮、衣服、保險套 , 在雨季時 , 你的手機就會有 。
and these were the condoms that we introduced .	這些是我們推出的安全套 。
one says , " weapon of mass protection . "	其中一個說: 「 大規模保護的武器 。 」
we found you know somebody here was searching for the weapon of mass destruction , but we have found the weapon of mass protection: the condom .	我們發現這裡有人在尋找大規模毀滅性武器 , 但我們已經找到了大規模保護的武器:保險套 。
and then it says here , with the american flag , " don't leave home without it . "	美國國旗說: 「 若沒有它 , 就不要離家了 。 」
but i have some to give out afterward .	但我後來還是有一些要放棄的 。
but let me warn you , these are thaisized , so be very careful .	但 , 讓我先警告各位 , 這些是泰國化的 , 非常小心 。
and so you can see that condoms can do so many things .	你可以看到保險套可以做很多事情 。
look at this i gave this to al gore and to bill senior also .	看看這個 , 我把這個給了algore和比爾高三 。
stop global warming ; use condoms .	停止全球暖化、使用保險套 。
and then this is the picture i mentioned to you the weapon of mass protection .	這張照片是我剛剛提到的大規模保護的武器 。
and let the next olympics save some lives .	讓下一屆的奧林匹克拯救了一些生命 。
why just run around ?	為什麼要跑來跑去 ?
and then finally , in thailand we're buddhist , we don't have a god , so instead , we say , " in rubber we trust . "	最後 , 在泰國 , 我們是佛教徒 , 我們沒有神 , 所以 , 我們說: 「 在橡膠裡 , 我們信任橡膠 。 」
so you can see that we added everything to our endeavor to make life better for the people .	所以 , 你們可以看到 , 我們把所有東西加到我們的努力中 , 讓人們的生活變得更好 。
we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在旅館和學校的冰箱裡都裝有安全套 , 因為酒精會損害判斷力 。
and then what happened ?	然後發生了什麼事 ?
after all this time , everybody joined in .	在這段時間之後 , 所有人都加入其中 。
according to the u . n . , new cases of hiv declined by 90 percent , and according to the world bank , 7 . 7 million lives were saved .	根據聯合國的統計 , 愛滋病毒的新感染率下降了90% , 根據世界銀行的統計 , 拯救了770萬條生命 。
otherwise there wouldn't be many thais walking around today .	要不然 , 今天就不會有這麼多泰國人了 。
so it just showed you , you could do something about it .	它只會告訴你 , 你可以做點什麼 。
90 percent of the funding came from thailand .	90%的資金來自泰國 。
there was political commitment , some financial commitment , and everybody joined in the fight .	政治承諾 , 財務承諾 , 每個人都參與了這場戰役 。
so just don't leave it to the specialists and doctors and nurses .	所以不要把它留給專家、醫生、護士 。
we all need to help .	我們都需要幫助 。
and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定協助人們脫離貧窮 , 現在我們讓愛滋病脫離貧窮 , 這次 , 不只是政府 , 而是和商業界合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 無法取得功勞 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	這些都是商業界所提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著將他們變成赤腳企業家 , 將他們變成小生意人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法就是透過企業 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	這筆錢從公司到村落的村莊移植 。
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 把錢用在微型貸款基金中 , 我們稱之為鄉村發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進來 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你能借錢之前 , 你需要被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信如果你想幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮環境的人 , 信用能力一定是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用必須是一種人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠無法擺脫貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	在取得貸款之前 , 你必須先受過訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	我們稱之為 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功 。
these are some of the businesses: mushrooms , crabs , vegetables , trees , fruits , and this is very interesting nike ice cream and nike biscuits ; this is a village sponsored by nike .	這是一些企業:蘑菇、螃蟹、蔬菜、蔬菜、水果 , 這是非常有趣的東西 , nike冰淇淋和nike餅乾 。 這是由nike贊助的村落 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧型手機可能會像是個朋友 , 但真正的朋友會給你微笑 , 在2013年 , 在ted2013年 , 克萊納多•里納多•德•羅摩 , 智慧型手機的迷你機器人 , 能和你一起散步 , 滑動一杯咖啡 , 橫越桌子 , 並對你做出反應 , 做出可編寫的表達 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個迷你機器人 , 由你的手機驅動 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉一下手 , 在座有多少人家裡有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	你們當中不少人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好的 , 事實上 , 如果你不把那些手放在房間裡 , 有多少人在家裡有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這是我們在romotive解決的問題 , 我和romotive的其他20位宅男 , 都深深著迷於解決問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	我們真的想要創造一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是八歲或八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個非常困難的問題 , 因為你要打造一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 它不僅要負擔得起 , 它還必須讓人真的想要帶回家 , 帶著他們的孩子回家 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這種機器人不會很詭異或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該要很友善、很可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是個機器人 , 用你已經知道且喜愛你的iphone來當大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過iphone處理器的力量 , 我們能創造出一個機器人 , 它能被wi-fi和電腦視覺化 , 能容納150美元的價值 , 這大約是過去機器人在過去所花費的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他就在創造模式裡 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他其實是在使用裝置上的攝影機來追蹤我的臉孔 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我倒下 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很小心 , 所以他會一直盯著我 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來到這裡 , 他會轉身跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我過來這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會感到害怕 , 就像其它生物一樣 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	在許多層面上 , romo就像一隻擁有自己大腦的寵物 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探索這個世界--嗯 , 羅馬的累了--如果我想要用romo來探索這個世界 , 我其實可以把他和任何其他的ios設備連接起來 。

so i'll show you really quickly , romo actually he's streaming video , so you can see me and the entire ted audience .	我很快地讓你們看一下romo他其實是串流影片所以你們可以看到我和整個ted觀眾

and in the same way that you scroll through content on an ipad , i can actually adjust the angle of the camera on the device .	就像你在ipad上滑動瀏覽內容一樣 , 我可以調整儀器上鏡頭的角度 。

but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但關於romo最重要的是 , 我們想要創造一種完全完全直覺的事物 。

so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他其實是用雙向音頻和影像在任何兩個智慧型裝置之間的音頻 。

so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	我們之前談到遠端臨場 , 這是個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲大的女孩 , 她有一個iphone , 她媽媽買了機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 寄一封電子郵件給住在國家另一端的奶奶們 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩捉迷藏 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她可能只能一年見到她的孫女一次或兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	所以這些是現在romo能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但最後 , 我想談談我們未來在做的事 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這是我們其中一個工程師 , 多姆 , 在一個週末建成的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google的開放框架上 , 叫做blockly 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這樣你就能拖拉和丟掉這些代碼的積木 , 創造出任何你想要的機器人的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編寫romo的行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	實際上你可以在瀏覽器中模擬出它的行為 , 也就是你在左邊看到romo正在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載到你的機器人上 , 並且在現實生活中執行它 , 在現實生活中執行程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有某樣東西你很驕傲 , 你可以和世界上每個擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所有這些無線科技的機器人 , 都能互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以專注於建造一個人都能訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人學中最令人信服的使用例子是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會從人變成人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你要在家裡裝一個機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己的想像力的表現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子的 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道 , 這不是一百年或一百億美元 , 或一個大型人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	今天個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 像romo這樣的人 , 以及像你們一樣的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及要讓你們所有的機器人 , 我們等不及要看看你蓋了什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作家和激進份子伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、對女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有在這場演說中 , 熱情的定義 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、教養、說故事、女性、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德講述充滿熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你們 。 非常恐怖的是 , 在這裡是最聰明的一群人 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴各位幾個關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有個猶太人這麼說 , 我很喜歡 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真相更真實 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個說故事的人 , 我想要傳達一個比我們共同的人性更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有的故事都讓我感興趣 , 有些故事一直困擾著我 , 直到我最後寫下這些故事 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我知道我們周圍的謎題 , 所以我寫下巧合、預防、情緒、夢想、自然的力量、自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我一直活在匿名狀態 , 直到2006年2月 , 我在義大利冬季奧林匹克舉行了奧林匹克運動會 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為了名人 。 現在人們在梅西百貨中認識我 , 而我的孫子們認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我來談談我四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	一名籌辦奧林匹克大會的籌辦人打電話給我 , 說我被選為旗手之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答 , 這肯定是個錯誤認同的例子 , 因為我的身分和身為運動員的身分差不多 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我可以在體育場四處走動 , 沒有助行器 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是在笑的事 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性才能帶著奧運國旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性代表五大洲 , 三位奧林匹克金牌得主 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 自然而然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 一套制服 , 要求我的衡量標準 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對自己有著迷人的遠景 , 看起來像是米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我在杜林 , 熱情的群眾在街頭八十個奧林匹克的隊伍歡呼 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了所有在比賽中競爭的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得勝利 , 但運氣有其元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一小片雪花 , 一英吋的冰 , 風的力量 , 可以決定比賽或比賽的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是訓練或運氣是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都和熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	尿道上佈滿了紅色海報 , 宣佈奧林匹克的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就在這裡 , 不是嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們決定我們命運的原因 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這是我書中角色所需的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要有殘障人士、異議人士、冒險家、外部人 , 和叛逆份子 , 他們提出問題 , 彎曲規則 , 冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	那些有常識的好人不會成為有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會交配好的前伴侶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了其他旗幟師:三位運動員 , 演員蘇珊珊珊珊和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 兩個有熱情心的女性:旺加里•馬塔伊 , 肯亞諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種下了三千萬棵樹 , 透過這麼做 , 她改變了土壤、氣候、在非洲的某些地方 , 當然也改變了許多村落的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	柬埔寨行動主義者索馬利亞的行動主義者 , 積極地對抗兒童妓女 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣給了妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 男人相信和非常年輕的處女做愛 , 會治好愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	在那些被迫每天接收五、十五個客戶的妓院裡 , 如果他們反抗 , 他們就會被電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡 , 我拿到制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的那種服裝 , 但那不是我所預期的米其林男裝所穿的那種服裝 , 真的是不錯的 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但大部分的旗幟 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 普遍的美和熱情的象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅70多歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很瘦 , 很高 , 有著很深的棕色 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你要如何有一根深色的坦克車 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當電視訪問問到: 「 她怎麼能看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背永遠是直的 , 我不會製造老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	這裡有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有吵鬧 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有打招呼 , 沒有跟自己說話 , 沒有偏執偏見 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有那麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的時候 , 我們被召喚到體育場的翅膀 , 大聲說出了奧林匹克市旗 , 首先 , 音樂也是從這裡開始的 , 艾達遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我還高 , 數不清頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿 , 肩上握著旗子 。 我在後面慢慢跑跑跑 , 手伸上支旗 , 這樣我的頭其實在該死的旗子底下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都在索菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我也出現了 , 雖然通常在蘇菲雅的腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都很想去的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘 , 都是在奧林匹克的體育場上的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我老公很不高興我說這句話雖然我跟他解釋說我們私底下所做的事通常會花不到四分鐘 , 這樣他不該親身體驗
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	每四分鐘 , 我都有媒體點擊 , 因為我不想忘記 , 當老年人摧毀我的腦細胞時 , 我不想忘記他們 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著我心中的奧林匹克熱情的關鍵詞 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這裡有個充滿熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 那個地方是一座監獄裡的圖西族難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順帶一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的人都是女人和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱這個地方為剛果的死囚營 , 因為沒有被殺的人會死於疾病或餓死的人 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 蘿絲•瑪班多 , 她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了 , 一個寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵迫使她看著她的丈夫被虐待和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知何故 , 她能讓她七個孩子活下來 , 幾個月後 , 她產下早產的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子切斷臍帶 , 用自己的頭髮連起來 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她以難民營指揮官的指揮官命名 , 以得到他們的喜好 , 用黑茶餵食 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。

somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼地 , 這個家庭存活了十六個月 , 接著 , 靠著非凡的運氣 , 還有一位年輕男子薩夏•查諾夫的熱心 , 他成功將她送上美國救援飛機 , 蘿絲•瑪班多和她的九個孩子 , 最後到了亞利桑納州鳳凰城 , 在那裡 , 他們現在居住並茁壯成長 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	瑪班多 , 在斯瓦希里語 , 意味著偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書裡的主角是堅強且充滿熱情的女性 , 像蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不編造它們 , 不需要它們 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都看得到 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在和女性合作 。
i know them well .	我對他們很熟悉 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古代 , 在世界末日 , 一個父權天主教和保守家庭 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪到五歲時 , 我是個憤怒的女性主義者 , 雖然這個詞還沒有達到智利 , 所以沒有人知道我有什麼毛病 。

once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒保拉在二十多歲時 , 她告訴我 , 女權的約會 , 我應該繼續走下去 。

yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒和我們今天在這裡的特權女性來說 , 但對世界上大多數的姊妹來說 , 她們仍然被強迫成熟的婚姻、妓女、強迫她們的孩子們 , 她們不想要或無法進食 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或生活 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打 , 有時被罰款殺害 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對於現今大部分西方的年輕女性來說 , 被稱為女性主義者是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從未如此性感 , 但讓我向各位保證 , 它永遠不會阻止我調情 , 我也不會因為缺乏男性而受苦 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權主義已經消失了 , 絕對沒有 。

call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為 「 蚜蟲 」 , 或 「 金星 」 , 或 「 金寶 」 , 或 「 隨便你叫什麼名字 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 就會支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這裡還有另一個充滿熱情的故事 , 這是個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉的一個小型婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	今年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫 , 在她三週假期的假期間 , 曾到診所當志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備好了乾淨的牙齒 , 但她到了那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所就只是一間蒼蠅的小屋 。

the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人處於極度痛苦中 , 因為她有數個腐敗的圓柱 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到唯一的解決方案就是拔掉不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 , 她從來沒有這樣做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她很常冒險 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些非古柯鹼 。

she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她祈禱過來 , 祈禱過來 , 開始行動 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病人鬆了一口氣 , 親了她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 海生衛生組織拔出更多的牙 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一位病人在等著她丈夫 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	這位女士的臉看起來像個西瓜 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫大到看不見眼睛 。

jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮被她所做的事嚇壞了 , 但翻譯員解釋說病人的狀況和手術沒有關係 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打她 , 因為她沒有及時準備晚餐給他 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性都住在這樣的生活中 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然世界上三分之二的勞動女性只能擁有不到1%的全球資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們比男性薪水低於男性 , 如果他們薪水不高 , 他們仍然很脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 而且他們經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。

if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人有能力 , 她的孩子和家人就會變得更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家屬繁榮 , 村落就會繁榮 , 最終整個國家也一樣 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	waangarimaathai到肯亞的一個村落

she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女們種植新的樹木 , 用水灌溉 , 一滴地滴下來 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	大概五六年左右 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤被豐富 , 村落被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮、最退化的社會 , 往往是那些讓女性失望的社會 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個顯而易見的真相卻被政府忽略 , 也被慈善事業忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一美元 , 女性的方案就有20美元被頒給男性的方案 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性有51%的人類 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	給予他們能力 , 比科技、設計和娛樂 , 更能改變一切 。

in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡者是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和孩童 , 她們是間接的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人主導世界 , 看看我們有什麼問題 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大部分人都在問的根本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個世界 , 在那裡 , 生命是被保存下來的 , 而生活品質也被每個人豐富 , 不只是為了享有特權而已 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月時 , 我看到費南多•波特奧在加州大學柏克萊圖書館的畫展 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約畫廊的畫廊 , 那些畫有巴特羅的作品 , 沒有勇於展示這些畫作 , 因為主題是阿布格拉伊波監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	他們是巨大的畫作 , 充滿了酷刑和權力的虐待 , 以有聲無聲的巴特羅風格 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法將這些影像從我心中或我的心中移除 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是用懲罰的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力的權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 迫使其餘的群體接受現實 , 並遵循規則 。
