abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	從上往下滲到下層 , 虐待人 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和孩子 , 尤其是窮人 , 都在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最卑鄙的男人也有人可以虐待女人或小孩 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我被灌輸的力量是 , 少數人透過性別、收入、種族 , 及階級的力量 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 該是時候了 , 能夠在我們的文明中做出根本性的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但為了真正的改變 , 我們需要在世界的管理上 , 女性的能量 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要關鍵的女性掌握權力 , 我們需要培養男性女性化的能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	當然 , 我指的是有年輕心智的男人 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人沒希望 , 我們得等著他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我想要擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和傳說中的母乳 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但要做選擇 , 我寧願有勇敢的心 , 如瑪麗•瑪太、索馬利•瑪太、珍妮和蘿絲•瑪太 。
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界變好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是讓它變好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 這是有可能的 。 看看這房間內的這些知識、能源、人才和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們擺脫我們的粉絲 , 捲起袖子 , 激情地工作 , 創造一個近乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦這麼大的城市中 , 有三千萬份餐是供應的 , 但所有食物都來自哪裡 ? 建築師鋼鐵會討論每天供應食物的奇蹟 , 展現古老的食物路線如何塑造現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡洛琳鋼鐵:食物如何形塑我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	要如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代的一個大問題 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但很少被問到這個問題 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視為理所當然 , 如果我們走進一間商店或餐廳 , 或是在一小時內進入這間戲院的門廳 , 就會有食物在那等著我們 , 奇蹟般地從某個地方來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但 , 當你認為 , 倫敦這麼大的城市 , 每天都要產出足夠的食物 , 運輸、買、賣、賣、吃、丟棄 , 同樣的事每天都要發生 , 地球上每個城市的食物 , 都很了不起 , 城市的食物會被吃掉 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 彷彿他們是世界上最自然的東西 , 忘了 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要進食 , 事實上 , 我們對自然界的依賴 , 和我們的古老祖先一樣 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著更多人搬到城市中 , 更多的自然世界被轉化為非凡的景觀 , 就像我身後的景觀一樣 , 在巴西的馬托格羅斯諾的大豆田野為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些景觀是非凡的 , 但很少人見過這些景觀 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	日益增加的景觀不僅僅是為我們提供食物 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	當更多人搬進城市時 , 更多人會吃肉 , 全球每年三分之一的穀物正在被餵給動物 , 而非我們人類 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	既然它需要三倍的穀物 , 實際上是十倍的穀物 , 才能餵飽一個人 , 如果它先經過動物的話 , 那就不是非常有效率的餵食方式 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個正在逐漸惡化的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計我們居住在城市的兩倍之多 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	據估計 , 肉類和乳製品的消耗量會增加兩倍 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和城市化的需求在逐漸增加 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將造成一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 六十億個肚子餓著的肉食動物 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 實際上 , 如果我們像現在一樣堅持下去 , 這是個我們無法解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九千萬公頃的熱帶雨林消失 , 造成了新的耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	儘管同時我們也失去了大量的耕種 , 足以讓鹹化和侵蝕發生 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也很渴望化石燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	西方所消耗的每一卡路里大約需要十卡卡路里的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	雖然我們所生產的食物非常昂貴 , 我們卻不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	半數在美國生產的食物被丟棄了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	總之 , 在這個漫長的過程中 , 我們甚至無法適當地餵食這個星球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	十億人過胖 , 卻有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一切都不合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	想想現在全球百分之八十的糧食交易只由五個跨國企業所控制 , 這是個很殘酷的照片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們進入城市時 , 世界也接受了西方人的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看向未來 , 它是一種不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 稍微簡單一點的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 是這個過程的開始 , 是在古老的近東 , 也就是所謂的近東 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是近期的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	而且它也很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約一萬年前 , 在這裡 , 兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市化 , 發生在同一地點 , 同時發生 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市都聚集在一起 , 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為它是由我們古代的祖先第一次發現穀物所產生的 , 產生出足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久居住 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些居住地是怎樣的 , 我們看到它們是緊密的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	它們被生產式農場的土地包圍 , 被像烏爾這樣的大型神殿主導 , 實際上 , 精神分配中心 , 中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神廟 , 整理收割 , 聚集在穀物裡 , 向眾神獻上 , 然後給予眾神不讓眾神吃下的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 若你想 , 這些城市的所有靈性和實體生活 , 都是由維持它們的穀類和收穫所主導 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老的城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但 , 當然 , 並非全部都是那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	最有名的是 , 在第一世紀 , 羅馬就有大約一百萬個公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	像這樣的城市是如何自給自足的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就是我所謂的 「 古老的食物路線 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬能夠接觸到海 , 讓它能夠從非常遠的距離來進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是唯一能做到這一點的方式 , 在古老世界中 , 因為要把食物運送到馬路上是很困難的 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地發動戰爭 , 在像carthage和埃及等地點打仗 , 只為了在穀物保留區取得他們的爪子 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 整個帝國的擴張其實有點像是一個長期的 , 被軍事化的購物精力所吸引 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提一下:羅馬從倫敦進口牡蠣 , 在某個階段 , 我覺得這很不尋常 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	羅馬用它的食慾來塑造它的後陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看一下十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 是從泰晤士河來的 , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場就在這個城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	這條道路從它們到廉價的道路 , 也就是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看這些街道的名稱 , 麵包街 , 你可以知道三百年前在那裏發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也來到河裡 , 也是一樣的 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 比林斯大道很有名 , 是倫敦的魚市場 , 一直到1980年代中期 , 一直在運作 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	仔細想想 , 這真是太不尋常了 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他人都帶著看起來像磚頭的行動電話到處遊蕩 , 有點像在港口發生的小魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	在城市裡 , 食物還有一件事:一旦食物進城市的根部被建立起來 , 它們就很難移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉品是一個很不一樣的故事 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進這個城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦大部分的肉都來自西北部 , 蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來了 , 抵達倫敦的西北部 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常有名的肉市場 , 位在那 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽從東安格利亞進來 , 一直到東北方 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像一個氣象女人在做這件事 。 總之 , 鳥兒也跟著腳踏進 , 保護著小小的帆布鞋 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	當他們到達便宜的東端時 , 便是他們賣的地方 , 叫做 「 波爾圖 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看任何城市的地圖在工業時代之前 , 你可以追蹤食物的來源 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以實際看到它是如何被食物所塑造的 , 不論是閱讀街頭的名稱 , 給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在前一輩 , 是你在星期五去買你的魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也要想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共場所是唯一一個購買食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年的史密斯菲爾德的形象 , 你可以看到 , 很難住在這樣的城市 , 且無法意識到你的食物從何而來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在做星期日午餐 , 可能有三天前你窗戶外的心情或出血 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機的城市 , 是有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 最早的火車乘客當中有一些是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們在視力和心智方面被屠殺 , 在鄉間的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們是用鐵軌來到這個城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 它讓它第一次能夠在任何地方種植大小和形狀的城市 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去城市被地理限制住 ; 過去 , 必須透過非常困難的身體手段取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們就從地理分析中解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	正如你從倫敦的地圖上所看到的 , 在火車來襲的90年後 , 倫敦的地圖從動物們進來的一小塊開始 , 很容易餵飽牠們的小點 , 以此類推 , 如此如此 , 非常難以餵飽任何人的腳 , 無論是動物還是人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然這只是開端 。 火車來了之後 , 這真的是這過程的結尾 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是這座城市最後的解放 , 從任何與大自然的關係中解放出來 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是那種沒有氣味、沒有混亂的城市 , 當然也沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢想走在這樣的地景中走路 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們把食物送到他們的車裡 , 開到郊區某處的一個箱子裡 , 帶回一週的購物 , 納悶著該怎麼做 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	此時此刻 , 我們與食物和城市的關係 , 徹底改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	過去 , 我們有食物是中心 , 是城市的社會核心 , 位在邊緣 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	它曾經是一個社交活動 , 購買和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會做菜 , 現在只要加點水 , 或加點點蛋 , 如果你在做蛋糕之類的 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是把標籤貼在包裝上 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不重視食物 。 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 我們害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	我們不再珍視它 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的諷刺之處在於他們已經做出承諾要讓事情變得更容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由使它可以在任何地方、任何地方建立城市 , 它們確實使我們遠離了最重要的關係 , 也就是我們和自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	而且 , 它們也讓我們依賴的體制 , 只有它們能提供 , 如我們所見 , 它們是無法永續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	所以 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪斯•摩爾問他自己 ,
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的著作《烏托邦》的前面 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	這是一系列半獨立的城邦 , 如果那聽起來很熟悉 , 每天從一個地方散步 , 每個人都有農作物 , 家後院種植蔬菜 , 一起享用共享餐點等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想 , 你們可以說食物是烏托邦的基本規則 , 即便是更多人從來沒有這樣做過 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這是另一個非常著名的烏托邦的願景 , 伊伯內茲霍華的作品 , 《花園城市》 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	相同的概念:一系列半獨立的城市 , 都市裡的小型都會區 , 周圍有可耕作的土地 , 用鐵路連接在一起 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可以被說是他視覺的有秩序原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來了 , 但和霍華所擁有的這個遠景沒什麼關係 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是這些烏托邦思想的問題 , 他們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是個詞 , 湯瑪斯•摩爾故意使用這個詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為希臘語有雙重衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以意味著一個好地方 , 或不在任何地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為那是很理想的 。 這是假想的 。 我們無法擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 用來思考人類居住地最深刻的問題 , 這樣就不太有用了 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 來自希托邦 , 古希托邦 , 「 食物 」 , 「 地點 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經生活在希托邦了 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們了解到 , 我們可以把食物當作一個非常強大的工具──一個概念性工具 , 設計工具 , 用不同的方式塑造世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	如果我們這樣做 , 希托邦會長什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我覺得這看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我要用這張投影片 , 只是狗的臉上的表情 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	總之 , 這是生命的中心 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌的 , 被享受的 , 人們花時間為它奮鬥 。
this is where food should be in our society .	食物就在我們的社會裡 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但除非有像這樣的人 , 否則你不能有這樣的場景 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順帶一提 , 這也可以是男性 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到食物 , 會想 , 先計畫 , 誰能盯著一堆生菜 , 實際認可他們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網路的一部份 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這種人 , 我們就沒有這種地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	這裡 , 我刻意這樣選 , 因為那是一個男人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網路、市場 , 食物在當地生長 。
it's common . it's fresh .	很普遍 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	它是社交生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為沒有了這些 , 你就不可能有這種地方 , 當地種植的食物 , 也是當地種植的 , 也是風景的一部分 , 不只是在看不見的地獄裡的零和商品 。
cows with a view .	牛群有一種看法 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽堆積如山 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整個過程結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多參觀的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 孩子們被告知所有的食物 , 自己種食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這是一株叫做凱文的植物 , 或者它屬於凱文的孩子 , 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	總之 , 這些試圖與大自然重新連結的計劃是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 希托邦 , 對我而言 , 是一種看待的方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 意識到 , 希托邦已經存在於各地的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅在於加入他們 , 把食物當作一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就不再把城市看作是大的、大都市化的、沒生產力的區塊 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看作是這樣 , 它是生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 無可避免地 , 與它們相連 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是很好的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再這樣生產食物了 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更深入思考永續栽培 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖可以總結出我們該做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	這是對食物如何塑造我們的生活的一種觀念 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像 , 是650年前的 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	安布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂的《良好政府的寓言》
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市與鄉村之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 這個國家會照顧這個城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	現在我想問大家 , 安布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂的油漆是怎樣的如果他今天畫了這張圖 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	如今良好政府的寓言會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個很迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的問題 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們是吃什麼的 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們把這個點子用作是非常強大的工具 , 來改善世界的形狀 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	同情心發行的幾週後 , 凱倫阿姆斯壯在二十一世紀 , 探究宗教角色:它的教條能否分裂我們 ? 還是它會讓我們團結在一起 ? 她會檢視能驅使世界的信仰重新找回信念的催化劑 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted大獎 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , tedglobal2009年的tedglobal , 暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:咱們先從黃金法則開始吧 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直感到沮喪 , 因為身為一個宗教歷史學家 , 我突然意識到同情心的核心 , 在世界上所有的大宗教信仰中 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都演化出自己所謂的黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 會有正面的版本 「 總是對待別人 , 只要你想要對待自己 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是 , 負面的版本 「 不要對其他人做你不希望他們做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你的心 , 去了解它是什麼讓你疼痛 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 去衝突別人的疼痛 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們很重視同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很棒 , 而是因為它有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了 「 孔子的黃金法則 」 時 , 如孔子所說: 「 整天、每天 」 , 不只是在做好事而已 , 再回到貪婪和自我意識的一生中 , 而是一整天都在做這件事 , 把自己從世界的中心剝奪走 , 再來 , 超越自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它為你帶來了一種名為 「 神 」 、 「 涅 」 、 「 涅 」 、 「 道 」 的存在 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的超越了我們的自我意識 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你永遠不會知道這在宗教生活中是如此的重要
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些很棒的例外 , 當宗教人士聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 他們爭論抽象的教義 , 或是說出一堆仇恨或煽動對同性戀或類似的事的仇恨 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	人們通常不想變得有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	有時我會看到 , 當我在和一群宗教人士談話時 , 有點像是站在嘴邊的表情 , 因為人們通常會希望是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然會打敗運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我對ted這麼感激 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很輕鬆地把我從我的書籍研究帶到21世紀 , 讓我能對一個比我想像的更廣的觀眾說話 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我感到很急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們無法在全球實施黃金法則 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 都一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 把下一代交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代最偉大的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球性社會 , 如我所說 , 讓人們可以和平共處 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	宗教應該要做出重大貢獻 , 反而被視為是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 想像力的想像力的行為 , 把自己放在他人的位置上 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有一個選擇 , 對我來說 ,
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續或強調我們信仰的教條和寬容的面向 , 或者我們可以回到拉比希爾 , 和耶穌相處的年長者 , 當他站立在一條腿上時 , 去總結整個猶太教教教的教誨 , 他說: 「 這樣對你不好 , 不要對你的鄰居做 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	這就是托拉 , 其他一切都只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	而拉比和早期教會的父親們 , 他們說 , 任何對經文的詮釋 , 任何對仇恨和鄙視的經文都是不合法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要復活那份精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這並不只是因為愛的精神喚醒我們而已 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們得要讓它實現 , 且我們能用ted推出的現代傳播溝通來實現它 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對所有夥伴的回應都感到非常興奮 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群人 , 會用這一系列規定來治癒新加坡社會的分裂 , 最近在新加坡有一些國會議員 , 想要在政治上實施它 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 會有一場藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家會帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 向他們展示 , 同情心同時也隱藏在所有藝術的根部 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在歐洲各地 , 穆斯林社區都在舉辦活動和討論 , 正在討論同情心在伊斯蘭和所有信仰的核心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能就此停止 , 它無法停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教學 , 也是我們如此誤解的地方 , 僅僅是相信abstrustrus的教誨而已 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教導必須永遠導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在我過世的那一天做這個工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我希望和我們的合作夥伴繼續做兩件事 , 來教育和激發同情心 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育 , 因為我們已經失去了同情心 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常認為這只意味著對某個人感到抱歉 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但 , 當然 , 如果你只是想一想 , 你並不了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須這樣做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望媒體參與其中 , 因為媒體在幫助我們分化一些我們對其他人的刻板印象 , 使我們和其他人分開 。
the same applies to educators .	同樣適用於教育家 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望青少年能夠體會到動態的感覺 , 一種充滿同情心的生活方式的動態和挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也可以看到它需要有急性智慧 , 不僅僅是單純的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想要呼籲學者 , 探索自己和其他人的傳統中慈悲的主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的是 , 鼓勵大家對於沒有同情心的言論 , 這麼一來 , 因為人們有這本憲章 , 不論他們的信仰 , 不論他們的信仰 , 不論他們的信仰 , 或他們缺乏信仰 , 他們的言論就會被賦予 , 不論他們的宗教領袖 , 他們的政治領袖 , 來自工業界的船長 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們能改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把這章放上網路 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然被困在一個舊世界裡 , 一大堆的博芬斯坐在一間房間裡 , 引發了另一則神秘的陳述 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted介紹了我一種全新的思考和呈現想法的方式 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為那就是ted美妙的地方 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專業知識 , 如果我們同心協力 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 問題有時似乎無法解決 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但我想要引用一句話來結束這場演講的結尾是關於一位英國作家牛津作家我不常引用他的話來引用c.c.s.路易斯
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一篇從我還是個學童時就一直牢記在我的心裡的東西 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	這是在他的書《四個愛人》中 。
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 他區分性愛 , 當兩個人凝視、拼字 , 彼此的眼睛時 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把友誼和友誼做比較 , 當兩個人站在同一陣線 , 肩並肩 , 他們的眼睛固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信不疑
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	在我們對vey的小小判斷過程中 , 我感覺到它非常強烈 , 當不同說服的人聚在一起 , 肩並肩作戰 , 朝向共同的目標前進 , 差異會融化 。
and we learn amity .	我們會學習到 「 同情心 」 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會了一起生活 , 了解彼此 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	davidmacaulay仰賴風力 , 有時甚至超現實的旅程 , 朝向羅馬競技場的勝利之路前進 , 他對於歷史城市的致敬致敬 。
macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	macarthurgant , 藝術 , 藝術 , 藝術 , 藝術 , 城市 , 溝通 , 文化 , 設計 , 娛樂 , 幽默 , 說故事 。
i draw to better understand things .	我畫畫得更加深入地去了解事物 。
sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時 , 我畫了很多圖 , 但我仍然無法理解我在畫什麼 。

he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他下到地下室 , 開始檢查電線 , 然後逐漸地 , 爬到建築的頂端 , 每間公寓 , 檢查每個電視機 , 檢查每一個連線 , 希望能找出問題的所在 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他一直往上走 , 終於 , 樓梯直到他抵達閣樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開閣樓的窗戶 , 當然 , 還有一張桌布 , 圍繞著建築的電視天線 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他移除它 , 問題就解決了 , 所有在palazzo的人都很快樂 。
and of course , he also solves his own problem .	當然 , 他也解決自己的問題 。
all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在要做的就只有一個完美的桌子 , 就是等她到來 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但似乎不足以傳達任何我想要表達的關於羅馬的訊息 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 好吧 , 我只會做廣場 , 我會進進去 , 下面我會展示這些東西 , 因而塑造了它們的形狀 , 以此類推 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 不 , 我只把我最喜歡的部分和片段放到萬神殿裡 , 這樣你就可以看到聖誕節的頂端 , 金字塔提斯的金字塔 , 還有布拉曼特的泰坦女神 , 都站在這個神奇的空間裡 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這只是一幅圖 , 所以我想也許皮納西去見埃舍爾赫爾是時候了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你可以看到我開始真正失去了控制權 , 同時也失去了希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條非常薄的藍色線條 , 貫穿了這條路 , 讓這條路連接在一起 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在幹嘛 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不只是收集和儲存資訊的好方式 , 還包含了一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 一層一層一層一層一層地偏離另一層 ; 我們認為他們是一頁 , 以某種方式進行 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但 , 把它們想像成層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是個地層 , 水平層 , 垂直的層次 , 我在想 , 如果把一頁剝去 , 就可以讓你們用正確的方式來思考 , 讓我來呈現出層次的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	在羅馬大部分建築的牆壁上 , 許多樓房都覆蓋著疤痕 ; 數世紀來 , 數個世紀的疤痕被改造 , 而不是被拆除 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你們展開 , 看見背後的我說的是疤痕組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 製造出更小的窗戶是必要的 , 因為壞人會來或其他的 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	各式各樣的適應作用都被埋在了黏土下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這張palazzo的頁面拿出來讓你們看看裡面發生了什麼事
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我也可以讓你們看看 , 在這些偉大的建築物的角落裡 , 那些巨大的石塊 , 或那些用磚頭和石灰做成的假石塊 , 情況更加常見 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它會變得有點3d立體 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以帶你走下一條狹窄的小街 , 進入其中一個令人驚訝的廣場 , 使用雙重摺疊頁 , 如果你和我小時候看一本彈出式書 , 希望你把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把頭上的紙包覆著 , 用在那短暫的時間內的廣場上 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我真的沒有做任何比摺疊頁更複雜的事 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但接著我想 , 也許我可以簡單一點 。

here's a book completely wide open .	這是一本完全開放的書 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不打開這本書 , 如果我只打開90度 , 我們就在俯視萬神廟的前面 , 往下看 , 往下看 , 往下看 , 往下看 , 往下看 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我翻開書 , 翻過來 , 我們就在萬神廟前方橫越廣場 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有把戲法變成一本沒有打開整體的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這似乎很有希望 。 我心想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 我甚至可以把摺疊作品和一部分開放的書結合在一起 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	我們進入萬神廟內部 , 它會不斷的變大 , 以此類推 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我是站在正確的軌道上 , 但它似乎失去了人類的特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的觀點 , 總是一件好事 , 如果你想讓人們專注於一本書 , 一路上收集資訊 , 這是一件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 震撼了我 , 是個難懂的頭銜 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果這是一隻親愛的鴿子 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是這趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個頭銜能成功 , 用它 。 但它會是一段經歷羅馬的旅程 , 展示出我喜歡羅馬的所有事物 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	這是一隻教堂頂上的鴿子 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天去做正常的鴿子之類的事 。 回來 , 整個位置都覆蓋著鷹架和綠色網路 , 而這種鴿子無法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	現在這是一隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 它將必須找到另一個居住的地方 , 這使我能走過我最喜歡的目錄 , 我們從最高的開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回去和家人一起生活 , 這不一定是好事 , 但它確實能讓鴿子再次結合在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這很有趣 , 但或許有一個人應該要這樣做 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他一生都在照顧生病鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方 , 讓他們感到危險的地方 , 不論如何 , 他們都會和這個人交朋友 , 學會為他做招術 , 在午餐時間 , 或像那樣娛樂他 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	有一種真實的連結存在於老人和這些鴿子之間 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事的結尾時 , 病得非常嚴重 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教導他們拼他的名字 , 那是aldo 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	有一天 , 三、四天沒見到他之後 , 他住在這個小小的車庫裡 , 他們拼出他的名字 , 四處飛舞 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到了足夠的力量 , 爬上梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有鴿子 , 一個紅色的氣球 , 都在等著他 , 他們把他帶到城市的牆壁上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這個:只要他失去一隻鴿子 , 他就會把那隻鴿子帶到城市的牆壁外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在羅馬的舊習俗中 , 死亡人士從未被埋在牆壁中 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這個故事真的很開心 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這將會有很長的路要走 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了...再一次 , 如果包裝不管用 , 如果故事不在哪裡 , 我只想出了標題 , 希望書名能在正確的方向上把我踢下 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時它的確讓我有足夠的專注 , 我甚至會做個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	這些全部都是書名 , 最終引領我找到解決方案 , 這是關於一位年輕女性的故事 , 她在羅馬城外的羅馬城外傳遞訊息給羅馬人的故事 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	鴿子正從阿塔維亞往下飛過去 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看見墳墓和松餅 , 一路上諸如此類 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你看到的是鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不見紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時此刻 , 必要和可能 , 試圖傳達出那種在城市中飛越城市的感覺 , 不用移動就知道飛越城市的感覺 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	穿過了西斯提烏斯金字塔 , 這對你來說很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬 , 過過了大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這有點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這種鴿子做了一件大多謀殺鴿子沒做的事:它採用了一種篩選路線 , 我覺得這個裝置有必要把這本書延伸到四頁以外 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞過羅馬競技場 , 越過聖母瑪麗亞教會的聖母堂 , 和海克力士通往河流的神廟 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎碰撞了palazzzofarnesse的作品 , 米開朗基羅的作品 , 用里程碑縮小的距離建造了石塊 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們往下滑過卡波迪利的fiori 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我向我的學生展示的其中一件事 , 因為這完全是對任何規則都否認的 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的觀點是 , 如果它看起來可信 , 你已經成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出這些消失點在哪兒 ; 有幾個在火星上 , 還有一些在克雷門的其他人 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在廣場上 , 在聖母瑪麗亞•戴拉•帕斯的前面 , 無一例外 , 有一場足球比賽正在進行 , 我們被足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是個很糟糕的例子 , 說明被足球擊中的畫面 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的作品:聖母瑪麗亞•德拉•羅斯 , 有足夠的球 , 有一點點鳥翅膀 , 什麼也沒發生 , 所以我得要重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	假如你想要看到聖母瑪麗亞•迪拉的步調 , 這些書非常有彈性 , 非常有互動性 , 只要把它反過來 , 用另一種方式來看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過對話 , 我們可以看到紅線的影響 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	之後 , 鳥能夠把自己拉過來 , 這座中世紀的高塔 , 剩下的中世紀塔塔樓之一 , 朝聖聖地奇教堂前進 , 最周圍的高塔 , 向下看向廣場 , 我們已經提到過、見過、飛過數次了 ; 在這四條河流的前幾座上 , 還有穿過美麗的布羅米努伊•聖母堂 , 停在足夠的26英呎高度上 , 來到達我們呼吸的房間 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們可以在內部四處飛行 , 因為我們在飛行 , 我們不用擔心這個特定時刻的重力 , 這樣這幅圖在紙上的任何方向都可以 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會有點開心 , 用這種方式來模仿建築並不讓人意外 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	經過一面美麗的牆壁 , 充滿了我剛剛所提到的混合物 ; 美麗的雕刻品被捲入了neonstants的牆壁中 , 簽名等等 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最終 , 我們終於抵達了palazzo的庭院 , 也就是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入一扇窗戶 , 進入閣樓 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把留言從鳥的腿上移除 , 這就是它所說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看這幅畫板 , 我們看到他正在做的事 , 其實是一張旅程的地圖 , 鴿子剛剛走過的地圖 , 紅線延伸了所有的視野 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 這樣我們就能完成理解的循環 , 你所要做的就是讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的天然資源研究員在自我組裝上工作 , 不用建造任何東西 , 我們能創造出一些材料 , 來建造它們自己 , 就像一股dna一樣 。 這是個大概念 ; 在初期 , tibbits告訴我們三個項目 , 來暗示一個自我組裝的未來 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	高空的tibbits:我們能不能做出東西來製造自己 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天 , 我想讓大家看看我們創造東西的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 我們的建築物和機器很快就會自行組裝、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	接下來我要讓大家看看 , 我相信目前的生產狀態 , 再和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	目前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓 , 兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個部分 , 相當複雜、新、令人振奮的技術鋼、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人振奮的機器可以帶領我們進入太空五年的組裝時間 , 兩百五十萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你觀察自然生態系統 , 我們有兩百萬種蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈秒折疊 , 或dna有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以在我們的自然系統裡有這麼多的複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠遠超過任何我們能建立的任何東西 , 遠遠超過任何我們能建立的任何東西 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們的效率更高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎沒有犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然系統有超級有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以把它翻譯成我們的建築環境 , 那麼 , 對於我們建造東西的方式 , 會產生一些令人振奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	如果我們想要在實體環境中自行組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的複雜性 , 這樣我們的建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解讀簡單的序列 , 基本上就是我們建築物的運作方式的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部分 , 來使用該序列 , 來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量讓它啟動 , 讓我們的零件能夠從程式中折疊起來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的矯正措施來保證我們已經成功地建立了我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	接下來我要向各位展示幾個項目 , 是我在麻省理工學院的同事和我正在研發的 , 能夠達成這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前面的兩位是巨型機器人和底特律機器人 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些項目都是大型的可重組的機器人 , 8英尺 , 12英呎長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們被嵌入在機械裝置和感應器中 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	解碼你想要摺疊的東西 , 變成一連串負120 , 負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120 , 負120這類的事情 ; 所以一連串的角度 , 或旋轉 , 再把序列送進去 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每一單位都需要負120單位才能轉動 , 檢查一下是否到達 , 再把信息傳遞給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是優秀的科學家、工程師、設計師 , 致力於此項目的設計師 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為這真的會帶來光明:這真的是可擴展的嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 數以千計的人 , 花了很多時間 , 才做出這八英呎的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的可以擴大規模嗎 ? 我們真的可以把機械裝置嵌入每一個部位嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 探討被動的天性 , 或者被動地試圖重新組裝程式 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但更進一步 , 它會嘗試實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它嵌入了最基礎的電腦運算、數位邏輯閘門 , 直接進入你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是nand大門 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體 , 就是這個門會做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 正如你正在建造你的磚頭一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一個則是取自過去的磚頭 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會在3d空間中輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要的磚頭上加入他們想要的 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它之前所做的事 , 你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間上上上上下移動 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於0輸出 , 往下 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 0 , 輸入1輸出 , 會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著 , 我們現在的結構 , 包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有嵌入在他們身上的信息 , 關於構成的信息 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自我導向的複製 , 因為你的結構中包含著確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以替換一個部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都嵌入在告訴你們如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以擁有爬上去讀取它 , 然後在1和1之間輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接嵌入 ; 沒有任何外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個項目叫做偏見鏈 , 它可能是我們現在所擁有的最令人振奮的例子 , 就是被動的自行組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	需要重新配置和編寫能力 , 讓它變成完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都完全相同 , 且它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以 , 每個鏈、每一個元素 , 都想要向右或向左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每一個單位 , 如果它應該向左或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖動鏈接的時候 , 它會折疊成任何你已經編寫過的圖形 , 像螺旋結構 , 或者 , 在這裡 , 兩個立方體相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上你可以將任何立體形狀或單一的雙維度 , 完全被動的置入這條鏈中 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們什麼是未來的 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為這告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復我們實體結構、建築物、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些地區有新的可編程性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那之後 , 你就有了新的電腦可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 所有我們的磚塊都能夠計算出來 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是驚人的平行和分散式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這是很令人振奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以 , 我認為我在這裡展示的這些專案計畫 , 只是朝向這個未來邁進的一小步 , 如果我們實行這些新科技 , 為一個新的自行組裝世界實施 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了大陸地圖 , 甚至去過海上兩次最深的地點 。 留給下一代去探索 ? 生物學家和nathanwolffe提議:幾乎每件事都可以做得到 。 然後我們開始吧 , 跟這個不可思議的小世界說 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:剩下什麼要探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛特 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡 , 為了榮耀一個偉大的20世紀探險家羅伊.查普曼•安德魯斯 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , 安德魯斯帶領一系列的探險進入了未知的地區 , 例如在戈壁沙漠的這裡 。
he was quite a figure .	他是一個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說 , 他後來被認為是印第安納瓊斯角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛特市時 , 我在一群中學生的公開演說 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 如果在ted演講中有沒有什麼比在座各位更嚇人的話 , 它會試著把一千個12歲孩子的注意力集中在45分鐘的演講上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	演講結束時 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時起 , 有一件事一直困擾著我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們要去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想 , 很多人有一種感覺 , 地球上最偉大的探索時代已經結束了 , 對下一代來說 , 他們將必須去外太空或深海 , 去尋找有意義的探索事物 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	我們真的沒有辦法在地球上探索到什麼嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回想起生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是個未知世界的探險家 , 馬丁斯貝尼傑林克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	beijerinck開始尋找菸草鑲嵌疾病的成因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是從菸草植物中吸取受感染的汁液 , 並且用越來越小的過濾器過濾它 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他接觸到他認為一定有比當時已知的最小生命形式更小的東西存在 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為神秘的媒介命了名 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 的拉丁文 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露病毒時 , beijerinck真的為我們開啟了一個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒構成了地球上大多數基因信息 , 遠超過所有其他形式的生物的基因信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯的 , 已經有大量的實際應用 , 和這個世界有關的 , 像是天花的消滅 , 子宮頸癌的出現 , 我們現在知道大部分都是人類乳突病毒造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們沒有意識到組成地球上大部分基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	現在我們有了這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索未知的世界 , 像是深度定序 , 讓我們能做的 , 遠遠超過表面 , 去觀察特定物種的個別基因組 , 而是去檢視整個測期限 , 充滿了微生物的群落 , 不斷地在我們身邊 , 記錄了這些物種的所有基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技術應用在從土壤到皮膚之間的所有東西上 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在定期這樣做 , 來確認疫情爆發的成因 , 正是造成疫情的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓你們了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上 , 取了一把鼻塞糖 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們通常會去尋找呼吸道性病毒 , 如流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	我們會看到的第一件事 , 是非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些基因信息 , 我們會看到一些普通的嫌疑犯 , 當然 , 很多人類的基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分來自你鼻子中完全無害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了非常非常驚人的結果 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始檢視這些資訊時 , 我們會發現你鼻子中大約20%的基因信息 , 並不符合任何我們以前見過的東西 , 不管是植物、動物、真菌、病毒 , 或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們完全不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	而對於那些實際研究這種數據的小組 , 實際上我們當中有一些人開始稱之為 「 生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是任何我們以前見過的東西 ; 它有點像是在我們自己的基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子中有20%的基因信息是很多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對比較無菌的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質無法被分類 , 無法被輸入或匹配任何我們以前見過的東西 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始 , 我們以為這也許是人工製品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的技術相當新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得越來越精準時 , 我們已經判斷這些資訊是一種生命形式 , 至少有些是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設 , 只存在於它們的初期 , 有一種非常令人振奮的可能性存在:被埋在生命中 , 在這個遺傳信息中 , 是還未被辨識的生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串的a、t、t、c、g , 我們可能會發現一種全新的生命類型 , 像是beijinck , 會從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	也許這能讓我們找出折磨我們或辨識出疫情爆發的致病因子的原因 , 或許能讓我們辨識出我們不熟悉的疫苗來源 , 或創造出分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣布 , 和史丹佛大學、加州理工學院及加州大學舊金山的同事一起合作 , 我們目前正開始著手探索生物暗物質 , 來探索新形式生命的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們對病毒一無所知 , 一種組成地球上大部分基因信息的生命形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚訝 , 我們可能完全沒有意識到一種新的生命類型 , 全都在我們的鼻子底下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	的確 , 地球上所有的大陸我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳類動物但這並不表示地球上沒有其它可探索的生物
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同事 , 為下一代的探險家提供了一堂課 , 探險家們 , 像那位來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想如果我們用這一課來闡述 , 應該是像這樣的:不要假設我們目前所認為的就是全部的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	追隨你選擇去探索的任何領域的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊到處都有未知 , 且等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家大衛•戴德•戴斯奇在背上放上理論物理 , 討論更急迫的問題:我們物種的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、宇宙、環境、全球議題、物理、科技、宇宙等 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛•迪特在宇宙中的位置 ,
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要踏出肢體 , 說出讓人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這樣做 , 但我想要從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 事實上 , 史上大部分的歷史都知道這個現象 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境等等 , 都是獨一無二的適合維持我們的進化或創造 , 正如我們過去的思想和現在的存在一樣 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	今天這個想法有個戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這裡的想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是極度不友善的 , 而在我們的內心 , 我們依賴的只有這些 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們無處可去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二 , 大家都知道的 , 與我們對人類歷史的信念相反 , 人類其實不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬•霍金所說 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面的化學污垢 , 存在於一個典型的星球上 , 位於一個典型的銀河系的郊區 , 諸如此類的 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 大家都知道的兩件事 , 有點像是說我們正處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨特穿著等等 , 而第二件事則是說我們正處於一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其當你把這二者看作是深奧的真理 , 並以此來呈現你的生活決策 , 那麼他們似乎會互相矛盾 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止兩者都變成完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是的 。 讓我從第二個故事開始:典型的 。 這是典型的嗎 ? 嗯 , 讓我們看看四周 , 往一個隨機的方向看 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學污染物 , 這完全不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只需要在同一個方向上走幾百英里 , 然後往回看 , 你不會看到任何牆或化學污染 , 你所看到的都是藍色的星球 。 如果你走得更遠 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 太陽系 , 恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是宇宙的典型 , 因為星星存在於銀河中 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 都不在任何一個星系附近 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再往外看 , 直到我們在星系外 , 然後再往回看 , 巨大的星系 , 螺旋狀的手臂在我們面前擺放 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時 , 我們已經從這裡來了十萬光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然離宇宙中典型的地方很近 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到一個典型的地方 , 你要到達1000倍的空間 , 到達星系間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那會是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方長什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 昂貴的代價 , ted已經安排了一個高解析度的虛擬實境展示了星系間空間 , 從星系間空間來看 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 讓大家看看吧 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不是很完美--你看到在星系間的空間中完全是黑暗的 , 漆黑的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	很黑暗的 , 如果你在看離你最近的恆星 , 那顆星爆炸成超新星 , 而你正直盯著它看 , 當它的光照到你的時候 , 你還是看不到它甚至連一顆小金星都看不到 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙就是這麼大 , 黑暗的 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星如此的明亮 , 如此聰明 , 以至於它會在幾光年內殺死你 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從星系間的空間來看 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你甚至看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡的溫度也非常低 , 低於絕對零度的三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它非常的空虛 。 那裡的真空 , 密度比地球上最好的科技所能創造出來的高一百萬倍 。 這就是我們在這個地方所能創造出的不同之處 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	我們能把燈光打回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們怎麼知道一個離我們這麼遙遠的環境 , 如此不同 , 如此陌生的環境呢 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球的環境 , 以我們的形式創造了知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	這是什麼意思呢 ? 嗯 , 再往外看 , 比我剛剛所說的更遠 , 用望遠鏡 , 看那些看起來像星星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們被稱為 「 夸拉斯 」 , 原本的意思是兩邊形的物體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著那些看起來有點像星星 , 但不是星星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 , 幾十億年前 , 數十億光年之外 , 銀河系中心的物質掉落在一個超大質量的黑洞上 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 密集的磁場引導了一些重力崩潰的能量 。 其中一些物質 , 以極大的噴射流形式 , 照亮了葉子 , 以我認為是一兆個太陽的亮度 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人類大腦的物理學 , 幾乎不可能和這種噴射機的物理有所不同 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法一瞬間存活下來 。 一瞬間 , 一瞬間 , 一旦試圖描述某次的噴射流中 , 語言就會崩解 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這會有點像經歷超新星的爆炸 , 但在瞬間 , 每次都要經歷數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這種噴射的發生 , 正是數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 預測 , 和解釋 , 最重要的是 , 在現實中 , 你所看到的一切事物 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另一個夸拉體的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不只是表面的圖像 , 雖然它也包含了這個圖像 , 還有一個解釋性的模型 , 體現了相同的數學關係和相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 一個結構的信念 , 相似於時間的增長 , 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	這個實體物體 , 不像它們能做到的那樣 , 仍然可以體現出同樣的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間越來越多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	我們是一個不一樣的化學污垢 。 這種化學污垢有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的構造有著不斷提升的精準度 , 每件事的結構 。 這個地方 , 而非宇宙其它的地方 , 是一個中心 , 包含了整個物理實體的結構和因果關係 。 到目前為止 , 物理學的原理是不可忽視的 , 事實上 , 物理定律允許這種現象發生的 , 甚至是物理世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼 , 太陽系和我們的環境 , 以我們的形式 , 如何獲得這個與宇宙其他部分的特殊關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	關於史蒂芬•霍金的評論 , 有一點是對的 , 但這是錯的 , 重點是它沒有任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有特殊的放置 , 沒有特殊的放置 , 沒有特殊的放置 , 沒有特殊的放置 , 沒有奇蹟是介入的 。 它有三個我們所擁有的豐富 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的成長是信息處理的一種形式 。 信息處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 沒有任何方法可以製造一台電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體對我們所發現的知識產生影響 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 不具體 , 但對於開放式知識、解釋的開放式解釋而言 , 其本質就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境中充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們碰巧要做測試 , 例如 , 牛頓的重力定律 , 大約300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們過去做得到的證據在過去數十億年間 , 地球上每平方公尺的降落著 , 之後還會持續數十億年 。 其他的科學也一樣 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發掘所有科學中最根本的真相的證據 , 只是為了讓我們的星球發生的事 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們所在的位置充滿了證據 , 也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的前提條件是最低限度的 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說的 , 是空的 , 是冷的 , 外面是暗的 , 是嗎 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一個狹隘的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	想像在星系間空間中有一個立方體 , 大小和我們的房子、太陽系大小相同 。 現在 , 立方體是人類的標準非常空的 , 但這仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造出一座自給自足的太空站有一群科學家致力於創建開放式的知識流
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 遠遠超出現在的科技 , 甚至聚集到星系間的氫 , 將其轉化成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但問題是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 哪些東西能阻止我們去做 , 除非我們知道如何做呢 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 問題在於知識 , 而非資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣地 , 如果我們能自動取得能源供給 , 因為轉變會是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 同樣地 , 人類的感官也很暗 。 但你只需要用一個望遠鏡 , 即便是用現今的設計 , 看看外面的銀河 , 就像我們從這裡看到的一樣 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	用一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你可以看見星星 , 行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你可以做天體物理學 , 並且學習物理定律 。
