and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	局部在那裡 , 你可以建立粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最難做的科學可能是生物學實地考察 , 因為要花上數億年才能到達最近的生物體 , 再回來 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我得告訴各位 , 很抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從來不喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每隔幾億年就完成一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以 , 事實上 , 星系間空間確實包含了所有開放式知識的前提 。 任何一個立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何一個角落 , 都可以變成跟我們一樣的樞紐 , 如果知道怎麼做的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	我們並不是在一個獨特的友好環境裡 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間的空間能夠創造出一串開放式的解釋流 , 那麼 , 幾乎其他的環境也是 。 地球也是污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	限制因素 , 這裡和這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充足 , 但知識 , 很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個宇宙知識型的觀點 , 也許我認為應該讓我們感到非常特別 。 但這也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有需要特定的知識 , 能夠在宇宙中持續存在的挑戰中存活下來 , 我們就無法存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要幾光年的超新星消失 , 我們就死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁•雷斯最近寫了一本書 , 關於我們對於各種事物的脆弱 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗出錯 , 最重要的是 , 和大規模毀滅性武器的恐怖主義有關 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為人類文明只有50%的機率能在這個世紀存活下來 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚點會在研討會上討論這個議題 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的類別 , 可以討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他的看法 , 我們可以生存下來 , 我們可以失敗生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這並不取決於機率 , 而是在於我們是否能及時創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	這種危險完全不是前所未有的物種會絕種
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明的結尾 , 絕大多數的物種 , 和所有的文明 , 都是現在的歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想要成為例外的話 , 那麼我們唯一的希望就是使用一種特徵來區分我們人類和文明 , 與其他所有特徵 , 即 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋能力 , 新的知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	讓我把這個應用在當前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是要說明我要說的 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議就是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是一個物理學家 , 但是我不是一個正確的物理學家 。 以全球暖化的角度來說 , 我只是個懶人 。 理性地 , 要認真看待科學的理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太晚了 , 無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果這是真的 , 我們目前最好的選項是防止二氧化碳排放 , 像是京都議定書 , 經濟活動的限制 , 以及數百億美元的巨大成本 , 不管是什麼 , 那就已經是個災難了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而那些倡導的行動 , 甚至沒有被提出來解決這個問題的行動 , 僅僅是稍微延遲這個問題 , 已經太遲了 。 要避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 自從任何人意識到它的危險就開始了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代 , 可能已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放量即將造成數十億人死亡的新冰河時代 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這件事讓我很清楚 , 我也不知道為什麼它沒有公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	這是我們永遠無法得知的 。 當我們知道即將發生的災難 , 以及如何解決這災難的代價不到災難的代價時 , 真的沒有太多的爭論 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 , 可以避免我們還沒有預防的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個解決問題的立場 , 而不是僅限於問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	的確 , 一盎司的預防方法等於一磅的解藥 , 但這只是我們知道如何預防 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你已經在鼻子上打了一拳 , 那麼醫學的科學就無法教你如何避免拳擊 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再尋求治療 , 只專注於預防 , 那它也幾乎無法達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	此時此刻 , 世界正忙著計劃著減少氣體排放的計劃 , 不計代價 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要以計劃來降低溫度 , 並計劃生存到更高的溫度 , 不計代價 , 而是更有效率、更便宜的計劃 。 有些計劃是 , 像是一群鏡子 , 來將陽光偏轉 , 鼓勵水分生物消耗更多二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	此時此刻 , 這些都是邊緣的研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力解決這個問題的核心 , 也不是一般性的解決方法 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	有了我們還沒意識到的問題 , 能夠正確地解決問題的能力 , 不是無限期地避免好運的能力 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 還有生存問題 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩個石板 , 刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個 , 雕刻: 「 問題是可以解決的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	而在另一個雕刻上: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果一個國家的制度被困在不良的制度下 , 要如何讓一個掙扎的國家擺脫貧窮 ? 如果它被困在不良的制度下 ? 經濟學家保羅•羅默揭開一個大膽的想法: 「 特許城市 」 、 「 城市 」 的行政區 , 被國家聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、政治 ,
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅•羅馬極端的想法:特定的城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在做功課 , 是在首都機場的路燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特定的學生 , 但我碰過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子 , 綠色襯衫的這一隻 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭尼爾森有一支手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼nelson可以使用先進技術 , 像手機 , 但無法取得一個一百年的技術 , 來在家中產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	糟糕的規則可以防止雙贏的解決方案在人們可以把新科技帶進來 , 讓像nelson這樣的人可以使用 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司遵循一條規則 , 認為它必須以非常低的價格銷售電力 , 事實上 , 它的價格很低 , 賣掉的每一單位都要價錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它既沒有資源 , 也沒有動機去連結許多其他用戶 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這條規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他見到 , 有一組不同的規則和規則 , 讓企業獲利很小 , 所以他們有動機去登記客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這是尼爾森從下面運作中購買手機電話的那種規則 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統已經知道這些規則如何運作良好 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變電價價的規則 , 但他碰到的卻是來自企業和消費者的抗議暴風暴 , 想要保存既有的補貼比率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他堅守著規則 , 避免他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森卡在街燈下學習 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰在於 , 是試著弄清楚如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	有一些規則我們可以發展出改變規則的發展嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想強調的是 , 有一個普遍的抽象的見解 , 能夠實際做事的見解 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給予人們更多的選擇 , 對許多國家的領導者更多的選擇 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 呈現出這兩者之間的反對意見是很有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給領導者的那種選擇 , 像是給總統在電力上提高價格 , 在經濟上 , 剝奪人民想要的選項 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇繼續使用補貼的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到方法給雙方更多的選擇 , 那就給了我們一套規則 , 來改變那些讓我們脫離困境的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	現在 , 尼爾森也能上網 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的破壞作用 , 規則能讓人們在黑暗中 , 看著美國太空總署在晚上拍攝的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是看看亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你拉近這裡 , 可以看到北韓 , 在這邊的線上 , 跟旁邊的黑洞相比 , 像個黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則讓人們在黑暗中保持在黑暗中
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 重要的是要了解 , 北韓和南韓始於一貫的制度 , 無論是法律或法規 , 還是更深層的理解、規範、文化、價值觀 , 和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做了選擇 , 導致他們各自的規則走上了非常不同的道路 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	我們可以改變身為人類的我們 , 可以改變我們彼此互動的規則 , 改善或改善 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在讓我們看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大在海地上 , 在這邊的線上 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 相較於這裡的鄰居多明尼加共和國 , 那裡的居民數量也差不多 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家都是黑暗的 , 相較於波多黎各 , 波多黎各有一半的居民是海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是 , 規則是不好的 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不光是這些規則是不好的 , 因為政府的力量太大 , 太壓迫 , 就像在北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想創造出有良好規則的環境 , 我們不能只拆掉 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也得想辦法建設 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地展示了與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到資料的一開始 , 中國是世界上高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國擁有先驅科技 , 例如鋼、印刷、火藥等技術 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從來沒有採用 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則上 , 來鼓勵那些想法散播出去的利益動機 , 這樣才能鼓勵散播出去 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 減緩了創新的速度 , 把中國從世界其他地方除去 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	隨著世界上其他國家的創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 也發展新的規則 , 中國也從這些進步中脫離 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	那裡的收入仍然停滯不前 , 隨著世界其他地方的收入逐漸縮小 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪了中國的平均收入在美國是平均收入的百分比
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在1950和1960年代 , 大家可以看到 , 大約有3%的人在空中盤旋 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代末期 , 情況改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	成長在中國開始 , 中國開始趕上美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在晚上回到地圖上 , 你可以得到一條線索 , 引領中國的體制有劇烈變化 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的地點 , 在這條線的邊緣 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港只是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀 , 大部份的運作都是以非常不同的規則運作 , 相較於其餘的中國規則 , 當時勞動市場經濟 , 由英國政府來執行 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個有數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸到大陸 , 開始像縫製衣服、做玩具的地方 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了進一步 , 增加收入 , 增加技能 , 導致非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個典範 , 領導人像鄧小平能夠複製 , 當他們決定將整個大陸移向市場模式時 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫中國的每個人立即轉換到市場模式 , 他們不如通過創建一些特區 , 某種程度上來說 , 可以做到的 , 英國所做的是:讓機會與市場規則一同使用 , 讓那些想要參與市場的人們能夠參與 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港周圍建立了四個經濟特區 , 讓中國能夠來工作 , 城市在當地成長非常快速 ; 外國企業也可以進來 , 做點什麼 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的其中一區有個城市叫做深圳 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有一家台灣公司製造了你們很多人都擁有的iphone , 他們和來自中國的勞工一起工作 , 他們搬到深圳的中國人 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	在四個特別的區域之後 , 有十四個沿海城市在同一方面開放 , 最終在這些地方展示出成功 , 人民可以選擇居住的地方 , 因為他們提供的優勢 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證實了成功導致一致同意向整個經濟體邁進市場模式的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了幾個點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一 , 保留對人的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	二:在正確的尺度上運作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變一個村落裡的規則 , 你可以做到 , 但村落會太小 , 無法得到好處 , 如果你有數百萬人都在做好的體制下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試圖改變這個國家的規則 , 你就不能給一些人一個機會來支撐 , 看看事情如何發生 , 讓其他人先放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但 , 城市給了你機會 , 創造出新地方、有新的規則 , 讓人們可以選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們夠大 , 足以得到我們所能擁有的所有好處 , 只要我們在數百萬人的統治之下 , 我們就能擁有所有的好處 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	提議的是我們構想一個叫做特區城市的東西 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則開始 , 規範所有規則 , 來吸引我們建立城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們得要吸引投資者 , 他們會建立基礎建設──能源系統、道路、港口、機場、建築 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引一家公司 , 他們首先會僱用那些搬到那兒的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭 , 接觸到那些將來會永久居住的居民 , 撫養他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子取得教育 , 取得他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了這個章節 , 人們就會搬到那裡去 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造起來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模式 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以不斷地重複這個動作 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些都在憲章中被捕獲 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模式之中如果我們能在無人居住的土地上建立城市
you start from uninhabited territory .	從無人居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以在新的章節裡生活 , 但沒有人會被強迫在它底下生活 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後 , 我們需要的是對領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們希望領導者能做出的選擇我們需要讓國家之間的合作夥伴們能夠一起合作 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的方式 , 首先建構一個小小的市場模型 , 然後再將它擴大到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 不經意地 , 透過香港的行動 , 減少了世界貧窮 , 比上個世紀我們已經完成的援助計畫還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們讓這樣的合作關係再度重現 , 我們就能讓全世界都得到這些好處 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會讓負責任的授權 , 由一個國家的控制權授權到另一個國家 , 來接管一些行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這麼說的時候 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這會讓殖民主義恢復嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是 。 但很重要的是要了解到當我們開始思考這些事時所產生的那種情緒 , 可能會阻礙我們回過頭去 , 可能會停止我們的能力 , 同時我們對探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這和殖民主義不同 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義的不好之處在於 , 在某些援助計畫中 , 居住地很不好 , 是因為它牽涉到強權和優越的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這種模式的重點在於選擇 , 不論是領導者 , 對於住在新地方的人來說 , 都是如此 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是強迫和強迫的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何實踐它 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們看看某個特定的領袖 , 拉爾•卡斯楚 , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定想過他有機會為古巴古巴做些什麼 , 讓鄧小平在古巴島上沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確有一點點南方的光 , 南方的地位非常特別 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關達那摩灣周圍有一區 , 在那裡有條約為美國政府負責一塊土地 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚跑去加拿大總理的首相 , 說: 「 聽著 , 南基斯有個可怕的公關問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要逃出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	你為什麼不 , 加拿大 , 接管呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一座新城市在上面建設 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近有個香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會搬到那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會退縮 , 但這會是通往我國家的現代經濟和現代世界的通道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	那麼 , 這模式還能在哪裡試驗呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	非洲 , 我和非洲的領袖談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	當中許多人完全了解一個特區的概念 , 人們可以選擇一個特區來做為一條規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方法 , 讓人們選擇選擇愛因斯坦 , 沒有強制力 , 同時也沒有強制力 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解到 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更好的承諾 , 那些將來建造港口、建造道路的投資者 , 在一個新城市中 , 他們可以做出更可信的承諾 , 只要他們能和一個合作夥伴的國家合作 , 他們就能做出更好的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許就算在某些安排中 , 有點像信託管理帳戶 , 你把土地放在信託管理帳戶裡 , 另一半的國家也需要對它負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	在非洲也有許多土地可以建造新城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是在我沿著海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣的大地 , 有著巨大的延伸 , 讓數億人可以住在這樣的土地上 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	如果我們概括一下並思考 , 不只一到二個特區 , 而是數十個城市 , 能為數億億人創造空間 , 也許未來的數十億人會搬到城市去 , 在未來的未來有足夠的土地給他們 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在全世界 , 如果我們看看夜晚的燈光 , 其中一個誤導是 , 視覺上看來 , 世界上大部分的人已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我來解釋為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把所有土地的樣貌呈現出來 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方塊 , 代表地球上所有的可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被現在居住的三十億人口所佔據的城市 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到長方形的底部 , 你可以看到 , 目前存在三十億個城市居民的城市只佔地球上百分之三的可耕地 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要為另外十億人建造城市 , 他們就會變成這樣 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從3%的耕地 , 變成4% 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們大幅減少了人類在地球上的足跡 , 藉由建造更多人們可以移動的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市遵守良好的規則 , 就能成為人們從犯罪、疾病和衛生的安全城市 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到一份工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以得到一些基本公共事業 , 像是電力 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要花什麼代價 , 才能開始建造第一座特區的城市 , 擴大規模 , 才能建造出更多這樣的城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	一份手冊會比較好 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們可以做的就是撰寫一些文章裡的細節 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們經營城市 , 走出去設計城市 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者在野外 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們開始思考一些問題 , 例如 , 假設加拿大不僅能處理拉帕斯楚問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西是參與者 , 西班牙也是 。 或許古巴想成為四方聯合創業的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何撰寫協定來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	之前的比例較少 , 但這可能很容易被解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助它 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 新加坡和香港都是一開始擁有土地的巨大收穫城市 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的收穫來支付警察、法庭的費用 , 但學校的體制和健康照護體系 , 使得土地更具吸引力 , 更具吸引力 , 讓人們有更高的收入 , 如此一來 , 土地就會更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 協助建造這塊區域的人的誘因 , 建立起它 , 建立基礎的規則 , 朝向正確的方向前進 。
so there are many other details like this .	還有很多其他的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓那些低成本的建築物 , 讓第一份工作的人們 , 組裝成iphone , 卻能讓這些建築物節能 , 確保它們是安全的 , 不會落在地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	很多技術上的細節已經被解決了 , 但是我們這些已經開始追求這些東西的人已經知道沒有路障、沒有阻礙 , 除了想像力的失敗之外 , 還會讓我們無法實現真正的全球雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片作結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	儘管地球上有這麼多人 , 我們之所以能如此順利 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現他們時 , 他們也會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	這不像稀少的物品 , 共享意味著我們每個人都會變少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用這種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另外一類的想法:主導我們如何互動的規則 ; 例如 , 規則 , 讓我們來制定一個支援研究大學的課程系統 , 免費提供某種程度的知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們建立一個制度 , 讓土地在政府部門登記的土地 , 讓人們可以承諾作為抵押品 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們可以在規則的空間上創新 , 特別是在創新體制中想出改變規則的概念 , 所以我們不會被壞規則卡住 , 那麼我們可以繼續進步 , 真正地讓世界變得更美好 , 讓尼爾森和他的朋友在街燈下不再學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	克雷格•凡特 , 基因組學先驅休息了一下他的史詩般的圓環探險 , 來談談他的團隊目前發現的數百萬個基因 , 來繪製出海洋生物多樣性的地圖 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技等 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	dna和大海上的craigventer和craigventer 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	等一下 , 幾個人問我對於老化辯論的看法 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀的人比悲觀者要活得更久 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我在18分鐘內要告訴你們的是我們如何從閱讀基因編碼轉換到開始編寫程式的第一階段
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅十年前 , 這個月 , 我們出版了第一組免費生存有機體的序列 , 即嗜血桿菌 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這需要一個從13年到4個月的基因組計劃 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八個小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去的十年裡 , 大量的基因組被加入了:大部份的病原體、幾株植物、幾隻昆蟲和幾種哺乳動物 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	想法在十年前的這個階段的基因組學是 , 今年底 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組學的基因組學定序 , 大約是幾百個 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂•摩爾基金會取得了一筆資金 , 今年已經完成了130項基因定序 , 做為環保有機體的一邊專案 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但 , 仔細看 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有抓到這個星球上的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分的人沒有意識到它 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔了地球生物總量的一半 , 而所有的動物只佔了所有生物總量的1/1 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人不常做的事 , 但如果你去海邊 , 吞了一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的海水中有大約一百萬個細菌 , 以一千萬個病毒的數量持續到一千萬個 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	不到5000種微生物種類在兩年前就已經有了特徵 , 所以我們決定採取行動 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了索克爾二號探險 , 在那裡 , 我們在那裡 , 進行了偉大的海洋探險 , 試圖在200英里內捕捉海洋樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始做我們的測試計畫 , 接著搬到霍利法斯 , 沿著美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉巴哥群島 , 橫越太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫越印度洋的這一步 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的任務 , 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 一方面幫助激勵年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只用海水過濾 , 用不同的濾鏡收集不同大小的生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 每24小時可以對基因編碼進行一億億個字母排序 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	通過這樣做 , 我們得到了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 有人認為我們眼中的視覺色素 , 只有一兩種有機體存在於這樣的環境中 , 有著相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有在上層海洋中在溫暖的地區的生物都有相同的光感應器 , 用太陽光來源 , 用它們的能量和溝通 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地方 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬個新基因 , 和多達5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在已經把它延伸到空氣中 , 用的是sloan基金會的補助金 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量有多少病毒和細菌 , 每天都在呼吸 , 特別是在飛機上或封閉的演講廳 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的儀器過濾過濾 ; 我們從每天在紐約市的一棟建築上 , 收集十億微生物的數量 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們正處於目前的定序的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就資料收集方面來說 , 我們穿越加拉巴哥群島的地方 , 我們發現幾乎每兩百英里 , 海裡的樣本就有驚人的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些在邏輯上是合乎邏輯的 , 就不同溫度的梯度來看 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張以溫度為基礎的衛星照片 , 紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色則是冷的 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣本和冰冷的水樣本有很大的不同 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令人驚訝的事情是這些光感應器偵測不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列預測這些波長 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些變化從地區到地區的變化極大 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外 , 在深海中 , 大部分是藍色的 , 感光受體往往會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有大量的葉綠素時 , 它們看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們變化更大 , 可能更趨向紅外線和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估我們的基因如何進行自我複製 , 我們把所有的資料組合起來 , 包括我們目前在探險中所有的資料 , 佔據了地球上所有基因資料的一半以上 , 包含了大約兩億九千萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些基因放入基因族群中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們發現了已知族群的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的族群 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因族群 , 但是我們在環境中所採取的每一個新樣本 , 都會在這些新族群中增加一個線性的族群 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	我們正處於基礎基因的初期階段 , 在這個星球上組成和生命的階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們觀察所謂的進化樹 , 我們在右上角和動物相處 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	大約有2億9千萬個基因 , 我們的基因組只有24 , 000個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物的基因組合在一起 , 我們可能只有三萬個左右 , 也許只有十幾萬個基因族群 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認爲這些基因現在不僅是進化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	以基因為中心的觀點 , 或許可以回溯到理查•道金斯的觀點 , 而不是以基因為中心的觀點 , 這種觀點不同於這些基因組成的成分 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna的能力 , 合成dna的能力 , 在過去的十到二十年間 , 已經有了和dna定序的速度一樣的改變 , 而且變得非常非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組學 , 當時我們在1995年完成了第二個基因組定序 , 這是從麥可柏斯的生殖器得到的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們穿著非常好的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 再加上500 , 是否有一小組基因組成最小的操作系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	於是我們開始進行轉錄病毒療法 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子只是一小部分的dna , 隨機插入基因密碼中 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果它們插入到基因中間 , 就會阻斷它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以 , 我們做了一張地圖 , 說明了所有能夠接受轉位子插入的基因 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明環境是至關重要的 , 你只能依據環境的特徵來定義一個必要或不必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智慧方法和13種相關有機物的基因組做比較 , 我們試著比較所有這些基因 , 看看它們有什麼共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們找到了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現 , 只有173個基因是共有13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一種細胞寄生蟲 , 稍微擴大一點點 , 如果我們去看核心基因組 , 大約310個左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 依據你的觀點 , 到達約300到400個基因 , 從500個最小基因到最小 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法 , 就是建立一個人工染色體 , 裡面有這些基因 , 我們必須在以分類為基礎的時尚中做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 合成精確的大片dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	史密斯和clydehutchison , 我的同事開發了一種令人振奮的新方法 , 讓我們在兩週的時間內合成一個5000個鹼基對的病毒 , 精確到100% , 以其序列和生物學的角度來說 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個很令人振奮的實驗當我們把合成的dna注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始製造病毒粒子反過來然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這並不是最早的合成病毒--一個小兒麻痺病毒--在一年前就被製造出來了 , 但它只是一個十分之一的活性病毒 , 花了三年的時間才完成 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix-174的結構的漫畫 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體現在打造自己的硬體的例子 , 這就是我們對生物學的看法 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上就開始關心生物戰的議題 , 而我最近在參議院委員會前發表了證詞 , 也是美國政府設立的專門委員會來檢視這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 把現實留在心中 , 是很重要的 , 對人的想像力會有什麼影響 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 現今任何已經被定序過的病毒 , 都有可能被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們會立刻對伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚恐 , 但這個有機生物的dna沒有傳染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做了天花的基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正令人擔憂的是安全部門有設計師的病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 才有重大的努力 , 試圖創造生物戰火的代理 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那項研究真的停滯不前 , 將來 , 對於製造設計師病毒的知識 , 應該沒有任何活動 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為在兩年內 , 單細胞生物是可能的 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	那些我們擁有的 , 可能在十年內就有可能做到的 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以現在我們正在做數十種不同的建構 , 因為我們可以改變人造染色體的種類和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 如何把其他的全部都放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些片段開始 , 然後有一個同源重組的重組系統 , 可以將這些片段重新組合到染色體中 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這源自於一種有機體、耐輻射奇異球菌 , 足足有三百萬個輻射 , 沒有被殺 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在這個放射線爆炸之後 , 它會在12到24小時內重新組合它的基因組 , 在它的染色體被完全爆炸之後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這個有機體在地球上無所不在 , 可能因為我們在外太空旅行而存在 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是半個玻璃杯 , 經過約五十萬拉德輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始裂裂開 , 微生物坐在底部 , 變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這裡有一張實際的照片上面的圖片顯示了一百七十萬拉德輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體完全被炸掉了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動重新組合起來 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	令人驚訝的是 , 這些生物能夠做到這一點 , 我們可能有成千上萬 , 在地球上有能力做到這一點的物種 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以 , 我們認為合成細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了理解生物學的基礎 , 更希望是環境和社會問題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們做過的第三個有機體中 , janacuschii的甲烷酸鹽水中生存的甲烷酸鹽水溫 ; 它的能量來源是氫氣 , 它所吸收的二氧化碳來自於環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 成千上萬種不同的生物 , 活在二氧化碳上 , 還能捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其從石油中取得碳來進行合成過程 , 我們有機會利用碳來捕捉它 , 將它從大氣中捕捉回來 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物 , 住在一氧化碳中 , 我們把水分解成低能量來產生氫氣和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有許多路徑 , 可以改造甲烷的新陳代謝 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦特有個重大的計畫 , 用挪威的油來捕捉和轉換從瓦斯場轉變成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短時間內 , 我認為將來會有一個新的領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因複製和同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 每天可以製造一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 正如所有生物學一樣 , 通過篩選 , 不論你在篩選氫化、化學生產 , 或純粹可行 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因的角色 , 將在可觸及的範圍內扮演好處 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用從陽光直接產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節的 , 我們認為有一種氧氣敏感的氫氣會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也結合了纖維素 , 將複雜糖分解成單醣和發酵的酵素在同一個細胞中 , 用來生產乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	使用微生物的製藥生產已經在主要實驗室裡進行了 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物的化學成分 , 比我們最好的化學家所能生產的還要複雜許多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的來源 , 希望是能源、環境修復的來源 , 也許可以取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用道德和政策的研究來結束今天的演講
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	在1999年我們延遲了實驗的開始直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查我們是否應該試著製造一個人工物種
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這真的是一項很奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖都在用他們的教義作為法律 , 他們無法在禁止製造生命的條件下找到任何教材 , 所以一定是沒事的 。 唯一會讓人擔憂的 , 是生物戰的方面 , 但給了我們預先做這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在sloan基金會已經在這個項目上提供了一份多機構的研究 , 來研究對社會有哪些風險和益處 , 以及像我自己的科學團隊所做的科學研究 , 在這個領域中 , 我們正試著建立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們可以設計東西來產生潔淨能源 , 也許革命開發中國家可以做些什麼 , 並提供各種簡單的處理方式 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普辛巴多說 , 快樂和成功深根在我們大部份人不認同的特質上:我們朝向過去、現在和未來邁進的方式 。 他建議我們調整時間的方向 , 作為改善我們的生活的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理、心理學、科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利普辛巴多開了個健康的開場 , 時間很長 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和各位分享一些關於時間的秘密的概念 , 很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好 , 開始計時 。 三十秒後 , 工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	請保持安靜 , 安定下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間到了 , 結束序列 , 開始 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10 , 9 , 8 , 7 , 6 , 5 , 4 , 3 , 2...
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利普辛巴多:咱們調一下亞當的誘惑對談 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 , 亞當 , 不要這麼想 , 去咬一口 。 」 「 我有 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 , 不要放棄夏娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹上麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好 , 一口 。 搞什麼鬼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生充滿誘惑 。 重點在於培養、抗拒 , 沒錯 , 沒錯 , 過後 , 衝動、反思、現在的焦點 , 和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的美德會勝出當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	十幾歲的女孩 , 她們承諾要在性愛上的異性戀和貞操 , 直到婚姻──謝謝你布希──大多數 , 百分之六十 , 一年內都受到性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分的人都沒有使用節育控制權 。
so much for promises .	對承諾有好多好處 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在我們來試試四歲小孩 , 給他們一份協定 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在有一顆棉花糖了 , 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們就會有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 它的價格會被用來等待 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子誘惑會發生的事 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等 , 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	牠們會抗拒誘惑 , 牠們會延遲誘惑
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特•米歇爾 , 我在史丹佛大學的同事 , 14年後回到史丹佛 , 試圖找出這些孩子有什麼不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	反抗的孩子與反抗的孩子在很多方面都有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些反抗的孩子在sat成績上有高達250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這是很大的 。 這就像一整套不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有得到那麼多麻煩 , 他們是好學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們很自信且堅定 。 而今天對我來說 , 對你來說 , 關鍵在於 , 他們是未來的焦點 , 而非現在的焦點 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 什麼是時間觀點 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	看待時間是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 將你人類在時間區或時間分類的經驗分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	並且在自動和無意識的情況下進行 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	它們在文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育水平之間有所不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是他們會變得有偏見 , 因為你學會了過度使用 , 忽略其他的 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做一個決定 , 決定你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只關注當下的情況 , 其他人在做什麼 , 和你的感受 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而這些人 , 當他們以那種形式做決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現實主義 」 , 因為他們現在的重點就是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在並不重要 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是說: 「 我過去經歷過的這種情況是什麼 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決策是建立在過去的記憶之上 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們稱這些人為 " 懷舊主義 " , 因為他們專注於所謂的 " 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的注意力總是在於預測後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們稱他們為 " 理想主義 " 。 他們關注的是未來 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想要說的是 , 時間觀點的悖論 , 會影響你所做的每一個決定 , 你完全沒有意識到 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有一種偏頗的時光觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實 , 總共有六種 。 有兩種方式可以當作既有的 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式被貼上 , 有兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面 , 或者說是負面的 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	可以是 " 享受主義者 " , 也就是說你專注於享受生活的樂趣 , 或者說 " 宿命論者 " --這不重要 , 你的生命受到控制 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是理想的 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你也可以是超然的未來:即 , 生命從死後開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維的靈活性 , 來轉換視角度 , 取決於情境的需求 , 這是你必須學習的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	很快地 , 最佳時光檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	過往正面的高度 , 過度高的未來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	以現代主義來進行調節 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於過去的負面和現代主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的節奏混合是從過去得到的 , 讓你的家人、身份、自我連結在一起 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	從未來 , 你從翅膀到翱翔到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	從現在的享樂主義得到的能量 , 是探索自己、地方、人、感性的能量 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	在過度觀點的任何時間觀點 , 都比正面觀點更加負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來要犧牲什麼才能成功 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲了家庭時間 , 犧牲了朋友的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲了有趣的時光 , 犧牲了個人的沉默
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了嗜好 , 他們犧牲了睡眠 。 這會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們為工作、成就和控制而生 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信這會和一些ted成員產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我產生共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯的貧窮家庭長大 , 一個西西里亞家庭 , 過去和現在都住在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來到這裡是一個將來由未來引導的人 , 走上頂端的人 , 他們犧牲了這些犧牲 , 因為老師們介入了 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你在等待你拿到兩顆球 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加入了現代主義 , 我也加入了過去式正面態度的關注 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只想說 , 我們把這個方法應用在許多世界問題上:改變輟學比率、對毒品成癮、增強青少年健康、對付退伍軍人的創傷──用時間隱喻來治療退伍軍人的創傷──促進永續性和保育 , 降低身體康復率 , 降低50%的輟學率 , 改變自殺式恐怖份子、改變家人的觀念 , 來達到衝突的目的地 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以 , 最後我想說的是:許多生命的謎題都能被解決 , 透過了解你的時間觀點和他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果是很深刻的 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	今天的新聞標題有多少人在一百年後才有意義 ? 一百年後 ? 有多少人 ? 克雷克•凱森的《長新聞》專案計畫現在不但很重要 , 還會有數十年的共共鳴 。 在2010年 , 他強調了近期的新聞標題 , 有可能會影響到我們未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkkcitron:現在 , 真正的新聞 。
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞裡 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社 , 每年就有三百五十萬則新聞報導出來 。
that's just one source .	這只是一個源頭 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:這些故事中有多少在長期來說是重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是 「 長期新聞 」 的概念 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是個由現在已久的基金會所完成的專案 , 由tedsters所創立 , 包括kevinkelly和stewartbrand 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的新聞報導 , 可能還牽涉到五十或十萬年前或一萬年之後 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過篩選器看新聞時 , 很多的消息會落在一邊 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	拿去年a.p的頭條新聞來說這在十年內是很重要的嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後是很重要的嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那很酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但去年的頭條是經濟 , 我敢打賭 , 遲早 , 這次的經濟衰退將會是老舊的新聞 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 哪種故事能為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 咱們來談談科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血流 , 去修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是一隻老鼠 , 就已經有一天了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近有些故事:奈米蜜蜂用真蜜蜂的毒液吸引腫瘤 ; 它們會把基因送到大腦 ; 一個可以在人體上爬行的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何養活90億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	今日 , 我們面臨60億人的困境 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人處於飢餓狀態 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國在沒有基因改造作物的情況下也會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	很幸運地 , 比爾蓋茲已經投入了十億在農業研究上 。
what about global politics ?	那麼全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界會變得截然不同 , 如果中國設立了議程 , 且可能會發生 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超過美國 , 作為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超過德國是最大的出口國 , 他們開始對孩子們做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們在尋找各種方法來把我們所知道的限制拉回來 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近的一些發現:現在阿根廷有一隻正在散播到每個大陸的螞蟻蟻蟻群 , 但南極 ; 有個自導導導的機器人科學家很快就發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 可能就不再需要我們了 ; 微生物在十二萬年前就開始出現了 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎沒有我們 , 生命就會延續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但去年 , 我挑選了長期新聞報導的最新故事是這個:水在月球上被發現 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	把一個殖民地放到上面 , 變得更容易 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果nasa不做 , 中國可能會 , 或在座的各位 , 可能會寫一張很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞報導比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡洛琳•帕爾科的影像顯示卡西尼航行到土星 , 聚焦在它最大的衛星泰坦星上 , 及在冷凍的土衛二上 , 似乎拍攝冰噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 太空 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡洛琳皮爾科向我們飛到土星 ,
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	接下來的18分鐘 , 我要帶各位踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這段旅程 , 你和我已經多年了 , 五十年前 , 人類第一次踏出我們的地球時 , 開始了 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不只真的登上了月球 , 我們還把機械太空船和所有八個行星分佈在各個行星上 , 我們著陸在小行星上 , 我們有了彗星 , 此時此刻 , 我們有一艘太空船正在運行 , 運送到冥王星的路上 , 前所知的星球 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械裝置的使命 , 都屬於更大的人類旅程:一趟旅程 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 去了解我們的起源 , 了解我們的起源 , 了解我們的星球 , 以及我們的星球 , 我們的生活 , 逐漸成形 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系裡所有我們可能去過的地方 , 尋找問題的答案 , 像是土星 。 我們曾到過土星 , 在八〇年代早期我們造訪過土星 , 但我們對土星的研究變得更加深入 , 自卡西尼號太空船在太空中穿梭於七年的星際太空船 , 在2004年的夏天時 , 已被送到土星上 , 此時此時此時此刻 , 已成為人類史上最前所未有的機械裝置 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是個很豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘的、科學的洞見 , 並且顯然超越了比較之外的光彩 , 而這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙範圍 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究光環 , 我們就能夠學到很多關於星星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一張美麗的照片 , 這是我們最接近的 , 最大型的銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	這裡有個美麗的旋風星系由哈伯太空望遠鏡拍攝
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以返回土星的旅程 , 其實是其中的一部分 , 也是人類更大的旅程的比喻 , 來了解我們身邊的事物之間的關聯性 , 以及人類如何融入這張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	讓我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位 , 我們在卡西尼學過的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向各位展示我們在過去兩年半中拍攝的所有美麗的照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我要把重點放在這次大型探險之旅中最令人振奮的兩個故事中 , 我們在土星周圍執行的兩年 , 過去兩年來 , 一直到現在為止 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	陪伴土星 , 由一大群多樣化的衛星所組成 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小範圍從幾公里到美國的大小 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍攝的土星大部份美麗的照片 , 事實上 , 土星和它的一些衛星的衛星相伴 。 這是土星和土星的衛星 , 顯示它們的直徑 , 月亮與土衛二相同 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	今日 , 土星47顆衛星有兩顆是起義的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛二和土衛二的衛星 , 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼號到達之前 , 是目前我們在太陽系中最大的未被探索的單一地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它是一個擁有長久以來觀看這些星球的人們的身體 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大、很厚的大氣 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像是我們在地球上所處的環境 , 至少在過去 , 比起在太陽系裡其它的身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層大多是分子氮 , 如你在這個房間裡呼吸的分子 , 只不過它的大氣中有簡單有機物質如甲烷、丙烷和乙烷等 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	而這些分子在泰坦的大氣層高高溫下分解 , 它們的產品結合在一起形成迷霧的粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這個迷宮無所不在 , 完全是全球化和開發的鐵達尼 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你不能用肉眼看到表面 , 眼睛在可見的區域中 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀顆粒在我們抵達卡西尼號之前 , 數十億年來 , 溫柔地飄到水面上 , 覆蓋在厚實的有機物的表面上 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	像這樣 , 泰坦也一樣 , 焦油 , 油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這就是我們所猜測的 。 這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以是土衛六表面溫度的液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是要跟土衛六一樣多的水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是冷凝的 , 所以 , 認識到這種情況為前面的世界帶來了一個怪異的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在這些雲之上有數百公里長的霧氣 , 阻止任何陽光照射到地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管那寒冷 , 你還是可以讓降雨掉到泰坦的表面 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	降雨在地球上所做的事:它雕刻了幾座河流和白內障 ; 它可以創造峽谷 ; 大盆地和隕石坑 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以在高山峰和高山丘上沖洗到低地 , 停下來想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試想土衛六的表面會長什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	一片黑暗 , 泰坦的中午 , 和地球上深處的黑暗一樣 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	天氣很冷 , 天氣很差 , 天氣很差 , 可能在下雨 , 你可能會站在密西根湖的密西根湖邊緣 , 用油漆很薄 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在卡西尼號抵達卡西尼號之前的景象 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在泰坦身上發現的景象 , 儘管它不一樣 , 和這個故事很迷人的景象一樣 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像卡西尼號一樣 , 一直以來 , 像一個朱爾•凡爾納的冒險故事成真了 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有很厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是土衛二的照片 , 由太陽光照射 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個衛星--我甚至不知道它是哪個 。 它是一個非常廣泛的大氣 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有儀器 , 可以透過大氣看到地表 , 我的相機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了這張照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你所看到的是明亮、黑暗的區域 , 且那正是我們所能達到的程度 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在太神秘了:我們無法弄清楚我們在泰坦看到的 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細看這個區域 , 你會開始看到一些圓形的管道 , 例如那些我們不知道的管道 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	後來我們發現 , 事實上 , 一個隕石坑 , 但在土衛六表面 , 很少有隕石坑 , 意思就是 , 土衛六的表面非常年輕 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來像個地形 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來像是已經被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在星球上看到任何線性的東西 , 那就意味著 , 有一個分裂 , 像一個斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它在地理上已經被改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道的六個月後 , 許多人都認為卡西尼探究了泰坦的高光 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	這就是惠更斯號探測器的部署 , 歐洲製造的huygensi號探測器 , 橫跨太陽系的七年 。 我們將它發射到泰坦的大氣中 , 要花兩個半小時才下降 , 還要在地表上著陸 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這是多麼重要的一件事
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是個人類製造的裝置 , 登陸在人類歷史上第一次 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	非常重要的是 , 在我心中 , 這是一場活動 , 值得慶祝 , 在美國和歐洲各個城市中 , 不幸的是 , 在美國和歐洲各個城市中 , 都應該要慶祝這個活動 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是個重要的原因 。 這是個國際性的使命 , 這個活動在歐洲、德國、以及慶祝的報導都出現在英語的口音、美國口音、德語、法語、義大利和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是個動人的示範 , 展示了 " 聯合國 " 的字眼 , 意思是:一個國家的真實聯合國 , 參與了一場為好的巨大努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 探索一個星球是非常重要的 , 為了了解一個星球系統 , 人類歷史上所有的星球都無法修復 , 而現在 , 人類已經觸動了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我只談起雞皮疙瘩 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極度情緒化的事件 , 而這也是我個人永遠不會忘記的事 , 你也不該忘記 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	儘管如此 , 探測器在往下一路測量大氣 , 同時也拍攝了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 看見泰坦表面的第一張照片是什麼樣子 。 這是我們看到的景象 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這實在很震驚 , 因為那是我們希望其他的照片從軌道上拍下來的 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	這是個不明確的模式 , 地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	這種樹突狀的排水模式只能由液體的流動形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以沿著這些管道 , 看出它們如何匯合 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們聚集在這裡的通道 , 滲透到這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像是一條海岸線
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在八公里拍攝的 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--大約是一架飛機高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機橫越美國 , 你會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這是你在鐵達尼亞航空公司飛越土衛六的照片 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器終於在表面上休息了 , 我將向你們展示 , 各位先生女士 , 這是第一次從外太陽系的衛星表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水冰鵝卵石 , 對嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在其中一個平坦的黑色區域 , 並且它沒有沉沒在視線中 。 所以我們著陸的不是液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器最後落入的基本上就是一片泥巴的泰坦 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一片無情的土地 , 充滿了液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	很可能這種材料已經透過我們看到的這些通道沖掉了泰坦高地 , 數十億年來 , 流失在低窪的盆地上 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 仍然沒有任何跡象出現在我們的影像中 , 甚至在huygens的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體都沒有 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 更讓人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們的電影 , 地下赤道的區域 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘是一百公尺高 , 以幾公里的高度偏離 , 再往上一英里 , 一英里 , 一英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	幾百英里高達一千或一千兩百英里的沙丘 。
