this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是泰坦的撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	這顯然是個非常乾燥的地方 , 不然就不會有沙丘了 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	再一次 , 令人困惑的是 , 沒有液體 , 直到終於 , 我們在極地看到湖 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在南極極地帶有一片湖在泰坦的南極區域 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大小相當於安大略湖的大小 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 就在一個禮拜前 , 我們飛越泰坦的北極 , 再一次發現 , 我們發現一個和卡斯匹亞海一樣大的特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎是液體 , 基於某些原因我們不了解 , 至少在這個季節 , 很明顯地 , 在泰坦的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你應該認同我們發現泰坦是個很了不起、神秘的地方 。 它很奇怪 , 很像外星人 , 有著類似的地球形態 , 有著很驚人的地理形態和多樣性的地理環境 , 而這個迷人的世界 , 在太陽系中只靠太陽能和地球的豐富度來源 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們繼續到土衛二 。 土衛二是一個小型的衛星 , 土衛六的大小約十分之一 。 你可以看到它在英國旁邊 , 向你展示它的大小 。 這不代表威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二非常白 , 非常亮 , 它的表面顯然是破碎的 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是一個地質上非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現大多在南極的發現 , 我們正在研究南極點 , 發現了這些碎形的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 因為它們是不同的成分 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被覆蓋著 。 這些碎片覆蓋著有機物質 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個南極區域的溫度上升了 , 溫度上升了 , 整個地球上最熱的地方 , 在身體上 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就好奇怪了 , 發現地球上的南極比熱帶地區還熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 當我們拍了更多照片 , 我們發現從這些裂痕中 , 正噴射出細微的冰粒 , 噴射到宇宙中數百英里外 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們用顏色來分析這個影像 , 來提取微弱的光線 , 我們看到這些噴流實際上是以數千英里的高度在土衛二上方的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊對這樣的圖片進行了研究 , 像這張 , 想了一下卡西尼號的其他成果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是 , 這些噴流可能是從土衛二地表下的液態水的口袋噴發出來的 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們可能有液態水、有機物質、過熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們有可能碰到現代行星探索的聖杯 , 或者說 , 一個可能適合生物生存的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系中其它地方生命的發現 , 不論在土衛二或其它地方 , 都會有很大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能夠證明 , 基因的產生不止一次 , 而是在我們的太陽系裡 , 兩次 , 獨立 , 那就表示 , 宇宙中有十七億年出現了驚人的數量 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球仍是我們所知的唯一星球 , 充滿了生命 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 它仍然是如此 , 到目前為止 , 我們唯一知道的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果在座有任何人在1960年代的時候有一名警察和一致 , 我們會原諒你 , 如果你不是 , 好 , 你會記得1968年阿波羅八號太空人所拍攝的這張非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次 , 地球從太空中被拍攝出來 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置產生了巨大的衝擊 , 我們對於保護地球的責任感也產生了巨大的衝擊 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼號拍下的第一張相片 , 是前所未見的 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是日全食從土星的另一端看到的 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張無與倫比的照片裡 , 你看到背光被太陽照射的主圈 , 你看到太陽折射出來的景象 , 看到這個光環 , 由土衛二的耗損所產生 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這還不夠精彩 , 我們能在這個美麗的圖像中看到我們自己的星球 , 在土星的光環中行進 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	對於從遠處看我們自己 , 有種深入的動人 , 深入了解到我們在其他星球上看得到的 , 藍色的地球 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	我們從中得到的看法 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這次的發現之旅中得到最好的獎賞 , 始於半個世紀之前 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	截至2005年 , 僅有15%的地球被繪製成地圖 。 這是在災難後 , 援助減緩了 , 隱藏了未被使用的土地和未知道路的經濟潛力 。 在演講中 , 谷歌的lalitechkatradasdemos繪製了全球各地的人所使用的地圖工具 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作 , 設計 , 地圖 , 科技 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	已故的katragada:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	在2008年 , 塞隆納基斯摧毀了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人受到極大的幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人趕出去 , 提供給當地的人 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有顯示醫院的地圖 , 沒有辦法幫助受害者接觸的地圖 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信在2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人被繪製在可數位化的細節上 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國也陷入了世界上大部分人口人口大臉孔的問題:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 救助也來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 有四十個志願者使用一個新軟體來繪製十二萬公里的道路 , 三千間醫院、物流和救災點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體呢 ? googlemapmaker.
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一項科技 , 讓我們能夠在地圖上繪製出我們熟知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這套軟體繪製了從道路到河流、學校到當地企業的地圖 , 到街角的商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名人赫爾南多•德•索托認爲開發中國家的經濟利益關鍵在於利用大量無限量的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 光在印度 , 一兆美元的房地產仍然是不成文的 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	僅在去年170個國家 , 成千上萬的使用者就已繪製出數百萬個細節的地圖 , 前所未見的細節地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這樣做是有可能的 , 因為到處都有熱情的使用者 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	讓我們來看看現在使用者所製作的一些地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 在我們的演說中 , 在這170個國家中 , 人們在繪製這個世界的地圖 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑 , 剛在塞內加爾繪製了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	再靠近一點 , 瓦拉 , 一個在班加羅爾的n.g.道路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何、手勢識別 , 和機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個使用者 , 一次編輯一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是個邀請 , 邀請我們70%未開發的星球 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落布德鲁斯村在一個月長達十個月的非暴力抗爭中停止一個障礙橫跨他們的橄欖樹林你聽到了嗎 ? 不這麼想巴西的電影製片人朱利亞•巴查查查納問我們為什麼只在以色列的衝突中留意暴力 , 而非暴力的領導者卻沒有權利 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情心、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:請注意非暴力手段 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	在過去八年間 , 我致力於記錄以色列和巴勒斯坦試圖用和平的方式結束衝突的人們 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國各地旅行時 , 總是有一個問題:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人沒有使用非暴力抗爭的抗爭呢 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我所面臨的挑戰是 , 通常我才剛從中東回來 , 那時我花了很多時間拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力的方式來保護他們的土地和水資源 , 不受以色列士兵和移民者的傷害 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人正在嘗試推動一個巨大的全國性非暴力運動 , 終結該地區的佔領 , 建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 在座大部分人可能從未聽說過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分裂發生在地上和國外發生的事情之間的差異 , 正是其中一個原因 , 也是為什麼我們還沒有一個巴勒斯坦和平的抵抗運動成功的原因 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我在這裡要談關注的力量 , 關注的力量 , 以及在西岸、加薩和其他地方 , 非暴力運動的出現和發展 , 今天我要談的是關於關注的力量 , 關於你們關注的力量 , 以及你們關注的力量 , 以及在西岸、加薩和其他地方的非暴力運動的發展 , 和發展 , 但今天 , 我的個案研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 要培養非暴力手段 , 最缺少的就是不要讓巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是要讓我們開始注意那些已經有暴力的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我帶各位了解一下這個點 , 藉由這個叫做布德鲁斯村的村子 , 來說明這個點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈要建立一個隔離屏障 , 其中的一部份會在村落的上方建起 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去百分之四十的土地 , 被包圍著 , 這樣他們就無法取得西岸其餘的銀行 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導力 , 他們發動了和平抗爭的運動 , 來阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些簡短的片段 , 你們可以體會一下在地上長什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們聽說牆壁將與以色列分開巴勒斯坦
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村 , 我們發現牆壁會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人:那道牆壁確實創造了恐怖的解方 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男人:今天你被邀請去一個和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	加入了數十位以色列兄弟姐妹 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列積極份子:軍隊最怕的就是非暴力抗爭 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女人:我們看到那些男人試著推開士兵 , 但沒有一個男人能這麼做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為這些女孩可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須清空傳統思想的心態 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們是完全和諧的 , 我們想要將它散播到所有巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	聊天:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯 , 及流行的前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主持人:這道牆上的衝突持續著 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被送去散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男人:這些就是現場的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像失落的jah , 到處射擊 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列積極份子:我確信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我周圍有一些人甚至不敢說出話來 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭不會停止這場戰爭 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是一場和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	聊天:我們做得到 ! 我們做得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴哈:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很驚訝 , 國際媒體在七年前就沒有報導這一連串驚人的事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民們 , 經過十個月的和平抗爭 , 說服了以色列政府將牆壁的路線從他們的土地移開 , 移到綠線上 , 國際上認可以色列和巴勒斯坦領土間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭從此散播到西岸的村落 , 再到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然對這些故事保持沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會帶來很深刻的影響 , 影響到非暴力可能會成長的可能性 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦生存的可能性 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭都有一個非常重要的共通點 , 它們都是劇場的一種形式 , 尋求觀眾的目標 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一不斷得到封面 , 吸引巴勒斯坦問題的國際性團體 , 那就很難讓非暴力的領導人轉向他們的社區 , 即公民不服從是個可行的選項 , 要解決他們的困境 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	關注的力量可能對在場的父母親一點都不驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓孩子更吵得更大聲的特技 , 肯定的是 , 第一次給予他關注 , 讓他放下一片水果 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	誘惑會變成童年心理學家所說的功能性行為 , 因為孩子已經知道他可以從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以透過給予或消除孩童注意力來激勵或抑制行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可能受到影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇聚焦於關注的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在終結中東的衝突的核心 , 並為我們帶來和平的核心 , 就是要將非暴力抗爭轉化為一種功能性行為 , 做法就是讓更多人關注在現今的非暴力領導者身上 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝我的電影的過程中 , 在西岸的村落、加薩、東耶路撒冷的村落 , 我見識到 , 連一部紀錄片都能影響改造 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做瓦拉杰的村落裡 , 座落在非常接近耶路撒冷的村落裡 , 社區正面臨著和布德魯斯非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們將被包圍 , 失去許多土地 , 失去許多土地 , 無法取得任何自由 , 無論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 他們一直在使用非暴力手段 , 但他們一直在使用非暴力手段 , 因為沒有人在注意 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們安排了一個螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們舉行了目前為止最完善、最有紀律的示範 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德鲁斯村的故事 , 被記錄在電影裡 , 覺得他們確實有跟隨他們在做的事 , 有人在乎他們在乎的事 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列的角度 , 有一種新的和平運動叫做索里達爾特 , 在希伯來語中代表團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領袖一直在用布德鲁斯村當作他們的主要招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說 , 以色列從未有過活躍過 , 看過電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰和索里德的暴動案例顯示即使只是一部小小的預算獨立電影也能在將非暴力轉化為功能性行為的情況下扮演一個角色 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 如果大媒體開始報導每週在村落中發生的非暴力示威 , 例如比爾賓、尼尼林、瓦拉杰 , 在耶路撒冷的社區 , 像希克拉和西爾瓦 , 非暴力領袖在工作中變得更加明顯、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信 , 最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不把注意力放在這些努力上 , 它們是看不見的 , 就好像它們從未發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我首先看到 , 如果我們這樣做 , 它們就會相乘 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們相乘 , 他們的影響會在以色列巴勒斯坦總體的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力正是那種能夠解開局面的影響力 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明了非暴力組織在布德鲁斯村等地區是行得通的 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們集中注意力 , 讓他們到處證明它是行得通的 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙奈克有個簡單但強大的模式 , 可以鼓舞人心的領導 , 全都以金色圓圈開始 , 問題是:為什麼 ? 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德•金 , 還有萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullsey , 企業家 , 企業家 , 領導力 , 銷售 , 成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙娜克:偉大的領袖如何啟發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你怎麼解釋當事情不如預設的樣子 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者更好的是 , 你如何解釋當其他人能夠達成似乎違反所有假設的事物時 , 你要如何解釋 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果這麼創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比他們所有的競爭對手都更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	但 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	它們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們也能接觸到同樣的人才、同樣的機構、同樣的顧問、同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那麼 , 為什麼它們似乎有些不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德金主導了民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受到驅逐前驅權的人 , 他肯定不是當時唯一的偉大演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出控制權、駕駛人飛機的原因 , 尤其是有其他團隊更有資格、更好的資金 。
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有實現動力的飛行 , 萊特兄弟也打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他的玩法 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我有了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作的看法 , 甚至深深地改變了我對它的運作方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有的偉大、鼓舞人心的領導者和組織 , 不論是蘋果、馬丁路德金恩、或是他們所有人認為的萊特兄弟 , 行為和溝通方式 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	它完全和其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的 , 就是將它編碼 , 可能是世界上最簡單的點子 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導者能夠激發出其他人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每一個人 , 地球上每一個組織都知道自己在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道如何做 , 不論你稱它為你有著不同的價值主張、你的屬性過程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少很少人或機構知道為何他們會做自己做的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	我所謂的 「 為什麼 」 並不是 「 創造利潤 」 的意思 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 , 永遠是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	我所謂的 「 為什麼 」 指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的起因是什麼 ? 你的信仰是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	你為什麼早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	嗯 , 結果 , 我們思考的方式、行為的方式、我們溝通的方式 , 都來自外在 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 。 我們從最清楚的轉變到最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但受到啟發的領導者和受到啟發的組織 , 不論他們的規模大小 , 不論他們的產業全都在思考 , 從內而外的行動和溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我使用蘋果 , 因為它很容易理解 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果和其他人一樣 , 蘋果的行銷訊息可能會像這樣: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用 , 很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? 』
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是大部份行銷的做法 , 大部份銷售的做法 , 大部份人和人之間的溝通方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們會說 , 我們的做法 , 我們會說 , 我們的做法不同 , 或說我們比較好 , 我們會期待某種行為、購買行為、投票 , 諸如此類 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律事務所:我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是為和我們一起做生意的客戶做表演 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很棒的氣體哩程數 , 有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果的溝通方式如下 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現況的方式是把我們的產品設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用和使用者 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好製造出很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同的對吧 ? 你們準備好從我身上買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它告訴我們 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每一位都對購買蘋果電腦感到非常舒服 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常舒適地從蘋果電腦買下mp3播放器 , 或蘋果電腦的手機 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如我之前所說 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能將他們與其競爭者的競爭者區別開來 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭對手都同樣有能力做出這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 閘道推出了平面電視螢幕 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很有資格做平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們已經做平面螢幕好幾年了 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾來自mp3播放器和pdas , 他們製造了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完全設計良好的產品 , 沒有人買的 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從戴爾維爾買一台mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	你為什麼要從電腦公司買一台mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這樣做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和你所需要的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的是:我告訴你們的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	全都以生物學的原理為基礎
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看看人腦的十字路口從上往下看 , 你看到的是人腦實際上分裂成三個主要元素 , 完美地與金色圓圈完美地相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 對應到 「 什麼 」 的層次 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮質層負責我們所有的理性、分析的想法和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部份構成我們的邊緣腦 , 而我們的邊緣腦負責我們所有的感受 , 例如信任和忠誠度 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它同時也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 而且它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外在溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特色、好處、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	只是它不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內在溝通時 , 我們就直接和控制行為的大腦對話 , 然後我們讓人們去理化它 , 用我們所說和做的事情來合理化它 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是腸子決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	有時 , 你可以給人所有的事實和數據 , 他們會說: 「 我知道這些事實和細節說了什麼 , 但感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	我們為什麼要用這個動詞 , 卻沒有 「 感覺 」 呢 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的大腦並不控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最多能忍受的就是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者 , 有時你說你在帶著你的心 , 或者你在帶著你的靈魂領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我很不想打破它 , 那些不是身體其他部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的大腦邊緣 , 控制決策 , 而非語言的部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你要做你所做的事 , 人們會回應為什麼你要做你該做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們為你投票 , 或從你身上買點東西 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 忠誠的 , 想要成為你所做的一部份 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再一次 , 目標不只是要賣給需要你所擁有的人 , 目標是要賣給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要雇用需要工作的人 , 而是要雇用那些相信你所相信的事的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你雇用員工 , 只因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為了你的錢而工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的人們 , 他們會用血、汗和淚水幫你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有比萊特兄弟更好的例子了 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分人不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	在20世紀早期 , 追求人類飛行的力量 , 就像當時的網路公司一樣 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierpontlangley有的 , 我們假設是成功的食譜 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我是說 , 就算是現在 , 你問人: 「 為什麼你的產品 ? 或為什麼你的公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是會給你同樣的看法 , 同樣的三件事:不受控制、不對的人、不好的市場狀況 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	永遠都是同樣的三件事 , 所以讓我們來探究一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley獲得了五萬美元的獎金 , 由戰爭部門提供 , 來找出這架飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	金錢也沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛任職 , 在史密斯尼任職 , 和當時的所有大型人物都非常相連 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的心態 , 找到了最好的心態 , 市場環境非常美妙 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑 , 每個人都在為langley加油 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼為什麼我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠在幾百英里外的俄羅斯 , 歐維爾和威爾伯萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為的成功的秘方 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們付錢給他們的夢想和他們自行車店的收入 ; 萊特兄弟的團隊沒有一個人受過大學教育 , 連歐維爾或威爾布爾都沒有 ; 紐約時報也沒有在任何地方追隨他們 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 歐維爾和威爾布爾布爾都是由一個原因所驅使 , 一個目的 , 一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信 , 如果他們能想出這架飛行機器 , 就會改變世界的軌跡 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要有錢 , 他想要成名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求財富 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	你看 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想的人 , 和他們一起工作 , 用血、汗水和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人則是為了付出而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 每當萊特兄弟出去 , 他們就得拿出五組零件 , 因為那是他們吃晚飯前的幾倍 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最終 , 在1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟起飛 , 沒有人去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後 , 我們發現了這件事 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明langley的動機是錯誤的:萊特兄弟起飛的那天 , 他辭職了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那是個驚人的發現 , 各位 , 我會改進你的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他辭掉了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談論你所相信的 , 你就會吸引那些相信你所相信的人們 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人們是很重要的 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂的創意散播法則 , 如果你不懂法律 , 你一定知道這個術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	最前面2.5%的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人是我們早期的採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是早期的大多數 , 是晚期的大多數 , 晚期的大多數和晚期的笑聲 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	人們買豆腐手機的唯一原因 , 是因為你不能再買腐爛的手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都在這個尺度上不同時間坐著 , 但創新的擴散法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或大眾市場接受一個點子 , 你不可能擁有它 , 直到你達成了15%到18%市場市場的頂點 , 再來是系統的尖端 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新企業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡跟你說: 「 喔 , 大概10%吧 。 」 很驕傲 。
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以去掉超過10%的顧客 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	只有百分之十的人 「 了解它 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這是我們如何描述它們的 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	就像那種直覺的感覺: 「 喔 , 他們就是懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到那些在你和他們做生意之前取得它的人 , 而不是那些沒有得到它的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	就是這裡 , 這個小小的差距 , 正如jeffreymoore稱之為 「 跨越隔閡 」 , 因為 , 大多數人在一開始就嘗試過它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者 , 以及早期採用者 , 他們都很自在地做出這些破壞性的決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們會比較自在地做出那些直覺的決定 , 被他們對世界的信念所驅使 , 而不只是產品能取得的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排了六個小時才買了一支iphone , 剛剛出櫃的時候 , 可以在下週走進商店買了一支架 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人一開始就花了四萬美元在平坦的螢幕上 , 儘管科技是潛在的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順帶一提 , 他們沒有這樣做是因為這項技術很棒 , 他們是為了自己而做的 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	這是因為他們想要成為第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 , 和你所做的 , 只是證明了你所相信的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	人們買iphone的原因 , 在最初的六小時內 , 排隊排了六個小時 , 是因為他們相信這個世界 , 以及他們希望每個人看到他們的方式:他們是第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你一個很有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 和一個有名的成功案例 , 關於創新的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	第一 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業性的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說的 , 第二個成功的做法是錢、對的人、對的市場環境 , 對嗎 ? 你應該要有成功的做法 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	大約八、九年前 , tivo上市時 , 至今 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 親手執行 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們的資金非常好 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場環境很美妙 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我總是把東西綁在我的垃圾時間華納的dvr上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo卻失敗了 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺過錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們到ipo時 , 他們的股票價格大約是30或40美元 , 然後價格下跌 , 從未超過10美元 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它比六個高度的交易 , 除了幾個小突起以外 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你知道 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們擁有的是什麼 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一種能暫停現場電視的產品 , 跳過商業廣告 , 重新現場電視 , 把你的觀看習慣記住 , 連問都沒有 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗的多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你在害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種想要完全掌控你生活各個層面的人 , 那麼 , 我們有一項產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停直播、跳過商業廣告、記住你的看法習慣、等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 , 而你所做的只是證明你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給各位一個成功的例子 , 關於創新的散播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 25萬人出現在華盛頓的商場上 , 聆聽金恩博士的演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有寄出任何邀請函 , 也沒有網站來查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說家
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一一個在美國遭受公民權利之前的男人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些點子很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有四處告訴人們美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處告訴人們他所相信的
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 。 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所相信的人們採取了他的理由 , 使這成為了自己的理由 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人知道答案 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	各位看 , 25 , 000人在對的日子裡 , 能夠聽到他說話的聲音 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人因此而出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己出席 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	他們相信美國讓他們在公車上旅行了八個小時 , 在八月中 , 站在華盛頓的陽光下 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人和白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種類型的法律:那些由較高權威人士所制定的法律 , 那些由人類所制定的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有人類定律的定律都和權威制定的定律一致 , 直到所有人類定律的定律都存在於一個公平的世界裡 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好公民權利運動正是幫助他生命的最佳成因 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了我一個 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	聽現在的政治人物 , 有他們全面的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有啟發任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的位置 , 但那些領導的人啟發了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們都追隨那些領導者 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 有能力啟發他們周圍的人 , 或找到鼓舞他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你要怎麼記住你車子停在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你正朝著正確的方向前進 ? 神經科學家尼爾負責研究周圍的神經機制 , 及它們如何連結到記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾•伯格斯:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在一個很大的停車場 , 我們要如何記住我們停車位的位置 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	以下是主角面臨的問題 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們將會試著去了解他的大腦到底發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 黃色標示 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有像阿茲海默症一樣的損害 , 你記不得東西 , 包括你把車子停在哪裡 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是以拉丁文命名的 「 海馬體 」 , 相似之處 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元所組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人腦內有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元藉由發送小脈衝或刺激的電流相互交流
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞組成 , 非常密切的相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 藉由記錄老鼠在覓食時的個別神經元或老鼠的覓食環境 , 記錄牠們覓食的環境 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	想像一下 , 我們從這隻老鼠海馬體內的單一個神經元記錄下來 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一小部份的電力時 , 會有一個紅點和一個點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們發現這個神經元知道當老鼠進入某個特定的環境時 , 就會知道這個神經元 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	藉由發送電刺激訊號到大腦的其他部位 , 訊號傳送到大腦的其他部位 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	我們可以把神經元的發射速度看作是動物所在位置的函數 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們記錄許多不同的神經元 , 就會發現當動物進入其周圍的不同區域時 , 不同的神經被激發 , 就像這個方形的盒子裡的一樣 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以他們一起為大腦的其餘部分建立了一張地圖 , 持續地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	癲癇患者有時會需要大腦監控的電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩過電玩遊戲 , 讓他們在小鎮附近開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬體內的位置細胞會開始活躍 , 開始發送電脈衝 , 只要他們開車經過一個特定的位置 , 就會開始發送電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 一個位置細胞怎麼知道老鼠或人在其環境中的位置呢 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界限特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	最上方的這一隻 , 喜歡在老鼠的箱子中間發射某種中間的火焰 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你把盒子放大 , 激發地點就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的這一塊會發出一道火 , 只要有一面牆 , 就會在南方靠近 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另外一面牆放進盒子裡 , 細胞就會被激發 , 不管在哪裡 , 只要有一面牆到南方 , 動物就會在盒子裡探索 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以這可以預測 , 感應你周圍的界限和邊界的距離等等 , 對海馬體來說尤其重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 輸入海馬體的細胞 , 會在海馬體中發現哪些細胞 , 會對偵測到界限或邊緣有反應 , 尤其是當老鼠在四處移動時 , 偵測到邊界或邊緣 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當這些動物靠近牆壁時 , 或沿著東邊的邊界時 , 不論是方形盒子的邊緣或圓形的邊緣 , 甚至是圓形的邊緣 , 動物就會在桌子上移動 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞在每當南方有界限時就會被激發 , 不論是在桌子或牆壁的下方 , 甚至是兩張桌子間隔開的距離 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這是一種我們認為位置細胞會決定動物在四處探索的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物體在哪裡 , 例如這個目標 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或者 , 你的車子在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 去看他們所記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們非常擅長把標誌放到他們認為旗幟或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們能改變環境的形狀和大小 , 如同我們在位置細胞上所做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個案例中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何被改變 , 就像是你如何改變環境的形狀和大小一樣 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	例如 , 你所看到的 , 如果國旗是在一個小方形的環境中 , 交叉處的位置 , 那麼如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但是你讓環境變得更大 , 他們認為國旗是從哪裡延伸出來的 , 和位置細胞被激發的位置完全相同 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你還記得國旗的所在地 , 透過儲存你所有的位置細胞的模式 , 你可以藉由四處走動 , 找到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以找到最好的位置 , 找到目前儲存的位置細胞被激發的模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	這會引導你回到你想要記得的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們的動作在哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們採取一些開放的路徑也許停下來 , 我們就會知道 , 因為我們自己的動作 , 我們可以大致上整合這條路徑 , 前進的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會得到這種路徑整合的訊號 , 來自一種細胞 , 叫做網格細胞 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞在海馬體輸入的輸入中也發現了它們有點像位置細胞
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處移動時 , 每個單獨的細胞在一系列不同的地點被激發 , 存在於一個令人驚異的三角形網格中 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你用不同的顏色來記錄這裡的數個格子細胞 , 就會有類似電網圖案 , 橫越整個環境 , 每一個細胞的網格狀會稍微改變 , 移向其他細胞 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的會在這個格子上發動 , 綠色的會在這個格子上藍色的 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	總而言之 , 這就像老鼠能夠在整個環境中穿梭一個虛擬的地點 , 有點像是地圖上找到的緯度和長距線 , 只是用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電子活動可以從其中一個細胞傳到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它所在的位置 , 這樣它就可以用它自己的動作去知道它在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	正因為所有類似激發模式的網格結構都有相同的對稱軸 , 在這裡以橘色標出的方向 , 代表所有的網格活動 , 尤其是大腦中所有網格細胞的網格活動 , 都應該要根據我們在六個方向之間運轉的位置來改變 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放到核磁共振儀裡 , 讓他們做一個像我展示給你們看的電玩遊戲 , 來尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你可以在人腦內看到它 , 就像是老鼠的網格細胞一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能想起他的車子從距離和方向來的位置延伸出建築物和界限在他停車的地方
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這是由邊界偵測細胞的發射所代表的 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從汽車公園走出的路徑 , 位在電網公園內的路線 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞被激發 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以藉由移動來找出目前在他停車位位置的位置找到最好的位置位置細胞的發射模式與目前停車位的儲存模式進行配對
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這會引導他回到那個位置 , 不考慮視覺線索 , 例如他的車子是否真的在那兒 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被吹倒了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去抓它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除了空間記憶以外 , 如果我們觀察整個大腦內的這些網狀的激發模式 , 就會在一系列的位置上看到它 , 當我們在做各種自動傳記工作時 , 像是記得上次參加婚禮時 , 記得會發生什麼事 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	可能是神經機制代表我們周圍的空間 , 也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重現空間的場景 , 至少 , 想像當我們想要想像時 , 發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果這正在發生 , 你的記憶可以從位置細胞開始藉由密度相互作用 , 藉由激活邊界細胞 , 來創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以在這個空間中移動這個視點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另外一種我還沒提到的細胞 , 頭部方向細胞 , 它們就像是指南針一樣 , 依照你所面對的方向 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你的視覺影像的方向 , 例如 , 當你在婚禮上的時候 , 可以想像你在婚禮上所發生的事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個新時代的例子 , 真的是在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理學的過程 , 例如你如何記得、想像 , 甚至想想數十億個獨立的神經元的行為 , 來決定我們的大腦 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一個全球安全機關合作的全球安全 , 由機構、政府機構、私人部門和大眾合作所驅使 。 這不僅僅是開放原始碼的粉絲 , 而是jamesstaravridis的遠景 , 北約的終極指揮官 , 他們在近期的軍隊中 , 共同對未來安全的理由 , 來解釋為什麼未來應該建造橋樑而不是牆 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放資源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史塔維迪斯:北約的最高指揮官如何看待全球安全問題 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要談的是開放原始碼的安全性 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們的安全性已經變得更好了 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	首先 , 讓我們回顧一下20世紀 , 了解一下這種安全方式對我們的安全是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 法國的戰場 , 位於北約在比利時總部的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在verdun , 1916年 , 超過300天 , 70萬人被殺 , 所以一天有2 , 000人被殺 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它向前推進20世紀的安全性到第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到斯大林格勒的戰鬥 , 300天 , 有2百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的壕溝 , 到第二次世界大戰的馬其頓路線 , 然後進入冷戰 , 鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的論點是 , 不是建造牆壁來創造安全 , 而是建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲一座有名的橋 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是沿著dina河流的橋樑 , 伊伏里克的小說主題 , 它談到如何在歐洲和巴爾幹地區 , 經過一段時間 , 歐洲和巴爾幹半島的巨大建牆壁 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在過去的十年裡 , 我們開始看到這些社區的起步 , 非常猶豫地團結在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我想再次強調 , 開放資源的安全性就是將國際的 , 跨部門的 , 私人的通訊 , 和在社交網路上的大多聯繫在一起 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物受到各種各樣的攻擊 , 沒有威脅到全球公有物的來源可以用牆壁來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	顯然 , 我是水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 排隊 , 穿過印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題嗎 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	在它的一邊 , 音樂廳有一條鋼絲 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	防止海盜攻擊海盜 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	海盜是現今在世界範圍內非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	海盜也在馬拉克的海峽非常活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它在幾內亞灣很活躍 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	這是全球運輸系統價值十億美元的損失 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 當時有20艘船 , 500名海軍陸戰隊持有人質 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何解決這個問題 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到另一種海洋 , 網路大海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	此時 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一個信用卡詐騙案 , 當中有超過一百億美元 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 是全球經濟2兆年的不連續性 。
two trillion a year .	一年有兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只不過是英國的國內生產總值 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以這個網路的大海 , 我們無止盡地知道這個網路開放是最根本的 , 在威脅之下也是如此 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	我在全球公有物中擔憂的另一件事 , 是人口販賣所造成的威脅 , 由毒品、鴉片等毒品的運動所造成的威脅 , 從阿富汗穿過歐洲到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心從andeanridge北方來的古柯鹼 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器的運輸 。 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣主要在海上移動 , 但在全球公有物的其它部分 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你 , 這是非常高科技的美國海軍裝備 , 我們用它來阻止人口販運 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是一個販毒集團的半潛水服 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是在南美叢林裡建造的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用低科技的木筏逮捕了它它 , 它帶著六噸的古柯鹼 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四人組成 , 精密的傳播溝通掃描 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種運輸 , 在人、在人、在武器 , 上帝禁止使用大規模毀滅性武器 , 是威脅全球公有物的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	讓我們在今天的阿富汗將它統一起來 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是在阿富汗的一片土地 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上百分之八十到九十的狗大便鴉片和海洛因來自阿富汗
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	當然 , 我們也看到了恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是基地組織的由來 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的暴動在那裏 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 這種恐怖主義的擔憂也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須解決的問題 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 這裡是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道二十世紀的工具行不通 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼辦 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我想說的是 , 我們不會只從槍筒的桶子裡外送安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會僅僅靠槍支的桶子來遞送安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這樣做時 , 我們必須把事情做好 , 並且很有能力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放安全是關乎國際的、跨部門的、私人的聯繫 , 由網路上的策略性溝通的概念結合在一起 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子 , 說明這如何以正面的方式運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 , 這些是阿富汗的士兵
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該要說: 「 這很奇怪 , 我想我讀到 , 在這二十、三十歲的年輕人中 , 大部分對阿富汗來說是不識字的 。 」
you would be correct .	你會是對的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	當他們進入阿富汗的安全部隊時 , 百分之八十五的人無法閱讀 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班教育的時期 , 在這些男人和女人學會閱讀的那段時期 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們在教導他們閱讀雅圖文學課程時 , 北約組織和私人機構合作 , 和開發機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教會了超過二十萬人的安全部隊以基本的水平去閱讀和寫字 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你在阿富汗讀和寫的時候 , 通常會把一支筆放在口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在典禮上 , 當這些年輕男性和女性畢業時 , 他們帶著驕傲的筆 , 放在他們的口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	全球有50個參與這項任務的國家--跨部門--這些發展機構和公共和共和國 , 來採取這類安全措施 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也教導他們對抗技能 , 但我認為 , 開放原始碼的安全性意味著 , 以創造更長久的安全性效應的方式連結在一起 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	叫做舒適感 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘姐妹船叫做慈悲 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船隻 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這個 , 舒適的狀況 , 在加勒比海和南美的海岸進行病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在一般的巡迴演出中 , 他們會做四十萬個病人的治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	船員不是嚴格地依靠軍隊 , 而是結合人道主義組織:營運希望、微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織則派來志工 。
interagency physicians come out .	內部的內部醫生出來了 。
they're all part of this .	它們都是其中的一部份 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲的小男孩 , 和他的媽媽一起走了兩天 , 來到舒適圈的眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他適合時 , 在他非常神奇的眼中 , 他突然抬頭說: 「 媽媽 , veoelmundo 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽媽 , 我看到世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	將這個技術乘以四十萬個病人的治療方法 , 私人和安全部隊的合作 , 你就會開始看到創造安全的力量 , 以截然不同的方式 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你看到的是棒球選手 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能挑出這張照片中的美國軍隊士兵嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是這兩位年輕人 , 不論是年輕男孩 , 這是一系列棒球診所的一部分 , 我們已經探索了一系列的棒球大聯盟 , 國務院 , 他們設立了外交部的部門 , 軍事棒球隊的球員 , 他們是真正的戰士 , 他們是真正有技能的戰士 , 但他們參與了這一系列的戰役 , 他們在拉丁美洲和加勒比 , 和加勒比 , 和加勒比 , 加勒比 , 加勒比 , 加勒比 , 創造了整個中美洲 , 加勒比 , 加勒比 , 加勒比 , 加勒比人和加勒比 , 加勒比 , 加勒比 , 加勒比 , 加勒比 , 加勒比 , 加勒比 , 加勒比人和加勒比人和加勒比人和加勒比人之間 , 加勒比 , 加勒比人之間 , 加勒比人之間 , 加勒比人和加勒比人之間 , 加勒比 , 加勒比人之間 , 加勒比人之間
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它顯示年輕男性與女性的角色榜樣 , 關於健身 , 以及我認為能為我們創造安全的人生 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	另一方面 , 這種合作關係的另一面是災難救援 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍直升機 , 在2004年海嘯過後 , 造成25萬人死亡 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在這些重大的災難中2004年的海嘯 , 250000人死於巴基斯坦的卡什里大地震 , 2005年 , 8萬人死亡 , 海地地地震 , 大約有30萬人死亡 , 更近期的地震混合 , 引發了日本和其核工業的衝突 , 在所有這些例子中 , 我們看到了國際介入的跨部門 , 跨部門、跨部門 , 和自然界的衝突 , 並且與自然界的衝突 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些例子都是關於開放原始碼的安全 。
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	透過這樣的方式 , 我們將它綁在一起 。
now , you're looking at this thinking , " ah , admiral , these must be sea lanes of communication , or these might be fiber optic cables . "	現在 , 你們看到的 , 是在想 , 「 啊 , 邁德 , 這些肯定是溝通的航線 , 或這些可能是光纖電纜 。 」
no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 , 這是twitter的圖表
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特 。 綠色是地理分配 。
white is the synthesis .	白色是合成 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	這是個完美的例子 , 關於大眾調查 , 世界上六大國 , 以下六大國家 , 依序排行:中國、印度、臉書、美國、推特 , 和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們要進到這些蚊帳呢 ?
why do we want to be involved ?	為什麼我們想要參與其中 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們先前談過阿拉伯之春以及這一切的力量
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉一個例子 , 也是你如何移動這條訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦發表了這樣子的演講 , 那時我跟各位說 , 我在臉書上 , 朋友我 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	觀眾笑了一下 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	有一篇文章 , 是由ap所主導 , 在電線上執行 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	世界上有兩個地方:芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:北大西洋公約需要朋友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	這個故事是個催化劑 , 隔天早上我有上百個facebook的朋友請求 , 來自印尼和芬蘭 , 大多說: 「 艾米 , 我們聽到你需要一個朋友 , 喔 , 北約是什麼 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	是的 , 我們笑著 , 但這就是我們如何移動這個訊息 , 移動那個訊息就是我們如何連結國際間的、私人的、以及這些社交網路 , 來協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我用嚴肅的話來說明 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是一張勇敢的英國士兵的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭警衛隊 。
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他站在頭盔上 , 在阿富汗南部 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我讓他來提醒我們 , 我不希望任何人離開房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力 , 不需要軍事人員 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	這是我們是誰的核心 , 我們所做的 , 我們為了保護言論自由 , 言論自由 , 所有我們在社會中珍視的事物 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但 , 你知道 , 生命並不是個開放的開關 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要有一支軍隊 , 不用在戰鬥中 , 不然就是在衝突中 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我會爭辯生命是一場盧安達 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你不得不把它撥進去 , 正如我思考我們如何在21世紀建立安全 , 在真正的戰爭和危機中 , 將會有好幾次 , 在我們今天所談的 , 我們的軍隊能夠成為一個21世紀安全、國際、跨部門、私人間的溝通系統的一部分 , 再加上溝通的能力 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後 , 我想說的是 , 我們今天早先聽到的關於維基百科的消息 。 我經常使用維基百科 , 來尋找事實 , 如同你們所知 , 維基百科不是由12位聰明的人所創建的 , 不是在房間裡寫文章 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科每天有數萬人輸入資訊 , 每天有數百萬人退縮這些資訊 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	這是個完美的圖像 , 對根本的觀點來說 , 沒有人和我們一起想的一樣聰明 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 我們沒有一個人像我們一樣聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的說法很簡單:一個讓每個人自由共享所有知識的世界 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 透過結合國際間的、跨部門的、私人的、策略性的溝通 , 在21世紀 , 我們能創造出安全的總和 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝 。 謝謝 。
